601 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Maple Tree Homes, Inc. v. County of Sullivan


96961


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


17 A.D.3d 965; 794 N.Y.S.2d 472; 2005 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 4443



April 28, 2005, Decided 
April 28, 2005, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal dismissed by Maple Tree Homes, Inc. v. County of Sullivan, 5 N.Y.3d 782, 835 N.E.2d 661, 2005 N.Y. LEXIS 1600, 801 N.Y.S.2d 801 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff original property owner appealed an order of the Supreme Court, Sullivan County (New York), which, inter alia, granted a cross-motion by defendant county for summary judgment dismissal of the owner's complaint, seeking to set aside a tax foreclosure sale of real property.


OVERVIEW: The property was the subject of fraudulent acquisitions. Thereafter, pursuant to N.Y. Real Prop. Tax Law § 1122, the county filed a verified list of delinquent taxes, which included the subject property. The original owner commenced an action against the fraudulent title holder and others, and a notice of pendency was filed. The county filed a petition and notice of foreclosure of tax liens, which was published in local newspapers and personally served upon the successor in interest of the fraudulent title holder, who was the apparent record owner. The foreclosure was granted and the county conveyed the property. The trial court held that the fraudulent deed was in fact void, and the property title was restored to the original owner, who then commenced the instant action to set aside the foreclosure sale. The trial court granted summary judgment to the county. On appeal, the court noted that the county had complied with N.Y. Real Prop. Tax Law § 1125(1)(a), as no notice of pendency or other indication of the original owner's interest was filed. It was noted that the owner did not attempt to determine the status of taxes on the property. There was no due process violation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the trial court.


HEADNOTES

Taxation--Tax Liens, Tax Sales and Tax Titles.--Complaint was dismissed in action seeking to set aside tax foreclosure sale of parcel of real property based on County's failure to provide plaintiff with personal notice of sale--after plaintiff acquired parcel, another party purportedly acquired parcel by deed which ultimately proved to have been fraudulently executed--County's obligation was to give reasonable notice to ascertainable interested parties under circumstances; that owners of record were not true owners of parcel and, as result, said true owners did not receive personal notice of proceedings, was not determinative--plaintiff was aware, prior to foreclosure sale, of fraudulent conveyance and was charged with knowledge that property taxes are regularly levied and that default may result in forfeiture of land.

 

602 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


People v. Eun Sil Jang


2004-03265


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


17 A.D.3d 693; 793 N.Y.S.2d 540; 2005 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 4378


March 31, 2005, Submitted  
April 25, 2005, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the County Court, Suffolk County (New York), convicting her of unauthorized practice of a profession, N.Y. Educ. Law § 6512(1), upon her plea of guilty and imposing sentence.


OVERVIEW: On appeal, the court found § 6512(1) was not unconstitutionally vague. The trial court providently exercised its discretion in denying that branch of defendant's omnibus motion which was for release of the grand jury minutes as she failed to demonstrate a compelling and particularized need for their production. By pleading guilty, defendant waived her claim that the evidence submitted to the grand jury was insufficient to support the indictment. In any event, the evidence before the grand jury was legally sufficient to establish the elements of unauthorized practice of massage therapy. The trial court also properly denied those branches of defendant's omnibus motion which were to dismiss the indictment on the grounds that the grand jury was defective and impaired. The People's submission of the minutes and attendance sheet for August 14, 2003, confirmed that an adequate number of jurors were present and concurred in the indictment. Moreover, the prosecutor's conduct did not impair the grand jury's integrity. The indictment, as supplemented by the bill of particulars, provided defendant with sufficiently specific information as to the manner, time, and place of the crimes charged.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


HEADNOTES  [***1] 

Constitutional Law--Validity of Statute.--Education Law § 6512 (1) is not unconstitutionally vague; statute provides person of ordinary intelligence with reasonable opportunity to know conduct that is proscribed and contains clear standards for enforcement.

Grand Jury--Inspection of Grand Jury Minutes.--Defendant was not entitled to release of grand jury minutes, as she failed to demonstrate compelling and particularized need for their production.

Grand Jury--Defective Proceeding

 

603 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


520 E. 81st St. Assocs. v. State


5633


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


19 A.D.3d 24; 799 N.Y.S.2d 1; 2005 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 4056



April 19, 2005, Decided 
April 19, 2005, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal dismissed by 520 E. 81st St. Assocs. v State, 5 NY3d 782, 835 NE2d 661, 2005 NY LEXIS 1597, 801 NYS2d 801 (2005)
Appeal denied by 520 E. 81st St. Assocs. v State, 5 NY3d 712, 840 NE2d 132, 2005 NY LEXIS 3183, 806 NYS2d 163 (N.Y., Oct. 25, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant corporate apartment building owner sought review of a judgment from the Court of Claims of the State of New York, which, in its suit for money damages due to a regulatory taking by respondent State, awarded it simple interest at the rate of 11 percent on the value of the property on August 1, 1985, for the period from 1985 to 1994, and awarded it 9 percent interest on that amount for the period from 1994 to 2000.


OVERVIEW: Ten years before the owner filed its suit, it was determined that the legislature's enactment of 1984 N.Y. Laws 940 constituted a regulatory taking by the State of apartment building units leased to a hospital for sublease to hospital employees. The owner's building was affected by the statute, and the court of claims determined that it was entitled to an award of compensation for the taking pursuant to U.S. Const. Amend. V and N.Y. Const. art. I, § 7(a). On appeal from the interest awarded, the owner argued that a nine-year delay in obtaining just compensation warranted an award of compound rather than simple interest to the aggrieved property owner. The court held that the calculation of interest should have been compounded for the takings period because in order to put the owner in the position it would have been in had the apartments been sold in 1985, it must be awarded compound interest calculated on the 1985 value of the property for the nine-year period during which it was prohibited from terminating the leases and selling the property. The court accepted the 11 percent figure for determining the yearly interest rate that would have been earned on the property's sale.


OUTCOME: The court ruled that the judgment should be modified, on the law, so as to award the owner a money judgment representing a calculation of compound interest at the rate of 11 percent on the value of the property on August 1, 1985, for the period from August 1, 1985 to October 20, 1994, and otherwise affirmed, without costs.


HEADNOTES

Eminent Domain -- Interest on Award -- Regulatory Taking -- Compound Interest Warranted Because of Long Delay in Obtaining Just Compensation

Claimant, the owner of condominium units formerly leased to a hospital that were subject to an unconstitutional regulatory taking for a nine-year period by virtue of a statute that deemed the hospital's employee subtenants to be qualifed primary tenants for purposes of lease renewal under the Rent Stablization Law (see L 1984, ch 940), was entitled to an award of compound rather than simple interest for the takings period in view of the long delay in obtaining just compensation. Just compensation included the interest claimant would have earned on the sale proceeds had the taking not occurred, calculated from the time of the taking. In order to put claimant in the same position it would have been in had the apartments been sold in 1985 and thus ensure just compensation, claimant was entitled to an award of compound interest at an 11% yearly rate calculated on the 1985 value of the property for the nine-year period during which it was prohibited from terminating the leases and selling the property. Claimant was entitled to the amount it would have earned had it sold the apartments in 1985 and invested the money as a prudent investor would have done, including reinvesting the interest earned on that investment. Furthermore, the award of compound interest is limited to the period up to the date the statute that created the regulatory taking was declared unconstitutional in 1994. Claimant was entitled to an award of simple interest at the annual rate of 9% for the ensuing six-year period until the date of the initial money judgment.

 

604 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


For the People Theatres of N.Y., Inc. v. City of New York


3714, 3715


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


20 A.D.3d 1; 793 N.Y.S.2d 356; 2005 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 3743



April 12, 2005, Decided 
April 12, 2005, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Reargument denied by, Appeal granted by, Stay granted by For the People Theatres of N.Y., Inc. v. City of New York, 2005 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 6994 (N.Y. App. Div. 1st Dep't, June 14, 2005)
Affirmed in part and modified in part by, Summary judgment denied by, Remitted by For the People Theatres of N.Y., Inc. v. City of New York, 6 NY3d 63, 843 NE2d 1121, 2005 N.Y. LEXIS 3349, 810 NYS2d 381 (N.Y., Dec. 15, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a City, its Mayor, its city planning director, and its buildings commissioner (City), appealed from two judgments denying their cross-motions for summary judgment, granting plaintiff adult establishments' summary judgment motions, declaring the 2001Adult Use Amendments to the 1995 Adult Use Zoning Ordinance unconstitutional, and permanently enjoining their enforcement. The appeal was transferred by the New York Court of Appeals.


OVERVIEW: The establishments argued that the City failed to generate any new empirical data as to the adverse secondary effects of adult establishments. The appellate court held that there was sufficient evidence that adult businesses had an adverse secondary effect. The City properly considered other jurisdictions' studies. The establishments did not show any basis to question those findings. The City also conducted studies of its own. That the bulk of the local studies contained anecdotal evidence did not render them worthless. The City Council reasonably believed that the nature of the 60/40 establishments, with a predominant focus on sexually explicit materials and/or featuring topless or nude women, remained unchanged and that the 2001 amendments were necessary to effectuate the original legislative purpose. There was not an unconstitutional taking as none of the establishments applied for an extension of the amortization period. Moreover, they all remained in operation pending the appeal. Finally, the amendments were not unconstitutionally vague as they did not suppress or greatly restrict access to lawful speech.


OUTCOME: The judgments were reversed. The establishments' motions were denied, defendants' cross motions were granted, the injunction was vacated, and the amendments were declared constitutional. The complaints were otherwise dismissed.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional Law -- Freedom of Speech -- Zoning Amendments Geographically Restricting Adult Entertainment Establishments 

The 2001 Adult Use Amendments to defendant City of New York's 1995 Adult Use Zoning Ordinance, which redefined and broadened the definitions with respect to "adult establishments" subject to regulation as to location, are constitutional. Supreme Court thus erred in declaring the amendments facially unconstitutional for regulating constitutionally protected expression without providing a rational basis for their adoption. The amendments were intended to clarify and affirm the intent of the 1995 ordinance by classifying as "adult establishments" any eating or drinking establishments or theaters that regularly featured adult entertainment, regardless of the portion of the floor area devoted to such entertainment, and establishing additional objective factors relating to the physical layout and operation for adult bookstores under the "60/40" substantial portion test. Defendant, in amending the 1995 ordinance, was not required to generate any new empirical data regarding the purported adverse secondary effects of "60/40" adult establishments. Rather, defendant was entitled to rely on the same Department of City Planning report it used in support of the original valid zoning restrictions. That report documented the link between adult businesses and negative secondary impacts, and thus provided a rational basis for the amendments.

 

605 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


State v. Dennin


96033


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


17 A.D.3d 744; 792 N.Y.S.2d 682; 2005 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 3606



April 7, 2005, Decided 
April 7, 2005, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] 
Appeal dismissed by State v. Dennin, 5 NY3d 824, 837 NE2d 737, 2005 N.Y. LEXIS 2546, 804 NYS2d 38 (2005)
Subsequent appeal at State of New York v. Dennin, 2007 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 4146 (N.Y. App. Div. 3d Dep't, Apr. 5, 2007)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the State of New York, appealed an order of the Supreme Court, Albany County (New York), which partially granted a cross-motion by defendant property purchaser for, inter alia, summary judgment dismissal of the complaint against him. The State sought recovery of remediation costs. The trial court also held that defendant daughter in law (DIL) was entitled to a hearing on the reasonableness of the costs.


OVERVIEW: The purchaser bought property and then sold it, by oral land contract, to his DIL. The DIL leased the property, which had a store and a gas station on the premises. Thereafter, the DIL arranged to remove the underground petroleum storage tanks in order to perform an environmental assessment of the property. When contamination was suspected, the DIL commenced remediation, but soon requested the State to proceed. The State expended funds to perform the remediation, pursuant to N.Y. Nav. Law § 179, and it filed an action, seeking reimbursement. The trial court granted summary judgment dismissal of the complaint as against the purchaser, and granted summary judgment to the State as against the DIL. The trial court indicated that the DIL was entitled to a hearing to determine the reasonableness of the remediation costs. On appeal, the court held that it was error to dismiss the complaint against the purchaser, as he had control of the use of the property, which was sufficient for purposes of liability under N.Y. Nav. Law § 181. Further, the DIL was not entitled to a hearing on the costs, as there were adequate due process safeguards. Constitutional challenges to § 181 lacked merit.


OUTCOME: The court modified the order of the trial court by reversing the partial grant of summary judgment dismissal of the complaint as against the purchaser, and reversing the grant of a hearing on the reasonableness of remediation costs to the DIL. The court granted the State's motion for partial summary judgment against the purchaser, and declared both the purchaser and the DIL liable for remediation costs.


HEADNOTES

Gas and Oil--Oil Spill Cleanup.--Record owner, who sold property by oral land contract to defendant, could be held liable under Navigation Law § 181 for cost of remediation, even in absence of evidence that he caused or contributed to discharge, since he knew that petroleum products were stored on and sold from premises when he acquired title and during his period of ownership, and he could control use of property, and activities which occurred there, through terms of land contract.

Gas and Oil--Oil Spill Cleanup--Due Process.--Unavailability of hearing to contest reasonableness of remediation costs in action by State seeking reimbursement does not offend due process--State has strong interest in protecting and preserving its lands and waters, and there is equally strong interest in ensuring reimbursement to taxpayer moneys expended in cleaning up polluted sites when discharger is unwilling to do so on his or her own accord; likelihood of erroneous deprivation of discharger's private financial interest is minimized by procedural safeguards combined with availability of CPLR article 78 review which provides dischargers with avenue to challenge costs associated with remediation.

Gas and Oil--Oil Spill Cleanup--Constitutionality.--Statutory scheme which allows State to recover costs of remediation from discharger is not unconstitutional--since statute authorizes discharger to undertake remediation without admitting liability, discharger is in position to control costs of remediation; State's waiver of immunity with respect to claims alleging willful, unlawful or malicious acts associated with remediation of spill sites, when combined with availability of CPLR article 78 proceeding to review plaintiff's actions, provides sufficient procedural safeguard to dischargers.

Gas Oil--Oil Spill Cleanup--Constitutionality.--Argument that Navigation Law § 172 (8) is unconstitutionally vague for failure to enumerate what omissions could give rise to "discharger" was rejected--while defendants posited hypothetical factual scenario in support of their argument, vagueness challenges are addresses based on facts of case, not hypothetical scenarios.

 

606 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Chavis v. New York Temporary State Commn. on Lobbying


96541


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


16 A.D.3d 886; 791 N.Y.S.2d 707; 2005 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 2641



March 17, 2005, Decided  
March 17, 2005, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Cross appeals were taken of a judgment of the Supreme Court, Albany County (New York), which ruled that the N.Y. Legis. Law § 1-n(b) and (c) were unconstitutional. Plaintiffs had sought to compel a finding that defendant, the New York Temporary State Commission on Lobbying, was an agency that was subject to the State Administrative Procedure Act (SAPA), N.Y. A.P.A. Law § 102.


OVERVIEW: The Commission was established by N.Y. Legis. Law § 1-b, and all of its members were appointed by the governor. As such, the court found that the Commission fell within the definition of an "agency" under N.Y. A.P.A. § 102(1) and was bound by the SAPA. The Commission had rulemaking authority under N.Y. Legis. Law §§ 1-p, 1-q. The Commission was also bound by the SAPA because it was authorized to make final decisions in adjudicatory proceedings where the legal rights of the parties were determined. The court also found the Commission to be an executive agency based upon its funding sources and enforcement duties. The court did not find N.Y. Legis. Law § 1-n(b) and (c) to be unconstitutional because the legislation detailed the procedure the Commission needed to follow if, after an investigation, audit, or other authorized inquiry, it suspected that an individual was not complying with the lobbying laws.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the lower court.


HEADNOTES

Statutes--Construction--Lobbying Act.--New York Temporary State Commission on Lobbying (Commission) is agency bound by State Administrative Procedure Act, and Legislative Law § 1-n (b) and (c) have not been shown to be unconstitutional--Legislative Law § 1-n (b) and (c) detail procedure which Commission must follow if, after investigation, audit or other authorized inquiry, it suspects that individual or entity has willfully and knowingly failed to comply with Lobbying Act; since statute requires hearing to address both basis for and amount of penalty assessment, challenged provisions are not abridgement of property without due process.

 

607 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


American Ind. Paper Mills Supply Co., Inc. v. County of Westchester


2003-10564, (Index No. 8524/03)


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


16 A.D.3d 443; 791 N.Y.S.2d 618; 2005 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 2594


January 18, 2005, Argued  
March 14, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal after remand at American Ind. Paper Mills Supply Co., Inc. v. County of Westchester, 2009 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 6512 (N.Y. App. Div. 2d Dep't, Sept. 22, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff licensee appealed the order from the Supreme Court of Westchester County (New York), which, in an action for a judgment declaring that a fee imposed pursuant to a local law was unconstitutional, granted defendant county's motion to dismiss the complaint as time-barred.


OVERVIEW: In 1999 the Westchester County Board of Legislators enacted the Westchester County Solid Waste and Recyclables Collection Licensing Law to regulate the collection and disposal of solid waste and recyclables in the county. Section 826-a.306(2)(b) of the Laws of Westchester County imposed a $ 20,000 per station annual fee on any licensee who owned, leased, operated, or controlled a transfer station that processed recyclables. The licensee filed suit seeking a declaration that the transfer station fee was unconstitutional because the fee was greater than a sum reasonably necessary to cover the costs of issuance, inspection, and enforcement and, therefore, constituted an unauthorized tax. The supreme court dismissed the cause of action as time-barred. On appeal, the court reversed, finding that because the licensee's challenge to the constitutionality of the local law could have been brought pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, the court erred in dismissing the action as barred by the four-month period of limitation under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 217.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order in so far appealed from and remitted the matter back to the trial court.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Proceeding against Body or Officer--When Remedy Available.--In general, proceeding pursuant to CPLR article 78 is not available to challenge validity of substance of legislative act; thus, so much of complaint as sought that relief should not have been dismissed as time-barred.

Green v. Liberty Mut. Ins. Co. Trust


2004-02113, (Index No. 27088/03)


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


16 A.D.3d 457; 791 N.Y.S.2d 630; 2005 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 2607


January 21, 2005, Argued  
March 14, 2005, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Appeal dismissed by Green v. Liberty Mut. Ins. Co. Trust, 5 NY3d 823, 837 NE2d 734, 804 NYS2d 35, 2005 N.Y. LEXIS 1832 (N.Y., Aug. 25, 2005)
Subsequent appeal at Matter of Green v. Liberty Mut. Ins. Co., 22 AD3d 755, 802 NYS2d 379, 2005 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 11355 (N.Y. App. Div. 2d Dep't, Oct. 24, 2005)



HEADNOTES

Insurance--No-Fault Automobile Insurance.--Complaint was dismissed in action to recover no-fault benefits--Insurance Law § 5106 (c) permits insurer or claimant to institute court action to adjudicate dispute de novo where master arbitrator's award is $ 5,000 or greater; since master arbitrator made no monetary award, statutory predicate for de novo court adjudication was not satisfied--statute does not violate due process and equal protection because classification it creates between claimants and insurance carriers is reasonably related to legitimate state interest and has rational basis.

 

609 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


La Rocco v. Goord


95845


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


15 A.D.3d 809; 790 N.Y.S.2d 265; 2005 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 1922



February 24, 2005, Decided  
February 24, 2005, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant inmate appealed the judgment of the Supreme Court, Ulster County (New York), dismissing the inmate's application, in a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, to review a determination of respondent Commissioner of New York Correctional Services denying the inmate's request for a merit time allowance.


OVERVIEW: The inmate's disciplinary record included 213 days of keeplock confinement. As a result, he was denied eligibility for a merit time allowance. N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 7, § 280.2(b)(3) barred inmates who had committed serious disciplinary infractions, including disciplinary sanctions totaling 60 or more days of keeplock time, from receiving merit time consideration. The withholding of merit time was a discretionary determination pursuant to N.Y. Correct. Law § 803(4). Pursuant to N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 7, § 280.2(b)(3) and the fact that the inmate's disciplinary record included more than 60 days of keeplock time, the Commissioner's denial of the request for a merit time allowance was not an abuse of discretion.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Prisons and Prisoners--Jail Time Credit--Merit Time Allowance.--In view of clear language of directive and fact that petitioner's disciplinary record included more than 60 days of keeplock time, there was no abuse of discretion in denial of his request for merit time allowance.

 

610 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


People v. Brown


5055 5056, Ind. 389/02


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


14 A.D.3d 356; 789 N.Y.S.2d 106; 2005 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 65



January 6, 2005, Decided  
January 6, 2005, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Appeal denied by People v. Brown, 4 N.Y.3d 852, 830 N.E.2d 325, 2005 N.Y. LEXIS 1283, 797 N.Y.S.2d 426 (2005)
Appeal denied by People v. Burwell, 4 N.Y.3d 852, 830 N.E.2d 325, 2005 N.Y. LEXIS 1287, 797 N.Y.S.2d 426 (2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Supreme Court, New York County, New York, after denying the first defendant's motion to suppress and both defendants' motions to dismiss the indictment, convicted two defendants of robbery in the second degree, and sentenced the first defendant, as a persistent violent felony offender, to a term of 16 years to life, and sentenced the second defendant, as a second violent felony offender, to a term of 11 years. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: Police had reasonable suspicion to justify a temporary investigative detention of the first defendant for prompt identification, based upon a sufficiently specific description of him and police observations of his suspicious behavior as he went in the reported direction of flight a few minutes after and a few blocks away from the robbery, and the fact that he reasonably appeared to be accompanying the second defendant, who met the description of the other robber and was also acting suspiciously. The trial court properly exercised its discretion in denying defendants' request to call an expert witness on identification. The People had a good faith reason for an immediate grand jury presentation, which was that the victim, a foreign tourist, was about to leave the United States. The People did not violate defendants' rights under N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 190.50(5)(a) or to due process when they presented the case to the Grand Jury immediately upon the arrests and prior to any arraignment. The prosecutor had no duty to inform defendants of their right to testify before the Grand Jury insofar as they had not yet been arraigned in a local criminal court upon the felony complaint.


OUTCOME: The appeals court affirmed the judgments.


HEADNOTES

Crimes--Unlawful Search and Seizure--Reasonable Suspicion.--Police had reasonable suspicion justifying temporary investigative detention of defendant for prompt identification based upon sufficiently specific description coupled with police observations of his suspicious behavior as he proceeded in reported direction of flight only few minutes after and few blocks away from robbery, as well as fact that he reasonably appeared to be accompanying codefendant, who met description of other robber and was also acting suspiciously.

Grand Jury--Right to Appear before Grand Jury.--Defendants' rights under CPL 190.50 (5) (a) or to due process were not violated when People presented case to grand jury immediately upon arrests and prior to any arraignment; prosecutor had no duty to inform defendants of their right to testify before grand jury insofar as they had not yet been arraigned in local criminal court upon felony complaint, and there was no evidence that prosecutor intentionally delayed arraignment in order to deprive defendants of notice of grand jury proceeding.

 

611 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


N. Shore Cadillac-Oldsmobile, Inc. v. Tax Appeals Tribunal


94298


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


13 A.D.3d 994; 787 N.Y.S.2d 463; 2004 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 16184



December 30, 2004, Decided  
December 30, 2004, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended February 8, 2005.
Appeal denied by North Shore Cadillac-Oldsmobile, Inc. v. Tax Appeals Tribunal, 5 N.Y.3d 704, 834 N.E.2d 780, 2005 N.Y. LEXIS 1491, 801 N.Y.S.2d 1 (N.Y., June 29, 2005)



DISPOSITION:  The court decided that the determination was supported by substantial evidence, was rational, and was not constitutionally infirm. It affirmed the determination.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Sales and use taxes were originally owed by a dealer who became insolvent. Under N.Y. Tax Law arts. 28, 29, respondent Tax Appeals Tribunal (New York) sustained a sales and use tax assessment imposed on petitioner assignee (taxpayer) of the dealer after the dealer's secured creditor enforced it rights under a security agreement. The taxpayer requested review under N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer complied with the assignment contract and gave the Department of Taxation and Finance, Division of Taxation the required bulk sales notice. The taxpayer then bought the dealer's assets despite knowing the dealer might have an unpaid sales tax liability. The dealer fully paid the bank from the sale proceeds but paid no part of the sales and use taxes. The Division issued a notice of determination and demand to the taxpayer for payment of sales and use taxes. The transaction was not exempt from the payment of sales and use taxes under N.Y. Tax Law § 1141(c). That was because the transaction was a bulk sale under former N.Y. U.C.C. art. 6 and was not a sale, transfer, or assignment of business assets in settlement or realization of a valid lien, mortgage, or other security interest, an exception under N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 20, § 537.1(a)(4)(i), and former N.Y. U.C.C. Law § 6-103(3). Rather, the sale was directly from the dealer to the taxpayer. The bank was interested but did not directly take control of the assets or sell them at auction under its enforcement notice. The taxpayer had to live with the tax consequences of the form of the transaction.


OUTCOME: The court decided that the determination was supported by substantial evidence, was rational, and was not constitutionally infirm. It affirmed the determination.


HEADNOTES

Taxation--Sales and Use Taxes.--Determination which sustained sales and use tax assessment affirmed--despite being notified that debtor might have unpaid sales tax liability, petitioner closed pursuant to asset purchase agreement and bank, secured creditor, was fully paid--lien for unpaid sales and use taxes took priority over bank's perfected security interest--as bank did not solicit, direct or control sale of assets to petitioner, exception to bulk sale definition found in 20 NYCRR 537.1 (a) (4) (i) for transfer made directly to holder of security interest in satisfaction of debt or to designee of holder of security interest who assumes liability for outstanding debt had no application--determination that transaction in question was bulk sale was supported by substantial evidence and interpretation of regulation as requiring actual foreclosure by creditor before exemption is triggered was rational--petitioner's claim that its constitutional rights were violated was rejected; Tax Law § 1141 (c) provides bulk sales purchaser with ample protection from paying vendor's unpaid sales taxes; it was only by ignoring dictates of statute that petitioner became personally liable for debtor's unpaid sales taxes.

 

612 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


CWM Chem. Servs., L.L.C. v. Roth


CA 03-01712


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FOURTH DEPARTMENT


15 A.D.3d 77; 787 N.Y.S.2d 780; 2004 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 16270



December 30, 2004, Decided  
December 30, 2004, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Stay denied by CWM Chem. Servs., L.L.C. v. Roth, 5 NY3d 825, 837 NE2d 738, 2005 N.Y. LEXIS 1896, 804 NYS2d 39 (2005)
Motion granted by CWM Chem. Servs., L.L.C. v. Roth, 6 NY3d 732, 843 NE2d 1147, 2005 N.Y. LEXIS 3375, 810 NYS2d 407 (N.Y., Dec. 15, 2005)
Affirmed in part and modified in part by, Judgment entered by CWM Chem. Servs., L.L.C. v. Roth, 6 NY3d 410, 846 NE2d 448, 813 NYS2d 18, 2006 N.Y. LEXIS 515 (N.Y., Mar. 23, 2006)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed and defendant officials of New York State's Departments of Taxation and Finance and Environmental Conservation, in their official capacities, cross-appealed from an order and judgment of the Supreme Court, Niagara County (New York), which granted partial summary judgment to the taxpayer on its claim for refund and declared that N.Y. Envtl. Conserv. Law § 27-0923 violated the Commerce Clause.


OVERVIEW: Section § 27-0923 imposed special assessments on generation and disposal of hazardous wastes in the state. The taxpayer argued that an exclusion from disposal assessments for those who paid the generation tax in effect discriminated against out-of-state producers whose wastes were disposed of in New York State. The appellate court agreed that the provision discriminated against interstate commerce because it was not equivalent to a compensatory or complementary tax, but, in accord with the statute's severability clause, did not find it entirely invalid. It invalidated the generation assessment, but went on to uphold the disposal assessment, which became applicable to all taxpayers involved with hazardous wastes. There was no due process denial in limiting the taxpayer's refunds to those claimed within the time limit prescribed by N.Y. Tax Law § 1087, even though the limitations period was relatively short, because New York's tax laws provided a pre-deprivation (that is, declaratory judgment) remedy as well as the post-deprivation remedy of a refund.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment to hold only certain parts of the statute unconstitutional. It affirmed the remainder of the judgment, including the direction that refunds be paid only to the extent timely sought.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional Law--Commerce Clause--Validity of Special Assessments on Generation and Disposal of Hazardous Waste

The funding mechanism of the State's Hazardous Waste Remedial Fund, which provides for special assessments on certain hazardous waste either generated or disposed of in New York (ECL 27-0923; State Finance Law § 97-b), is partially invalid under the Commerce Clause. ECL 27-0923 (2) (d) and (3) are facially discriminatory against interstate commence to the extent that those portions of the "Superfund" statute, as applied by defendants, afford preferential treatment to intrastate hazardous waste over interstate hazardous waste. ECL 27-0923 (3) (c) is facially unconstitutional to the extent that it exempts from taxation hazardous waste resulting from remediation of in-state inactive hazardous waste sites without affording a similar exemption to remediation of similar out-of-state inactive hazardous waste sites. ECL 27-0923 (2) (d) is likewise unconstitutional to the extent that it exempts from taxation the disposal of hazardous waste generated in New York that has been taxed pursuant to ECL 27-0923 (1), without exempting from taxation the disposal of hazardous waste generated in another state that has been taxed pursuant to any other state's similar generation tax. Moreover, since the challenged statutory provisions do not impose sales or use taxes, they cannot be validated under the Commerce Clause as imposing compensatory taxes.

Taxation--Tax Refund 

Plaintiff, the owner and operator of a licensed hazardous waste treatment, storage and disposal facility, who challenged the constitutionality of ECL 27-0923, could not be awarded a tax refund (see Tax Law § 1087) in the declaratory judgment action. To the extent that plaintiff would be entitled to such relief, it must avail itself of the remedies available under article 27 of the Tax Law.

Chilberg v. Chilberg


CA 04-00334, Appeal 1


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FOURTH DEPARTMENT


13 A.D.3d 1089; 788 N.Y.S.2d 533; 2004 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 16334



December 30, 2004, Decided  
December 30, 2004, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Subsequent appeal at Chilberg v. Chilberg, 13 A.D.3d 1093, 786 N.Y.S.2d 766, 2004 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 16399 (N.Y. App. Div. 4th Dep't, 2004)
Subsequent appeal at Chilberg v. Chilberg, 13 A.D.3d 1093, 786 N.Y.S.2d 767, 2004 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 16405 (N.Y. App. Div. 4th Dep't, 2004)
Reargument denied by Chilberg v. Chilberg, 16 A.D.3d 1181, 792 N.Y.S.2d 368, 2005 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 2767 (N.Y. App. Div. 4th Dep't, Mar. 18, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Judgment unanimously modified by denying in part plaintiff's motion for partial summary judgment. As modified, judgment was affirmed without costs, and new trial was granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff accident victim sued defendants, the lessee and lessor of a pickup truck, for negligence. The Supreme Court, Niagara County, New York, granted plaintiff's motion for partial summary judgment and ruled that the lessee's negligence was the sole proximate cause of the accident. A jury awarded plaintiff $ 800,000 in damages; the lessor appealed.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff was sunbathing in the driveway of her family's home when she was accidently run over by a pickup truck driven by the lessee, her father. The appellate court held that the trial court erred in granting plaintiff partial summary judgment as there were triable issues of fact with regard to her culpable conduct and causation. The damage award of $ 650,000 for past pain and suffering and $ 100,000 for future pain and suffering did not deviate materially from what would be reasonable compensation. N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 388 did not violate due process as applied to long-term vehicle lessors, as one of its purposes was to ensure that persons injured by the negligent operation of a vehicle would have recourse to a financially responsible person, which was a valid governmental purpose, and imposing liability on lessors for the negligence of lessees was a reasonable means of accomplishing this objective. Section 388 did not violate the Equal Protection Clause, as it was rational for the legislature to distinguish between vehicle owners, including long-term lessors, and nonowners, including lienholders, and to allocate the statutory burdens based on that distinction.


OUTCOME: The damage award was reasonable. The trial court's ruling that the lessee was negligent was affirmed, but the partial summary judgment was reversed and a new trial was granted on the issues of plaintiff's alleged culpable conduct and the causal relationship, if any, between such conduct and the accident.


HEADNOTES

Negligence--What Constitutes.--In action to recover for injuries sustained by then-15-year-old plaintiff while sunbathing in driveway of her family's home when she was accidently run over by pickup truck driven by her father, plaintiff was properly granted summary judgment with respect to issue of her father's negligence; however, plaintiff failed to sustain her burden of demonstrating her entitlement to judgment as matter of law on issues of her culpable conduct and causation.

Motor Vehicles--Imputing Driver's Negligence to Owner.--Vehicle and Traffic Law § 388, which provides for vicarious liability on part of "[e]very owner of a vehicle used or operated in this state . . . with the permission, express or implied, on such owner' is not unconstitutional as applied to long-term vehicle lessors.

Am. Boxing & Ath. Ass'n v. Chemung County YMCA


95427


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


13 A.D.3d 842; 787 N.Y.S.2d 413; 2004 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 15286



December 16, 2004, Decided  
December 16, 2004, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Supreme Court, Chemung County (New York), granted the cross motion of defendant, the New York State Athletic Commission, for a permanent injunction against plaintiff, a non-profit corporation that promotes amateur boxing tournaments, prohibiting the corporation from holding a contest in New York. The corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: The general counsel to the Commission discovered that neither the corporation nor its sponsor were licensed boxing promoters in New York. In a letter dated March 13, 2003, the general counsel informed the venue that the corporation's contest was not sanctioned by the Commission and the contest was cancelled. The Commission was vested with the sole direction, management, control, and jurisdiction over all boxing matches or exhibitions conducted within the State of New York. To obtain an exemption under N.Y. Unconsol. Law ch. 7, § 31, a contest holder had to come within one of the three categories of exceptions. Since the corporation was not a military or educational institution, it could only qualify under the remaining exception if it met certain criteria such as demonstrating that its contests were conducted under the supervision of the USA Boxing association and complied with the association's rules for amateur events. Because the corporation did not so qualify, it was subject to the rules of the Commission. Thus, the trial court properly granted the Commission's cross motion for a permanent injunction prohibiting the corporation from holding the contest in New York.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's order.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Sporting Events--Boxing and Wrestling--Regulation of Boxing Events.--New York State Athletic Commission was properly granted permanent injunction prohibiting plaintiff from conducting boxing events without first complying with applicable law and licensing requirements--Commission is vested with sole direction, management, control and jurisdiction over all boxing matches or exhibitions conducted within State of New York, and plaintiff, nonprofit corporation which promotes participation in amateur boxing tournaments, was subject to rules of Commission--plaintiff's challenge to constitutionality of McKinney's Uncons Laws of NY § 8931 was unpersuasive.

 

615 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Berkshire Nursing Ctr., Inc. v. Novello


2003-06253, (Index No. 11971/01)


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


13 A.D.3d 327; 786 N.Y.S.2d 209; 2004 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 14852


October 18, 2004, Argued  
December 6, 2004, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action for a judgment declaring that N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 18, § 540.6(a)(1) was null, void, and of no effect on the ground of unconstitutionality, defendants appealed from an order of the Suffolk County Supreme Court (New York), which converted the instant action to a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding, denied a motion to dismiss the complaint as time-barred, and granted plaintiffs leave to amend the complaint.


OVERVIEW: Defendants contended that since the instant action should have been filed under N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, a four-month limitations period applied. But, the trial court determined that the statute of limitations was not a bar. On appeal, the court first held that defendants had the burden to assert the statute of limitations as a defense, and that defendants failed in such burden. A series of ambiguous communications between the parties occurred. Since any ambiguity created by defendants had to be resolved against them, and since the date of the last letter from plaintiffs was the earliest date from which the limitations period could run, the proceeding was timely commenced. Moreover, after defendants established a prima facie case for summary judgment, plaintiffs raised a triable issue of fact regarding whether defendants' denial of reimbursement under N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 18, § 540.6(a)(1) was due to circumstances beyond plaintiffs' control, and whether exceptions to the statute made by defendants were arbitrary. Therefore, summary judgment was properly denied.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Limitation of Actions--Four-Month Statute of Limitations.--In action for judgment declaring that regulation was null, void, and of no effect on ground of unconstitutionality, defendants failed to establish that decision provided notice more than four months before proceeding was commenced--series of ambiguous communications between parties ended with letter from plaintiffs, and proceeding was timely commenced within four months of date of letter.

 

616 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


People v. Brown


14193


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


13 A.D.3d 667; 786 N.Y.S.2d 592; 2004 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 14670



December 2, 2004, Decided  
December 2, 2004, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected January 25, 2005.
Appeal denied by People v. Brown, 4 N.Y.3d 742, 824 N.E.2d 55, 2004 N.Y. LEXIS 4169, 790 N.Y.S.2d 654 (2004)
Related proceeding at People v. Brown, 2009 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 2473 (N.Y. App. Div. 3d Dep't, Apr. 2, 2009)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial, the County Court, Rensselaer County (New York), convicted defendant of the crimes of stalking in the second degree and criminal contempt in the second degree (nine counts). He was sentenced, as a second felony offender, to a prison term of two to four years on the stalking conviction and concurrent terms of one year on the contempt convictions. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant contended that the letters he sent to the victim constituted protected speech and, as such, the stalking statute was unconstitutional. The appellate court held that the statute was not unconstitutional. Threatening conduct causing fear of physical harm was not protected speech, and the criminal statute proscribing such activity, N.Y. Penal Law § 120.50(3), did not implicate the 1st and 14th Amendments of the United States Constitution or N.Y. Const. art. I, § 8. Further, defendant's remedy for challenging the constitutionality of his prior conviction was upon direct appeal from such conviction or by way of a motion to vacate the judgment pursuant to N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 440.10. Finally, the elements of stalking in the second degree and criminal contempt in the first degree were not identical, and it was altogether possible to commit the former without committing the latter. As such, the jury could have found defendant guilty of the former and not guilty of the latter without such determinations being repugnant.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Crimes--Stalking.--Contention that letters defendant sent to victim constituted protected speech and, as such, stalking statute is unconstitutional, was rejected--threatening conduct causing fear of physical harm is not protected speech, and criminal statute proscribing such activity does not implicate 1st and 14th Amendments of US Constitution or NY Constitution, article I, § 8.

Crimes--Stalking.--Defendant's contention that his conviction for stalking in second degree must be reversed because predicate offense relied upon to enhance crime with which he was charged (from misdemeanor to felony) was constitutionally infirm was rejected since there was no provision for defendant to challenge constitutionally of previous conviction.

Crimes--Verdict--Inconsistent Verdict.--Contention that verdicts convicting defendant of stalking in second degree and acquitting him of criminal contempt were repugnant was unpreserved for review and without merit; elements of stalking in second degree and criminal contempt in first degree are not identical, and it is possible to commit former without committing latter.

 

617 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


People v. Van Dyne


KA 99-05505


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FOURTH DEPARTMENT


12 A.D.3d 120; 784 N.Y.S.2d 795; 2004 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13945



November 19, 2004, Decided  
November 19, 2004, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Reargument granted by, Amended by People v. Van Dyne, 789 N.Y.S.2d 455, 2005 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 1196 (N.Y. App. Div. 4th Dep't, Feb. 4, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed, plea vacated and matter remitted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Monroe County Court (New York) for murder in the first degree after defendant pled guilty. Defendant contended, inter alia, that reversal was required because his plea lacked statutory authorization.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted by the grand jury for charges relating to a murder that occurred during the commission of a robbery. The People filed a notice of intent to seek the death penalty pursuant to N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 250.40(1). Defendant appeared to enter a plea of guilty. Pursuant to the terms of the plea agreement, defendant would be sentenced to life imprisonment without parole. Before entering his plea, defendant signed a plea agreement outlining the rights he was waiving by pleading guilty. Following the colloquy, but before defendant entered his plea, the prosecutor handed a letter to the court which indicated the notice of intent was withdrawn contingent upon defendant's plea. The appellate court held that although the issues were not preserved for review, it would review them in the interest of justice. The notice of intent was still "pending" when defendant pled guilty and, consequently, the trial court lacked the power to accept his plea. Since defendant's plea was a condition precedent to the withdrawal of the notice of intent, which did not become effective unless and until defendant entered his plea, the notice of intent was still pending.


OUTCOME: The conviction was reversed. The plea was vacated and the matter was remitted to the trial court for further proceedings on the indictment.


HEADNOTES

Appeal -- Waiver of Right to Appeal -- Validity of Guilty Plea to Murder in First Degree

1. Defendant's waiver of the right to appeal executed in connection with his guilty plea to murder in the first degree (Penal Law § 125.27 [1] [a] [vii]) did not preclude him from challenging the validity of the plea on the ground that the plea was statutorily invalid because the People had not properly withdrawn the notice of intent to seek the death penalty (CPL 250.40 [1]) before entry of the plea. The issues raised by defendant involved matters of "societal concern" with implications for the integrity of the criminal justice system, and were thus not waivable.

Appeal -- Preservation of Issue for Review -- Validity of Guilty Plea to Murder in First Degree

2. Defendant's contention on appeal that his guilty plea to murder in the first degree (Penal Law § 125.27 [1] [a] [vii]) was statutorily invalid because the People had not properly withdrawn the notice of intent to seek the death penalty (CPL 250.40 [1]) before entry of the plea was not preserved for review. Defendant failed to move to withdraw the plea or vacate the judgment of conviction. However, the appeal was entertained as a matter of discretion in the interest of justice (see CPL 470.15 [6] [a]).

Crimes -- Capital Murder -- Statutorily Invalid Guilty Plea -- Ineffective Withdrawal of Notice of Intent to Seek Death Penalty before Entry of Plea

3. Defendant's conviction of murder in the first degree (Penal Law § 125.27 [1] [a] [vii]) based upon his guilty plea for which he received a sentence of life imprisonment without parole was reversed and the plea vacated because the People had not properly withdrawn the notice of intent to seek the death penalty (CPL 250.40 [1]) before entry of the plea. The prosecutor submitted to the court a written withdrawal of the notice of intent that was "conditioned" on defendant's plea of guilty and the court's acceptance of that plea. Defendant's plea was thus a condition precedent to the withdrawal of the notice of intent, which did not become effective unless and until defendant entered his plea. At the time of his plea defendant was therefore faced with the unconstitutional choice of either exercising his Fifth and Sixth Amendment rights and risking death, or abandoning those rights and avoiding the possibility of death. Under these circumstances, the notice of intent was still "pending" at the time of defendant's plea, and the court thus lacked the statutory authority to accept defendant's plea. In any event, the People did not comply with the filing requirements of CPL 250.40 (4) in attempting to withdraw the notice of intent. Submitting the written withdrawal to the judge did not constitute a proper "filing" of the withdrawal with the court prior to the entry of defendant's plea.

Payne v. County of Sullivan


95285


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


12 A.D.3d 807; 784 N.Y.S.2d 251; 2004 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13270



November 10, 2004, Decided  
November 10, 2004, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a boat storage and repair facility and its owner, appealed from an order of the Supreme Court in Sullivan County (New York), which dismissed plaintiffs' complaint against defendants, the County, its sheriff and one of its deputies. The complaint sought relief under several theories, including liability under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. A § 1983 action against defendant boat owner was also dismissed.


OVERVIEW: A dispute arose between plaintiffs and the boat owner about repairs and storage of the boat owner's vessel. Plaintiffs refused to release the vessel until they received payment completed repair work. The boat owner filed a complaint with the sheriff's office, asserting that the facility owner took her vessel without her consent. Plaintiffs relinquished the vessel after the repair facility owner was threatened with prosecution. Plaintiffs lawsuit was filed thereafter. The court affirmed dismissal of the complaint. While plaintiffs might have had a valid lien on the vessel, they failed to plead sufficient facts to support a claim of deprivation of that right without due process of law. The boat owner's complaint gave the sheriff and deputy probable cause to take action against the facility owner. The County could not be held liable on a theory of respondeat superior, and plaintiffs failed to demonstrate that some affirmative policy or custom on the part of the County caused the alleged constitutional deprivation. The action against the boat owner failed, as there was no evidence that she contributed to the governmental actions beyond filing her complaint with the sheriff.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of the § 1983 claims was affirmed. The remainder of the dismissed claims were not considered, as they had been abandoned by plaintiffs.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Civil Rights--Federal Civil Rights Claim.--In action in which plaintiffs alleged deprivation of constitutionally protected property interest when, in response to threat of prosecution made by Sheriff and Deputy, plaintiff was forced to release defendant's boat despite his lien against that property as garage keeper owed debt for services rendered, 42 USC §1983 claims dismissed against Sheriff and Deputy--although plaintiff may have had valid lien against boat, plaintiffs failed to support claim that plaintiff was deprived of that property interest without due process of law by misuse of governmental authority by defendants--Sheriff and Deputy acted within their authority in relying on defendant's sworn statement when informing plaintiff that he could face criminal charges.

Civil Rights--Federal Civil Rights Claim.--In action in which plaintiffs alleged deprivation of constitutionally protected property interest when, in response to threat of prosecution made by Sheriff and Deputy, plaintiff was forced to release defendant's boat despite his lien against that property as garage keeper owed debt for services rendered, 42 USC §1983 claims against County dismissed; even had some wrongdoing been pleaded with respect to Sheriff and Deputy, County "cannot be [held] liable on the basis of respondeat superior in a section 1983 action" and plaintiffs failed to demonstrate the "some affirmative policy or custom or other knowing act on the part of . . . the county has caused the alleged constitutional deprivation."

Civil Rights--Federal Civil Rights Claims.--In action in which plaintiffs alleged deprivation of constitutionally protected property interest when, in response to threat of prosecution made by Sheriff and Deputy, plaintiff was forced to release defendant's boat despite his lien against that property as garage keeper owed debt for services rendered, 42 USC §1983 claim against defendant dismissed; there was no evidence that defendant contributed to actions of County defendants beyond filing complaint against plaintiff; this was insufficient to demonstrate collaborative action necessary to render her liable, as private citizen, under 42 USC §1983.

Law § 440.20, vacating his sentence as a persistent felony offender, and finding the persistent felony offender statutory scheme unconstitutional.

Crimes--Sentence--Persistent Felony Offender

Evevsky v. Liberty Mut. Group


95472


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


11 A.D.3d 778; 783 N.Y.S.2d 96; 2004 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 12332



October 21, 2004, Decided  
October 21, 2004, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, the New York Workers' Compensation Board, ruled that claimant, a worker, was not authorized to receive medical treatment from a massage therapist. The worker appealed the decision.


OVERVIEW: The worker was awarded benefits for a permanent partial disability after sustaining injuries to her neck and shoulder in a work-related accident in 1993. The case was reopened in 2001 following, among other things, an objection by the employer's workers' compensation carrier to the worker's request for authorization of treatment by a licensed massage therapist. The workers' compensation law judge determined that the treatment was not authorized by N.Y. Workers' Comp. Law § 13-b, and the Board affirmed. N.Y. Workers' Comp. Law § 13-b prohibited medical providers from rendering care and treatment to recipients of workers' compensation benefits unless the providers were expressly authorized by the Board, or subject to one of the statutory exceptions listed thereunder. It was undisputed that the instant treating massage therapist was not so authorized. Furthermore, the therapist did not perform the treatment under the active and personal supervision of an authorized physician or under other circumstances that would warrant a finding that massage therapy was explicitly or impliedly authorized by the statute. Thus, the Board properly denied the benefits sought by the worker.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed, without costs.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Workers' Compensation--Treatment and Care of Injured Employees.--Claimant was not authorized to receive medical treatment from massage therapist--Workers' Compensation Law § 13-b prohibits medical providers from rendering care and treatment to recipients of workers' compensation benefits unless expressly authorized or subject to statutory exception--further, therapist did not perform treatment under active and personal supervision of authorized physician or under other circumstances that would warrant finding that massage therapy was explicitly or impliedly authorized by statute.

Delafield 246 Corp. v. City of New York


3911


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


11 A.D.3d 268; 782 N.Y.S.2d 441; 2004 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 11823



October 12, 2004, Decided  
October 12, 2004, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Appeal denied by Delafield 246 Corp. v City of New York, 4 N.Y.3d 703, 825 N.E.2d 133, 2005 N.Y. LEXIS 81, 792 N.Y.S.2d 1 (N.Y., Jan. 18, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a proceeding under N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, respondents, a city and its collection agent, appealed from a judgment of the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), that granted an injunction to petitioner property owner permanently enjoining them from selling or foreclosing on tax liens to which the owner's property was subject.


OVERVIEW: When the owner bought the property in a foreclosure sale, it bought it subject to large property tax arrearages, and it reached an agreement with the city regarding a payment schedule. When the owner fell behind on its payment schedule, sought to proceed with subdivision of the property, and discovered that the property was subject to tax liens, some of which had already been sold by the city, the owner claimed to have had a different understanding of the payment agreement and sought to enjoin further sales of tax liens and the foreclosure of any of them. The trial court credited the owner's account of its claimed misunderstanding, but the appellate court held that the trial court lacked the power to enjoin the sales and foreclosures just as the city would have lacked the authority to enter such an agreement. New York's Constitution forbade the bestowal of private gifts by government, and what amounted to interest-free financing of delinquent taxes would have amounted to just such a gift. Unless a statutory exemption existed, taxes simply had to be paid.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment, denied the petition for injunctive relief, and dismissed the proceeding.


HEADNOTES

Taxation--Tax Liens, Tax Sales and Tax Titles.--Petitioner real estate development corporation, which purchased property at mortgage foreclosure sale, was not entitled to have respondent city permanently enjoined from selling or foreclosing on certain tax liens apportioned against petitioner since court did not have authority to invalidate decade-old tax lien, notwithstanding alleged ambiguity of agreement respondent drafted and entered into with prior owner in effort to avoid foreclosure; all real property taxes and assessments and interest imposed thereon were, by operation of law, liens upon real estate and "shall continue to be, until paid" (Administrative Code § 11-301)--while Administrative Code § 11-405 authorized forbearance agreements with delinquent taxpayers, these agreements set up payment plan that postpones foreclosure for so long as required payments are made--estoppel is not generally available against government agency to prevent it from carrying out its statutory duties, especially when duty involves taxation.

Taxation--Tax Liens, Tax Sales and Tax Titles.--Allegedly ambiguous clause of agreement which petitioner allegedly relied upon to its detriment when it purchased property at foreclosure sale should not be construed against city since city was not party to judgment of foreclosure and sale whereby petitioner assumed obligations of agreement, agreement did not purport to be statement of property's tax account at time of purchase of property, petitioner's title company representative was sent tax bill reflecting arrears of principal and accrued interest as of day prior to closing, and all tax bills and delinquency notices sent to petitioner since it purchased property showed exact amount of arrears which differed from any computation that could be made pursuant to petitioner's interpretation of agreement.
