Sheila C. v. Povich


3331


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


11 A.D.3d 120; 781 N.Y.S.2d 342; 2004 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10400



August 26, 2004, Decided



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed in part and modified in part; complaint dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a television talk show guest, her mother, and her grandmother, appealed from the judgment of the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), that granted a motion by defendants, a talk show and its staff, to dismiss the complaint for failure to state a cause of action pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 3211(a)(7).


OVERVIEW: The complaint asserted that, in response to a televised solicitation aired during the show, the guest's mother contacted the show by telephone and explained that she was the mother of an out-of-control teen, specifically, the guest. The guest conceded not only that she was no longer in the staff's custody at the time of the alleged assault. The record revealed that the taping had ended hours earlier, her mother and her legal guardian had resumed control over her and were supervising her in their hotel room at the time a staff driver initially made his attempt to contact the guest, and they were still supervising her when the guest later absconded from her guardians. The guest was not released without further supervision, but directly into the custody and supervision of her mother and grandmother, into a situation which was not foreseeably hazardous or in any way presented an immediate risk to her safety. As such, her complaint was devoid of any allegations concerning the essential element of negligent supervision that the employer knew, or should have known, of the employee's propensity for the sort of conduct which caused the injury, or the identity of the employees involved.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Negligence -- Negligent Supervision of Child -- Talk Show Not Liable for Rape of Teenage Guest

1. Plaintiff, a teenager who was allegedly raped by defendants' "limo driver" after she appeared on defendants' talk show television program as an "out-of-control" minor with emotional difficulties, failed to state a negligent supervision cause of action against defendants. Defendants owed no duty of care to plaintiff at the time of the alleged attack, which occurred after plaintiff had been released from defendant's physical custody and control and returned directly into the custody and supervision of her mother and grandmother into a situation which was not foreseeably hazardous, or in any way presented an immediate risk to her safety. A temporary custodian does not have a continuing duty to protect a child from harm once that child has been returned to the custody of a parent or guardian.

Employment Relationships -- Respondeat Superior -- Negligent Hiring and Retention of Employee

2. Plaintiff, a teenager who was allegedly raped by defendants' "limo driver" after she appeared on defendants' talk show television program as an "out-of-control" minor with emotional difficulties, failed to state a cause of action against defendants for negligent hiring and retention in the absence of any allegations that defendants knew, or should have known, of their employee's propensity for the type of conduct that caused plaintiff's injury. Furthermore, plaintiff failed to identify the employee involved, and failed to establish that additional discovery was necessary to cure the pleading deficiencies.

Negligence -- Negligent Infliction of Emotional Distress

3. Plaintiff, a teenager who was allegedly raped by defendants' "limo driver" after she appeared on defendants' talk show television program as an "out-of-control" minor with emotional difficulties, failed to state a cause of action against defendants for negligent infliction of emotional distress. A cause of action for either intentional or negligent infliction of emotional distress must be supported by allegations of conduct by the defendants so outrageous in character, and so extreme in degree, as to go beyond all possible bounds of decency, and to be regarded as atrocious, and utterly intolerable in a civilized community. Plaintiff's allegations that defendants suggested she act provocatively, and allowed her to be introduced to a purported rapist, with whom she had a later, voluntary meeting, well after she was no longer in the physical custody of defendants, did not rise to the level of conduct necessary to sustain either cause of action.

Negligence -- Violation of Statutory Duty -- Endangering Welfare of Child

4. Plaintiff, a teenager who was allegedly raped by defendants' "limo driver" after she appeared on defendants' talk show television program as an "out-of-control" minor with emotional difficulties, failed to state a cause of action against defendants for negligence per se based upon a violation of the endangering the welfare of a child statute (Penal Law § 260.10 [1]). Since the statute only sets forth a general, abstract standard prohibiting individuals from knowingly engaging in acts likely to be injurious to the physical, mental or moral welfare of a minor, without specifically defining those acts, it cannot support a claim for negligence per se.

 

623 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Schantz v. O'Sullivan


94288


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


11 A.D.3d 22; 780 N.Y.S.2d 813; 2004 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10049



July 29, 2004, Decided  
July 29, 2004, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Appeal dismissed by Schantz v. O'Sullivan, 3 N.Y.3d 767, 821 N.E.2d 975, 2004 N.Y. LEXIS 3774, 788 N.Y.S.2d 670 (2004)
Subsequent appeal at Schantz v. O'Sullivan, 24 A.D.3d 1080, 806 N.Y.S.2d 753, 2005 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 14668 (N.Y. App. Div. 3d Dep't, Dec. 22, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Order of the Supreme Court reversed, on the law, without costs; Defendant's motion denied, Plaintiff's cross motion granted, chapter 71 of the Laws of 2002 declared unconstitutional, and matter remitted to the Supreme Court for further proceedings not inconsistent with this Court's decision.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant attorney commenced a foreclosure action against appellee matrimonial litigant. The litigant moved for an order directing the referee to cease and desist in the sale of her home. The attorney cross-moved for a declaration that 2002 N.Y. Laws 71 was unconstitutional as it violated the Contract Clause. The Supreme Court, Albany County (New York) granted the litigant's motion and denied the attorney's cross motion. The attorney appealed.


OVERVIEW: The matrimonial litigant gave her attorney two mortgages over a decade prior to the enactment of 2002 N.Y. Laws 71. The mortgages were given in 1988 and 1991 to secure payment for a debt in connection with legal services provided by the attorney in a divorce action, which settled in August 1994. 2002 N.Y. Laws 71 was enacted on May 21, 2002, and took effect immediately. It was intended primarily to prohibit the foreclosure of all mortgages given to secure payment of legal fees in matrimonial actions, including those obtained prior to the effective date of the rule. On appeal, the court found that 2002 N.Y. Laws 71 operated as a substantial impairment of the parties' contractual rights under the mortgages, which concededly were legal at the time they were given. Furthermore, 2002 N.Y. Laws 71 delayed foreclosure indefinitely and did not provide an alternate remedy, causing a sever impact on the value of the mortgages. Therefore, 2002 N.Y. Laws 71 constituted an unconstitutional impairment of the contracts.


OUTCOME: The order was reversed, the litigant's motion was denied, the attorney's cross motion was granted, 2002 N.Y. Laws 71 was declared unconstitutional, and the matter was remitted to the supreme court for further proceedings.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional Law -- Contract Clause -- Substantial Impairment of Contractual Rights -- Retroactive Statutory Prohibition on Attorney's Foreclosure of Mortgage Given by Client in Domestic Relations Matter 

Plaintiff was not precluded by chapter 71 of the Laws of 2002 from foreclosing on two mortgages executed by defendant in 1988 and 1991 in favor of her attorney (plaintiff's predecessor) to secure payment for a debt in connection with legal services provided in a divorce action which settled in August 1994. The court rule prohibiting foreclosure of a mortgage taken on a client's primary residence by an attorney in a domestic relations matter (22 NYCRR 1400.5 [b]; see also Code of Professional Responsibility DR 2-106 [c] [2] [iii] [22 NYCRR 1200.11 (c) (2) (iii)]) was inapplicable since plaintiff's predecessor commenced representation of defendant prior to the rule's November 30, 1993 effective date. Chapter 71, which expanded the prohibition to include mortgages obtained prior to the effective date of the court rule, is unconstitutional under the Contract Clause (US Const, art I, § 10) as applied to plaintiff, and thus did not bar plaintiff's foreclosure action. The statute, which delays foreclosure indefinitely for as long as the mortgagor chooses to retain the mortgaged property as a primary residence, without providing an alternate remedy for satisfying the debt, operated as a substantial impairment of the parties' contractual rights under the mortgages, which were legal at the time they were given. Furthermore, the fact that the legal profession is closely regulated did not preclude a finding of substantial impairment.

 

624 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Dalton v. Pataki


94493


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


11 A.D.3d 62; 780 N.Y.S.2d 47; 2004 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 9338



July 7, 2004, Decided  
July 7, 2004, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Motion granted by Dalton v. Pataki, 3 N.Y.3d 746, 821 N.E.2d 137, 2004 N.Y. LEXIS 3539, 787 N.Y.S.2d 711 (2004)
Motion granted by Dalton v. Pataki, 4 N.Y.3d 754, 823 N.E.2d 1292, 2005 N.Y. LEXIS 46, 790 N.Y.S.2d 644 (2005)
Motion granted by Dalton v. Pataki, 4 N.Y.3d 754, 823 N.E.2d 1291, 2005 N.Y. LEXIS 41, 790 N.Y.S.2d 643 (2005)
Affirmed in part and modified in part by Dalton v. Pataki, 5 N.Y.3d 243, 835 N.E.2d 1180, 2005 N.Y. LEXIS 1059, 802 N.Y.S.2d 72 (N.Y., May 3, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, taxpayers and others, challenged an order of the Supreme Court, Albany County (New York), which granted the cross motions for summary judgment filed by defendants, the governor and others, and dismissed the taxpayers' complaint that challenged the constitutionality of 2001 N.Y. Laws 383, pts. B, C, and D. Plaintiffs contended that these provisions, which authorized certain types of lotteries, violated N.Y. Const. art. I, § 9.


OVERVIEW: The challenged bill authorized the governor to enter into tribal-state compacts for casino gaming activities on Indian lands, 2001 N.Y. Laws 383, pt. B, pursuant to the Indian Gaming Regulatory Act (IGRA), 25 U.S.C.S. §§ 2701-2721, 18 U.S.C.S. §§ 1166-1168; permitted video lottery gaming, 2001 N.Y. Laws 383, pt. C; and authorized participation in a multistate lottery, 2001 N.Y. Laws 383, pt. D. Affirming in part but modifying in part, the court held that (1) because New York permitted the gaming activities authorized by 2001 N.Y. Laws 383, pt. B for charitable purposes, subject to heavy regulation, the gaming was properly the subject of a tribal-state compact; (2) video lottery gaming constituted a valid, state-operated lottery and was excepted from the general ban on gambling, but the requirement that vendor fees be dedicated to breeding funds violated the constitutional mandate that "the net proceeds" be applied exclusively to education under N.Y. Const. art. I, § 9(1); and (3) New York retained sufficient control over the multistate lottery within its borders to meet the requirement that lotteries be "operated by the State" under N.Y. Const. art. I, § 9(1).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the portion of the supreme court's decision holding that the provisions authorizing casino gaming on Indian lands and the participation in the multistate lottery was constitutional. It also affirmed the finding that video lottery gaming was constitutional, but because the provision authorizing that type of gaming did not apply net proceeds exclusively to education, the whole provision was struck as unconstitutional.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional Law -- Messages of Necessity

1. Legislation authorizing the Governor to enter into tribal-state compacts with Indian tribes to allow casino gaming on Indian lands and also authorizing the Division of the Lottery to license and implement the operation of video lottery gaming at certain pari-mutuel racetracks, as well as to operate, administer and enter into agreements for multistate lotteries within the state in cooperation with government-authorized lotteries of one or more jurisdictions (L 2001, ch 383) was validly enacted in conformance with the constitutional requirement of a "message of necessity" from the Governor for an immediate vote by the Legislature. The "message of necessity" provision requires that a bill in final form be on legislators' desks for "at least three calendar legislative days [before] final passage, unless the governor ... shall have certified ... the facts which ... necessitate an immediate vote thereon" (N.Y. Const., art III, § 14). The Governor's "message of necessity" indicated that "[b]ecause the bills have not been on your desks in final form for three calendar legislative days, the Leaders of your Honorable Bodies have requested this message to permit their immediate consideration." It further stated that the "facts necessitating an immediate vote on the bills" are that the "bills are necessary to enact certain provisions of law." The "message of necessity" literally and reasonably conformed with the constitutional requirements.

Constitutional Law -- Validity of Statute -- Casino Gaming on Indian Lands Pursuant to Federal Indian Gaming Regulatory Act

2. Legislation authorizing the Governor to enter into tribal-state compacts with Indian tribes to allow class III casino gaming on Indian lands (L 2001, ch 383, part B) pursuant to the Indian Gaming Regulatory Act (IGRA) (25 U.S.C. §§ 2701-2721; 18 U.S.C. §§ 1166-1168) was not violative of the State's constitutional prohibition against commercialized gambling activities (N.Y. Const., art I, § 9). IGRA authorizes a state to enter into tribal-state compacts permitting particular class III, casino-type gaming activities (see 25 U.S.C. § 2703 [8]) on tribal lands so long as the state "permits such gaming for any purpose by any person, organization, or entity" (25 U.S.C. § 2710 [d] [1] [B]). Under IGRA, class III games that are not criminally prohibited by state laws are properly the subject of negotiation in tribal-state compacts even if those games are heavily regulated and permitted to be played only by charities. Because New York permits casino gaming activities for charitable purposes, subject to heavy regulation (see General Municipal Law § 186 [3]; 9 NYCRR 5620.1), the gaming was properly the subject of a tribal-state compact. Furthermore, the legislation did not constitute an unlawful delegation of legislative authority to the Governor. The fact that the statute leaves discretion to the Governor in negotiating compacts with Indian tribes merely permits compliance with the State's obligation to engage in good-faith negotiations (see 25 U.S.C. § 2710 [d] [3] [A]).

Lotteries -- Video Lottery Gaming -- Constitutionality of Operation of Video Lottery Terminals at Pari-mutuel Racetracks 

3. Legislation authorizing the Division of the Lottery to license and implement the operation of video lottery terminals (VLTs) at certain pari-mutuel racetracks (L 2001, ch 383, part C; Tax Law § 1617-a) was not violative of the State's constitutional prohibition against commercialized gambling activities. VLTs do not fall within the definition of illegal slot machines (Penal Law § 225.00 [8]). Even though VLTs outwardly resemble slot machines, video lottery gaming, as implemented by the Division, falls within the constitutional exception to the general ban on gambling for state-operated "lotteries" (N.Y. Const., art I, § 9 [1]). The games offered on VLTs involve the elements of consideration, chance, prize, tickets and multiple participation necessary to constitute "lotteries" (see Penal Law § 225.00 [10]). Play on VLTs involves electronic tickets, which are transferred from the central system to site controllers and then to display terminals upon purchase, but which are not printed or reduced to paper. The electronic tickets are thus the functional equivalent of paper tickets. The State Constitution contains no bar to the introduction of new technological methods of delivering lottery tickets to the public.

Lotteries -- Video Lottery Gaming -- Constitutionality of Operation of Video Lottery Terminals at Pari-mutuel Racetracks - Invalidity of Revenue Distribution Scheme

4. Legislation authorizing the Division of the Lottery to license and implement the operation of video lottery terminals (VLTs) at certain pari-mutuel racetracks (L 2001, ch 383, part C; Tax Law § 1617-a) was not violative of the State's constitutional prohibition against commercialized gambling activities, since video lottery gaming, as implemented by the Division, fell within the constitutional exception to the general ban on gambling for state-operated "lotteries" (N.Y. Const., art I, § 9 [1]). However, that portion of the law requiring racetracks to transfer a portion of their vendor fees to breeding funds and for the purpose of enhancing purses at the racetracks where VLTs are located (see L 2001, ch 383, part C, § 2; Tax Law § 1612 [c] [1]), was violative of the constitutional mandate that "the net proceeds" of state-run lotteries "be applied exclusively to or in aid or support of education in this state." Reinvestment in breeding funds and enhanced purses is not a reasonable, necessary expense or cost of maintaining VLTs, and thus, funds dedicated for that purpose cannot be deducted from the net proceeds of the lottery without violating the constitutional requirement that lottery revenues be used to support education. Furthermore, the invalid revenue distribution scheme could not be severed to permit the statute to otherwise operate in a constitutional manner.

Lotteries -- Validity of Multistate Lotteries -- Compliance with Constitutional Requirement That Net Proceeds from State-Operated Lottery be used Exclusively for Educational Purposes

5. Legislation that directed the Division of the Lottery to operate and administer multistate lotteries within the state in cooperation with a government-authorized lottery of one or more jurisdictions (see L 2001, ch 383, part D, § 1; Tax Law § 1604 [a]), and further authorized the Director of the Lottery to enter into agreements for a multistate game, fell within the constitutional exception to the general ban on gambling for state-operated "lotteries" (N.Y. Const., art I, § 9 [1]). While certain joint functions and necessary operating costs of the "Mega Millions" multistate lottery game are shared, New York retains sufficient control over the operation of the multistate lottery within its borders (see 21 NYCRR part 2806) to satisfy the constitutional requirement that lotteries be "operated by the state." Furthermore, the transfer of funds to other states for operational expenses and prizes does not violate the constitutional requirement that the net proceeds from a state-operated lottery be devoted "exclusively to or in aid or support of education in this state." The funds transferred by New York to other states may be used only for payment of jackpot prizes and reimbursement of preapproved operational expenses. New York funds are not used by other states to reduce their administrative costs or to fund their governmental purposes.

Courtroom TV Network, LLC v. State


3964


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


8 A.D.3d 164; 779 N.Y.S.2d 74; 2004 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 8662; 32 Media L. Rep. 2217



June 22, 2004, Decided  
June 22, 2004, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Motion granted by Courtroom TV Network, LLC v. State, 4 N.Y.3d 786, 827 N.E.2d 280, 2005 N.Y. LEXIS 182, 794 N.Y.S.2d 297 (2005)
Motion granted by Courtroom TV Network, LLC v. State, 4 N.Y.3d 785, 827 N.E.2d 280, 2005 N.Y. LEXIS 195, 794 N.Y.S.2d 297 (2005)
Motion granted by Courtroom TV Network, LLC v. State, 4 N.Y.3d 786, 827 N.E.2d 281, 2005 N.Y. LEXIS 207, 794 N.Y.S.2d 297 (2005)
Motion granted by Courtroom TV Network LLC v. State, 4 N.Y.3d 808, 828 N.E.2d 986, 2005 N.Y. LEXIS 465, 796 N.Y.S.2d 29 (N.Y., Mar. 24, 2005)
Motion granted by Courtroom TV Network, LLC v. State, 4 N.Y.3d 823, 829 N.E.2d 669, 2005 N.Y. LEXIS 767, 796 N.Y.S.2d 576 (N.Y., Mar. 31, 2005)
Motion granted by Courtroom TV Network, LLC v. State, 4 N.Y.3d 823, 829 N.E.2d 668, 2005 N.Y. LEXIS 756, 796 N.Y.S.2d 576 (N.Y., Mar. 31, 2005)
Motion granted by Courtroom TV Network LLC v. State, 4 N.Y.3d 848, 830 N.E.2d 315, 2005 N.Y. LEXIS 1027, 797 N.Y.S.2d 416 (N.Y., Apr. 28, 2005)
Affirmed by Courtroom Tv Network LLC v. State, 5 N.Y.3d 222, 833 N.E.2d 1197, 2005 N.Y. LEXIS 1260, 800 N.Y.S.2d 522 (N.Y., June 16, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff television network appealed from the denial by the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), of the network's motion for partial summary judgment to declare N.Y. Civ. Rights Law § 52 unconstitutional, from the entry of summary judgment to defendant State on its cross-motion, from the entry of summary judgment to defendant county upon a search of the record, and from an order upholding the constitutionality of the statute on its face.


OVERVIEW: The network argued that it had a constitutional right to televise criminal trials. The appellate court held that § 52 did not violate the First Amendment, as it was sufficiently tailored to further an important state interest, namely, the preservation of the value and integrity of live witness testimony in state tribunals. The legislature could reasonably conclude that its interest in fair trials outweighed the benefits of permitting camera coverage. The availability of less restrictive means did not render the content-neutral statute invalid. Section 52 did not abridge the opportunities for the communication of thought in public places, as reporters were free to attend the trial and to report whatever they observed. The claim that there was a right under N.Y. Const. art. I, § 8 to televise court proceedings was also rejected. Although the New York Constitution was more protective of expressional freedoms than the U.S. Constitution in some respects, there was no precedent for a right of televised access, and art. I, § 8 had not been interpreted as granting any greater access rights than those provided under Richmond Newspapers v. Virginia and its progeny.


OUTCOME: The orders were affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional Law--Validity of Statute--Prohibition of Broadcast of Court Proceedings.--Section 52 of Civil Rights Law is not unconstitutional; there is no Federal Constitutional right to televise court proceedings and, although right to attend criminal trials is implicit in guarantees of First Amendment, right to view them on television screen is not (US Const 1st Amend; NY Const, art I, § 8)--assuming that section's prohibition of televised trials restricts "speech" within meaning of First Amendment, it is sufficiently tailored to further important state interest, namely, preservation of value and integrity of live witness testimony in state tribunals.

People v. Robinson


KA 01-02195


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FOURTH DEPARTMENT


8 A.D.3d 1028; 778 N.Y.S.2d 808; 2004 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 8241



June 14, 2004, Decided  
June 14, 2004, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Appeal granted by People v. Robinson, 2004 N.Y. LEXIS 3559 (N.Y., Sept. 16, 2004)
Motion granted by People v. Robinson, 3 N.Y.3d 733, 820 N.E.2d 286, 2004 N.Y. LEXIS 3975 (2004)
Motion granted by People v. Rivera, 3 N.Y.3d 747, 821 N.E.2d 138, 2004 N.Y. LEXIS 3540, 787 N.Y.S.2d 712 (2004)
Affirmed by, Sub nomine at People v. Daniels, 5 N.Y.3d 738, 833 N.E.2d 704, 2005 N.Y. LEXIS 1252, 800 N.Y.S.2d 369 (2005)
Writ of habeas corpus granted Robinson v. Superintendent of Wende Corr. Facility, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 37969 (W.D.N.Y., Apr. 16, 2010)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed, as modified, in part, reversed and new trial granted in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Following a jury trial, the Erie County Court (New York) convicted defendant of two counts of attempted murder in the first degree, in violation of N.Y. Penal Law §§ 110.00 and 125.27(1)(a)(i) and (1)(b), two counts of reckless endangerment in the first degree, in violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 120.25, and criminal possession of a weapon in the third degree, in violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 265.02. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with two counts of attempted murder in the first degree, two counts of reckless endangerment in the first degree, and criminal possession of a weapon in the third degree after he fired a semiautomatic weapon at police officers who stopped his vehicle. A jury found him guilty of all charges and the trial court entered judgment convicting defendant. The appellate court held that (1) defendant failed to preserve his claim that police violated his constitutional right against unlawful search and seizure when they seized items from his aunt's apartment, where he was apprehended, because he did not file a motion to suppress evidence the police seized; (2) the trial court did not err when it denied defendant's motion to suppress the showup identification of one of the victims; but (3) defendant should not have been convicted of attempted murder in the first degree and reckless endangerment in the first degree arising out of the same act and causing the same result, and the appellate court would exercise its power to review defendant's convictions as a matter of discretion, pursuant to N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 470.15(6)(a), and order a new trial on those charges.


OUTCOME: The appellate court modified the trial court's judgment by reversing those parts of the judgment that convicted defendant of two counts of attempted murder in the first degree and two counts of reckless endangerment in the first degree, affirmed the judgment as modified, and granted defendant a new trial on the charges of attempted murder and reckless endangerment.


HEADNOTES

Crimes--Identification of Defendant--Showup.--Court did not err in failing to suppress showup identification; officer at issue had unobstructed views of defendant's face four separate times, while police were attempting to stop defendant's vehicle and during shooting; in addition, during one of those occasions, spotlight from police vehicle was shining on defendant's face; officer identified defendant, who was handcuffed and in patrol car, in proximity to scene of shooting and 15 minutes after shooting; fact that defendant was handcuffed and seated in patrol car did not render procedure unduly suggestive.

Crimes--Verdict--Inconsistent Verdict.--Defendant failed to preserve for review his contention that verdict was repugnant insofar as he was found guilty of both attempted murder in first-degree and reckless endangerment in first degree--nevertheless, defendant cannot be convicted of intentional and reckless behavior arising from same act and causing same result, and contention is reviewed in interest of justice--judgment modified by reversing those parts convicting defendant of two counts each of attempted murder in first degree and reckless endangerment in first degree.

Huckaby v. N.Y. State Div. of Tax Appeals


92539


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


6 A.D.3d 988; 776 N.Y.S.2d 125; 2004 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 5008



April 29, 2004, Decided  
April 29, 2004, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Affirmed by Huckaby v. N.Y. State Div. of Tax Appeals, 4 N.Y.3d 427, 829 N.E.2d 276, 2005 N.Y. LEXIS 497, 796 N.Y.S.2d 312 (N.Y., Mar. 29, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Determination confirmed; petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner nonresident commenced a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, initiated in the court pursuant to N.Y. Tax Law § 2016, to review a determination of respondent New York Tax Appeals Tribunal, which sustained an assessment of personal income tax imposed upon the nonresident.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was a resident of the State of Tennessee and employed by a business located in the State of New York. In 1994 and 1995, petitioner spent approximately 25 percent of his time working in New York. He filed nonresident income tax returns, apportioning his income between New York and the Tennessee, to reflect the number of days he spent working in each state. New York's Department of Taxation and Finance determined that 100 percent of petitioner's income was allocable to New York and issued notices of deficiency. The tribunal affirmed the tax assessment and the art. 78 proceeding ensued. Petitioner contended that the "convenience of the employer" test used was inconsistent with N.Y. Tax Law § 631, which focused on the location of where the work was performed, rather than on the location of the employer. The court disagreed and held that New York's reliance on the "convenience of the employer" test to apportion nonresident income was rationally related to its legitimate interest in taxing nonresident income derived from New York sources. The court found there was a nexus with New York sufficient to support taxation of petitioner's income.


OUTCOME: The court confirmed the determination and dismissed the petition.


HEADNOTES

Taxation-Personal Income Tax.--Where petitioner, Tennessee resident who worked for organization based in New York primarily from his home in Tennessee, but spent 25% of his time working in New York, 100% of petitioner's income was allocable to New York--New York taxes income of nonresidents to extent that income is "derived from or connected with New York sources" (Tax Law § 631 [b] [1]), including any income attributable to "business, trade, profession or occupation carried on in this state" (Tax Law § 631 [b] [1] [B])--under "convenience of the employer" test, income earned from work in Tennessee was taxable by New York because it was not performed in Tennessee due to necessity of his New York employer--"convenience of the employer" test is not inconsistent with Tax Law § 631--since petitioner derived benefits from New York, there was ample justification for state to tax income he derives from New York--petitioner has not been deprived of equal protection by virtue of this tax scheme.

 

628 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Pataki v. N.Y. State Assembly


91757


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


7 A.D.3d 74; 774 N.Y.S.2d 891; 2004 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 4746



April 22, 2004, Decided  
April 22, 2004, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Affirmed by Pataki v. N.Y. State Assembly, 4 N.Y.3d 75, 824 N.E.2d 898, 791 N.Y.S.2d 458, 2004 N.Y. LEXIS 3796 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the state legislature, appealed from an order of the Supreme Court in Albany County (New York), which, among other things, declared unconstitutional the procedure used regarding 46 budget bills passed by the legislature and signed into law by respondent governor. The governor contended that such conduct ran afoul of the restriction on altering appropriation bills contained in N.Y. Const. art. VII, § 4.


OVERVIEW: The governor commenced an action in his official capacity, alleging that subsequent to his constitutionally-mandated annual submission of the executive budget, the legislature unconstitutionally (1) amended and altered nine of the 11 budget bills that he had submitted and (2) introduced and passed 37 appropriation bills in an improper attempt to disregard the governor's executive budget and substitute their own. When the legislature altered the governor's appropriation bills in an allegedly unconstitutional manner, the governor was injured, and thus, had standing to sue. Further, the governor was not obligated to exercise his veto power, as argued by the legislature, and thereby further prolong an already stagnant and fractious budget process in order to create judicially cognizable standing. Finally, the legislature's actions in amending nine of the budget bills submitted by the governor and introducing and passing 37 single-purpose appropriation bills violated N.Y. Const. art. VII, § 4.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Parties -- Standing -- Power of Legislature to Alter Governor's Budget Bills

1. Plaintiff Governor possessed standing to challenge the constitutionality of the actions of the Legislature in amending and altering nine of the budget bills submitted by plaintiff in 2001 allegedly in violation of NY Constitution, art VII, § 4. Plaintiff's failure to have vetoed the 46 budget bills enacted by the Legislature did not deprive him of standing or effect a waiver of his right to challenge the constitutionality of defendants' actions. Plaintiff was injured for standing purposes when defendants altered his budget bills in an allegedly unconstitutional manner. Plaintiff was not obligated to exercise his veto power and thereby further prolong an already stagnant and fractious budget process in order to create judicially cognizable standing.

State -- Budget -- Power of Legislature to Alter Governor's Budget Bills

2. The New York State Assembly and Senate acted unconstitutionally in amending nine of the budget bills submitted by plaintiff Governor in 2001, and introducing and passing 37 single-purpose appropriation bills in violation of NY Constitution, art VII, § 4. Defendants lacked the power to strike the substantive modifiers inserted by plaintiff within his appropriation bills. Such substantive modifiers were part of a gubernatorial appropriation bill and were thus subject to constitutional protection from being altered by the Legislature. Defendants' proper constitutional action was to refuse to pass plaintiff's appropriation bills and induce negotiations, not to alter and amend them and then substitute their own spending plans in the form of 37 single purpose bills.

 [***1] State--Unjust Conviction and Imprisonment Act.--Claimant failed to state claim for relief on any of grounds in Court of Claims Act § 8-b (3) (b) since reversal of his criminal conviction and dismissal of underlying indictment were not based upon unconstitutional application of underlying penal statutes, but was warranted by failure to comply with procedural requirement regarding prohibition of duplicitous indictments--alternative theory, that trial court lacked jurisdiction to prosecute him, is unavailing since indictment charging claimant, while duplicitous, was not jurisdictionally defective; in any event, claimant failed to show he would likely succeed in proving that he did not commit any of acts charged in accusatory instrument (Court of Claims Act § 8-b [4], [5]).

 

630 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Schulz v. N.Y. State Legislature


93821


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


5 A.D.3d 885; 773 N.Y.S.2d 174; 2004 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 2536



March 11, 2004, Decided  
March 11, 2004, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Appeal dismissed by Schulz v. N.Y. State Legislature, 2 N.Y.3d 793, 814 N.E.2d 463, 2004 N.Y. LEXIS 1068, 781 N.Y.S.2d 291 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners commenced a declaratory judgment action and N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding, following passage of certain resolutions relating to a solid waste resource recovery facility by respondents, two county board of supervisors. The Supreme Court, Albany County (New York), granted a cross motion by one of the boards for summary judgment, and granted the other board's cross motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: In two of the claims, petitioners were attempting, in part, to relitigate issues already unsuccessfully litigated in their original complaint, challenging the enabling legislation pursuant to which the facility was built. Those claims were barred by principles of res judicata and collateral estoppel. There was no merit to petitioners' assertion that one of the county's budget note resolutions constituted a contract of county indebtedness for a period longer than the probable useful life of the purpose of the debt. The undisputed purpose of the budget notes was to provide sufficient county funds to pay its contractual share of waste disposal fees. Thus, the purpose of the debt incurred by the budget notes (to pay the monthly disposal fees) would last at least as long as the debt (the budget notes). Also, petitioners' claim that the resolutions violated N.Y. Const. art. VII, § 7 lacked merit because the comptroller would actually be intercepting separate county sales tax revenues (not state sales tax revenues). Petitioners' claim that the home rule resolutions at issue violated N.Y. Const. art. VII, § 8 failed for the same reason.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Judgments--Collateral Estoppel.--In combined proceeding pursuant to CPLR article 78 and action for declaratory judgment concerning financing and maintenance of solid waste resource recovery facility, petitioners' attempt to relitigate contentions already unsuccessfully litigated in their original 1992 petition/complaint, i.e., "that the Counties' use of taxpayer funds to pay the monthly disposal fees constitutes aiding a public corporation or gifting/loaning to private corporation in violation of NY Constitution, article X, § 5 and NY Constitution, article VIII, § 1," is entirely barred by collateral estoppel precepts.

Judgments--Res Judicata--Collateral Estoppel.--In combined proceeding pursuant to CPLR article 78 and action for declaratory judgment concerning financing and maintenance of solid waste resource recovery facility, petitioners' challenges, whether new or repeated, to Laws of 1985 (ch 682) and to underlying agreements are completely barred forever by principles of res judicata and collateral estoppel.

Municipal Corporations--Home Rule Powers.--In combined proceeding pursuant to CPLR article 78 and action for declaratory judgment concerning financing and maintenance of solid waste resource recovery facility, petitioners failed to overcome strong presumption of constitutionality attached to challenged resolutions; no merit is shown in petitioners' assertion that Warren County Budget Note Resolutions constitute contract of County indebtedness for period longer than probable useful life of purpose of debt, in violation of NY Contitiution, article VIII, § 2; undisputed purpose of budget notes, which Warren County Board of Supervisors directed County to issue and which were to mature to less than on year, was to provide sufficient County funds to pay its contractual share of disposal fees (since insufficient funds had been appropriated in County budget to cover fees).

Municipal Corporations--Home Rule Powers.--In combined proceeding pursuant to CPLR article 78 and action for declaratory judgment concerning financing and maintenance of solid waste resource recovery facility, there was no merit to contention that Home Rule Resolutions violated NY Constitution, article VII, §§ 7 and 8; resolutions merely requested passage of legislation by Legislature and did not themselves take any action contemplated by constitutional provisions, such as paying state money or gifting/lending state money or credit, rendering inapplicable these constitutional provisions.

Local Gov't Assistance Corp. v. Sales Tax Asset Receivable Corp.


94390, 94533


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


5 A.D.3d 829; 773 N.Y.S.2d 460; 2004 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 2234



March 4, 2004, Decided  
March 4, 2004, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Appeal denied by Local Gov't Assistance Corp. v. Sales Tax Asset Receivable Corp., 2 N.Y.3d 731, 810 N.E.2d 904, 2004 N.Y. LEXIS 494, 778 N.Y.S.2d 452 (2004)
Motion granted by Local Gov't Assistance Corp. v. Sales Tax Asset Receivable Corp., 2 N.Y.3d 753, 810 N.E.2d 909, 2004 N.Y. LEXIS 595, 778 N.Y.S.2d 457 (2004)
Motion denied by Local Gov't Assistance Corp. v. Sales Tax Asset Receivable Corp., 2 N.Y.3d 771, 812 N.E.2d 1247, 2004 N.Y. LEXIS 949, 780 N.Y.S.2d 299 (N.Y., May 4, 2004)
Motion granted by Local Gov't Assistance Mayors v. Sales Tax Asset Receivable Corp., 2 N.Y.3d 771, 812 N.E.2d 1247, 2004 N.Y. LEXIS 952, 780 N.Y.S.2d 299 (N.Y., May 4, 2004)
Modified by Local Gov't Assistance Corp. v. Sales Tax Asset Receivable Corp., 2 N.Y.3d 524, 813 N.E.2d 587, 2004 N.Y. LEXIS 1049, 780 N.Y.S.2d 507 (N.Y., May 13, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Appeal from order entered 8/20/2003 dismissed; order entered 9/17/2003 affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a local finance corporation, appealed from an order of the Supreme Court, Albany County (New York), that denied its motion for a preliminary injunction enjoining defendants, a receiving corporation and a city, from implementing the Municipal Assistance Corporation Refinancing Act, and from an order that granted the city's motion for summary judgment declaring said Act constitutional as challenged.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to the Act, the local finance corporation, a public authority created to issue debt and provide funding for public services, was to make annual payments to the city. The receiving corporation was created as an assignee of such payments for the purpose of issuing bonds, the proceeds of which were to be used to retire the remaining debt. The finance corporation contended that by exempting payments from the requirement of annual legislative appropriations, the Act in its entirety was unconstitutional. The legislature intended to assure the rating agencies and prospective bond purchasers that there was little or no risk in such investment, thereby assuring the salability of the bonds. Such purpose could be accomplished even with the severance of the offending portion of the Act. Further, since the receiving corporation was assignee of the city's debt, the debt created was that of the receiving corporation, not of the city, which had previously been held to be constitutional. Finally, the finance corporation's requirement to make the annual payments was not inconsistent with the guarantees in N.Y. Pub. Auth. Law § 3832-a.


OUTCOME: The appeal from the denial of a preliminary injunction was dismissed. The order granting summary judgment was reversed, a portion of the Act was deemed unconstitutional and severed, and as modified, the judgment was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional Law--Validity of Statute--Municipal Assistance Corporation Refinancing Act.--Municipal Assistance Corporation (MAC) Refinancing Act (Act), which provides that Local Government Assistance Corporation shall transfer $ 170,000,000 annually to City for period of 30 years (see Public Authorities Law § 3238-a), violates NY Constitution, art VII § 11 to extent that it creates annual payment obligation not subject to annual appropriation by Legislature and not approved by referendum; entire Act need not be declared unconstitutional as offending portion is severable; overriding purpose of Legislature in creating Act was to assist City financially in enabling it to eliminate remaining payments due on MAC indebtedness; such purpose will be accomplished even with severance of offending portion of Act.

Constitutional Law--Validity of Statute--Municipal Assistance Corporation Refinancing Act.--Contention that portion of Municipal Assistance Corporation Refinancing Act providing for assignment by City of New York of Local Government Assistance Corporation (LGAC) payments to Sales Tax Asset Receivable Corporation (STARC) constitutes impermissible revenue financing in that City has obligated future sources of revenue for immediate cash to satisfy short-term indebtedness is rejected; while plaintiffs argue that City has contracted indebtedness without pledging its faith and credit in contravention of provisions of NY Constitution, article VIII, § 2, debt created is that of STARC, not City, and such financing schemes repeatedly have withstood constitutional attack.

Constitutional Law--Validity of Statute--Municipal Assistance Corporation Refinancing Act.--Municipal Assistance Corporation Refinancing Act does not unconstitutionally impair contractual rights of Local Government Assistance Corporation (LGAC) bondholders in violation of US Constitution, art I, § 10; while Act does provide that "[n]otwithstanding any inconsistent provision of law [LGAC] shall transfer" $ 170 million to New York City (Public Authorities Law § 3238-a), this provision is not inconsistent with pledge contained in Public Authorities Law § 3241 (1).

Levenson v. Lippman


2465


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


5 A.D.3d 86; 772 N.Y.S.2d 286; 2004 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 1976



February 24, 2004, Decided  
February 24, 2004, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Appeal denied by Levenson v. Lippman, 2 N.Y.3d 819, 814 N.E.2d 454, 2004 N.Y. LEXIS 1374, 781 N.Y.S.2d 283 (2004)
Motion granted by Levenson v. Lippman, 3 N.Y.3d 686, 818 N.E.2d 648, 2004 N.Y. LEXIS 2194, 785 N.Y.S.2d 7 (2004)
Motion granted by Levenson v. Lippman, 3 N.Y.3d 747, 821 N.E.2d 138, 2004 N.Y. LEXIS 3535, 787 N.Y.S.2d 712 (2004)
Motion granted by Levenson v. Lippman, 4 N.Y.3d 731, 823 N.E.2d 1279, 2004 N.Y. LEXIS 3837, 790 N.Y.S.2d 633 (N.Y., Dec. 16, 2004)
Motion granted by Levenson v. Lippman, 4 N.Y.3d 751, 823 N.E.2d 1288, 2005 N.Y. LEXIS 17, 790 N.Y.S.2d 640 (N.Y., Jan. 6, 2005)
Reversed by Levenson v. Lippman, 4 N.Y.3d 280, 827 N.E.2d 259, 2005 N.Y. LEXIS 139, 794 N.Y.S.2d 276 (N.Y., Feb. 15, 2005)



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; orders modifying the awards of counsel compensation vacated; the original award orders were reinstated; plaintiffs granted judgment declaring 22 NYCRR 127.2 void.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff lawyers sued defendants in the Supreme Court, New York County (New York) seeking a declaration that N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 22, § 127.2 was null and void. The trial court found the challenged provision valid, and the lawyers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court's administrative judge vacated other trial courts' awards paying the lawyers for representing indigent criminal defendants above N.Y. County Law § 722-b's limit. The appellate court held the awards were within the trial courts' discretion. The statute did not say the legislature thought such awards were administrative acts or that their appellate review was foreclosed. The administrative judge, unlike the appellate court, could not, under N.Y. Jud. Law § 21, decide a question argued orally outside his presence. Administrative review of assigned counsel compensation conflicted with N.Y. County Law § 722-b, and, thus, N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit 22, § 127.2, purporting to allow such review, had to yield to the statute and conflicted with appellate review of a trial court's order under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 5501(c). N.Y. Jud. Law § 212(1)'s grant of authority to the administrative judge to supervise trial court administration did not allow review of a judicial act, such as compensating counsel, which was subject to review, if at all, by the appellate court. The administrative judge's orders were subject to appellate review under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 5501(c) and 5701.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, its orders modifying awards of counsel compensation were vacated, and the original award orders were reinstated. Judgment declaring the challenged rule null and void was entered.


HEADNOTES

Appeal -- Appellate Division -- Matters Reviewable--Awards of Legal Fees Pursuant to County Law § 722-b 

The exercise of appellate jurisdiction by an administrative judge by modifying orders awarding legal fees pursuant to County Law § 722-b constituted an impermissible intrusion upon the appellate jurisdiction of the Appellate Division and was therefore ultra vires. 22 NYCRR 127.2 (b), providing for such administrative review, is null and void as having been amended in excess of the authority granted to the Chief Administrator of the Courts by the Legislature and the New York Constitution. Nothing in the language of County Law § 722-c suggests that the Legislature either considered the award of additional compensation due to extraordinary circumstances to be a purely administrative act or intended that compensation awards should be foreclosed from appellate review. Whether or not the award of compensation as fixed in County Law § 722-b may be said to be administrative in nature, the exercise of discretion to award fees in excess of the specified amounts constitutes a judicial function subject to review, if at all, by the appellate courts applying the traditional standard of abuse. There is no authority that would condone the transfer of this judicial function to an administrative judge. That the matter of counsel fees may be collateral to the criminal proceeding in which they are awarded does not render fee awards "administrative."

 

633 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Maine-Endwell Teachers' Ass'n v. Bd. of Educ.


93831


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


3 A.D.3d 685; 771 N.Y.S.2d 246; 2004 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 315



January 15, 2004, Decided  
January 15, 2004, Entered



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Judgment reversed; matter remitted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner union sued respondent education board in a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding after two public school employees, who were union members, were denied paid leave for up to three days of religious observances as provided in a collective bargaining agreement (CBA). The Broome County, New York, Supreme Court dismissed the suit because the provision in the CBA violated the Establishment Clause and was unenforceable. The union appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appeals court decided that the CBA's religious observance provision did not offend the Establishment Clause in that it did not impermissibly advance religion by coercing members of the union to profess a religious belief. The provision imposed no requirements regarding which religious holidays could be invoked and limited the number of such days to three. As such, the provision was more properly viewed as a reasonable "accommodation" of the two employees' religious beliefs, which was not violative of the Establishment Clause. Therefore, the provision was readily distinguishable from the Matter of Port Washington Union Free School District provision, a New York case. The provision in Port Washington not appearing to limit the number of religious holidays that could be taken went beyond reasonable accommodation and instead rose to a level of government pressure to participate in a religious activity, which was considered an obvious indication that the government was endorsing or promoting religion. To the extent Port Washington could be read to prohibit any religious observance clause as violative of the Establishment Clause, the appeals court declined to follow it.


OUTCOME: The appeals court reversed the judgment and remitted the matter to the trial court for further proceedings.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional Law--Establishment of Religion.--It was error to dismiss petition in proceeding brought by union of public school employees seeking judgment compelling respondent to comply with religious observance clause of collective bargaining agreement--contractual provision at issue did not offend Establishment Clause of US Constitution (see US Const 1st Amend) since it did not impermissibly advance religion by coercing members of union to profess religious belief.

Silver v. Pataki


1718


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


3 A.D.3d 101; 769 N.Y.S.2d 518; 2003 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13222



December 11, 2003, Decided  
December 11, 2003, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Affirmed by Pataki v. N.Y. State Assembly, 4 N.Y.3d 75, 824 N.E.2d 898, 2004 N.Y. LEXIS 3796, 791 N.Y.S.2d 458 (N.Y., Dec. 16, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff speaker of the state assembly filed an action against defendant governor, challenging the governor's use of a line-item veto against 55 amendments to bills the assembly passed. The Supreme Court, New York County (New York), granted the governor's motion for summary judgment, but allowed the state senate to intervene for purposes of appeal. The speaker and senate appealed.


OVERVIEW: In January 1998, the governor submitted his budget to the state legislature. The legislature made changes to appropriations bills which the governor submitted, but also changed other bills in ways that had the effect of modifying appropriations bills. The governor used a line-item veto to negate those changes and the speaker of the state assembly filed suit, arguing that the governor's use of the line-item veto was unconstitutional. The trial court found that the legislature exceeded its authority under the New York Constitution by changing non-appropriations bills in ways that affected appropriations bills, and it granted the governor's motion for summary judgment. The appellate court held that (1) the legislature's actions violated the non-alteration provision of N.Y. Const. art. VII, § 4, and the trial court properly granted the governor's motion for summary judgment; and (2) given the court's conclusion that the legislature's actions were unconstitutional, there was no need to address the speaker's claim that the governor's use of the line-item veto to invalidate the changes was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's order granting the governor's motion for summary judgment and agreed with the trial court that the constitutionality of the governor's use of line-item vetoes in this case need not be addressed.


HEADNOTES

State -- Budget -- Power of Legislature to Alter Governor's Budget Bills

1. The 1998 legislative amendments to the Governor's nonappropriation program bills with respect to the spending of appropriated funds unconstitutionally altered the budget bills submitted by the Governor in violation of NY Constitution, art VII, § 4 by reallocating or itemizing certain appropriations or conditioning them on subsequent legislative action. The no-alteration provision restricts the power of the Legislature to alter an appropriation bill submitted by the Governor "except to strike out or reduce items" or to add "items of appropriation provided that such additions are stated separately and distinctly from the original items of the bill and refer each to a single object or purpose." For purposes of the no-alteration provision, the Governor's "items of appropriation" properly include both the appropriation itself as well as the "when, how or where" directory provisions relating to the appropriation contained in nonappropriation bills. The no-alteration provision prohibits alterations of an appropriation bill by any means, not just by means of an alteration to the bill itself or by passage of a different appropriation measure.

Anthony v. Town of N. Hempstead


2003-00923


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT

Friedenburg v. N.Y. State Dep't of Envtl. Conservation


2001-05219


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


3 A.D.3d 86; 767 N.Y.S.2d 451; 2003 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 12447


October 3, 2002, Argued  
November 24, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected March 16, 2004.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, an estate administrator and others, sought to have defendant New York State Department of Environmental Conservation's denial of a wetlands permit be regarded as a taking of property without just compensation, and an order, pursuant to N.Y. Envtl. Conserv. Law § 25-0404, for condemnation proceedings. The Supreme Court, Suffolk County (New York), found that a taking without just compensation had occurred. The Department appealed.


OVERVIEW: The decedent owned the land parcel prior to the enactment of the Tidal Wetlands Act, N.Y. Envtl. Conserv. Law art. 25, ch. 790 (1973). The appellate court held that that the Department's denial of a permit for a single family dwelling did not constitute a categorical or per se taking of petitioners' property because it was conceded that the property retained at least a five percent residuary value. However, petitioners demonstrated a taking, as they established beyond a reasonable doubt that the regulation and denial of the permit destroyed all but a bare residue of the economic value of the property. The Department failed to rebut the appraiser's pre-regulation value as $ 665,000. It was determined that the residual property value was $ 31,500. Thus, there was a 95 percent reduction in value. Further, the Department's legitimate reasons for regulating tidal wetlands did not prevent petitioners from succeeding on the takings claim. Nor was there a finding of reciprocity of advantage or shared benefit, as petitioners were left with a situation where their only viable choice was to leave the property in its natural state.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional Law - Taking of Property - Tidal Wetlands - Regulatory Taking

1. The determination of respondent New York State Department of Environmental Conservation (DEC) which denied petitioners a tidal wetlands permit to construct a single family residence on their waterfront property, acquired by decedent in 1962 prior to the enactment of wetlands regulations, did not constitute a per se regulatory taking of petitioners' property where the property retained at least 5% of its preregulation value. A categorical or per se regulatory taking occurs only when a regulation permanently deprives property of all value. However, the reduction of the property's value by 95% from its nonregulated value still constituted a compensable regulatory taking under the applicable balancing test regarding the economic impact the regulation had on the property. Petitioners proved that there existed a strong probability that most, if not all, of the alternative recreational uses for the property proposed by DEC would not have been approved by the local zoning board. Petitioners thus demonstrated that the regulation and denial of the permit caused an almost total loss of the value of the property.

Courts - Jurisdiction

2. Where the Appellate Division upheld the finding of Supreme Court in a CPLR article 78 proceeding that the denial of petitioners' application for a tidal wetlands permit by the State Department of Environmental Conservation (DEC) resulted in a compensatory regulatory taking, if the DEC chooses to acquire the property under the exercise of its powers of eminent domain, which is its only option other than granting the permit, any further proceedings to determine compensation to be paid must be conducted in the Court of Claims.

Moran Towing Corp. v. Urbach


87765, 92881


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


1 A.D.3d 722; 768 N.Y.S.2d 33; 2003 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 11736



November 13, 2003, Decided  
November 13, 2003, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal withdrawn by Moran Towing Corp. v. Urbach, 3 N.Y.3d 635, 816 N.E.2d 196, 2004 N.Y. LEXIS 3570, 782 N.Y.S.2d 406 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgments affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayers challenged a judgment of the Supreme Court, Albany County (New York), which, inter alia, in a combined proceeding pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 and action for a declaratory judgment, declared N.Y. Tax Law §§ 301, 301-a to be facially constitutional and which granted respondent state tax commissioner's motion for partial summary judgment, denying the taxpayers' request for a refund of taxes previously paid.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers had commenced an action to overturn a decision of the state department of taxation, which denied its request for a petroleum business tax (PBT) refund premised on the ground that N.Y. Tax Law § 301(a)(1)(ii); 301-a(b)(2), (c)(1)(B) violated the U.S. Commerce Clause. After several appeals and remittals, the tax law was declared to be constitutional, and the taxpayers' requests for refunds were denied. The question before the court was whether the retroactive application of the PBT violated due process and, if so, whether refunds or counsel fees were due. The amendments to the tax law provided for tax credits in response to a prior decision, which had found the PBT tax unconstitutional in violation of interstate commerce. The court held that by making the refunds retroactively available, New York had provided meaningful backward-looking relief to rectify any unconstitutional deprivation. In addition, the taxpayers failed to sustain their burden of demonstrating that the retroactivity provisions were so harsh and oppressive as to transgress the constitutional limitation. Thus, the post-deprivation procedures to rectify the unconstitutional privation were adequate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the supreme court's judgments.


HEADNOTES

Taxation--Petroleum Gross Receipts Tax.--Amendments to Tax Law article 13-A (petroleum business tax) cured lack of internal consistency by providing credits, refunds and reimbursements to entites which were subjected to mutliple taxation--by making refunds retroactively available, state provided meaningful backward-looking relief to rectify any unconstitutional deprivation.

People v. Schehr


14551


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


1 A.D.3d 719; 766 N.Y.S.2d 642; 2003 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 11738



November 13, 2003, Decided  
November 13, 2003, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Counsel Corrected December 16, 2003.
Appeal denied by People v. Schehr, 1 N.Y.3d 601, 808 N.E.2d 368, 2004 N.Y. LEXIS 429, 776 N.Y.S.2d 232 (N.Y., Jan. 21, 2004)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment by the County Court of Tompkins County (New York) that, inter alia, denied parole; defendant claimed that the N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 410.91(4) consent to sentencing was unconstitutional as an improper delegation of judicial authority.


OVERVIEW: Claiming that he forged certain checks in order to support his cocaine habit, defendant sought to plead guilty and be sentenced to parole supervision for drug treatment pursuant to N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 410.91. However, when the prosecutor refused to provide the required consent under § 410.91(4), defendant pleaded guilty. The appellate court held that defendant failed to show that § 410.91(4) violated the separation of powers doctrine. While § 410.91(4) limited the court's discretion to the extent of requiring the prosecutor's consent prior to the imposition of a parole supervision sentence, it did not constrain the trial court to sentence defendant in any particular way. As such, defendant failed in his "heavy burden" of establishing that § 410.91(4) violated the separation of powers doctrine.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Crimes--Sentence.--While CPL 410.91 (4) limits court's discretion to extent of requiring prosecutor's consent prior to imposition of parole supervision sentence, it does not constrain court to sentence defendant in any particular way.

 

640 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Linzenberg v. Town of Ramapo


2003-00890


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


1 A.D.3d 321; 766 N.Y.S.2d 217; 2003 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 11527


September 26, 2003, Argued  
November 3, 2003, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant property owner sued respondent town, seeking a declaration that the town's zoning law was unconstitutional as applied to his property and to recover damages based on an alleged inverse condemnation of the property. The Supreme Court, Rockland County (New York), denied the property owner's summary judgment motion and entered summary judgment for the town dismissing the complaint. The property owner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The trial court dismissed the complaint on the ground, among other things, that it was time-barred. The appellate court ruled that since the gravamen of the complaint was to recover damages for inverse condemnation, the three-year statute of limitations set forth in N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 214(4) applied. Contrary to the trial court's determination, the inverse condemnation claim, if any, did not accrue until the town's zoning board reached a final decision regarding his application for area variances. Thus, the trial court erred in determining that the complaint was time-barred. Nevertheless, the cross motion to dismiss the complaint should have been granted on other grounds. The property owner never had an absolute right to build a single-family home on the premises without a variance. Even if the property owner had a cognizable property right, however, his conclusory allegations that the property could not yield an economically reasonable return as it was presently zoned were insufficient to establish an unconstitutional taking.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed, and the matter was remitted with instructions.


HEADNOTES

 [***1] Limitation of Actions--When Cause of Action Accrues.--In action for judgment declaring that Town Zoning Law is unconstitutional as applied to plaintiff's property and to recover damages based on approval by Town of certain subdivision and related actions which allegedly constituted inverse condemnation of property, it was error to dismiss complaint as barred by three-year statute of limitations (CPLR 214 [4])--inverse condemnation claim, if any, did not accrue until Zoning Board reached final decision regarding plaintiff's application for area variances.

Constitutional Law--Taking or Property.--Town Zoning Law is constitutional as applied to plaintiff's property, and challenged actions taken by Town did not constitute inverse condemnation of property--plaintiff never had absolute right to build single-family home on premises without variance; even if plaintiff had cognizable property right, his conclusory allegations that property could not yield economically reasonable return as it was presently zoned were insufficient to establish unconstitutional taking.

Weingarten v. Robles


2114


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


309 A.D.2d 614; 766 N.Y.S.2d 417; 2003 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10901



October 20, 2003, Decided  
October 20, 2003, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Appeal dismissed by, Appeal denied by Weingarten v. Robles, 100 N.Y.2d 630, 801 N.E.2d 414, 2003 N.Y. LEXIS 3359, 769 N.Y.S.2d 194 (N.Y., Oct. 23, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the Clerk of the City of New York and others, sought review of a decision of the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), which granted respondent voters' petition and declared N.Y. Mun. Home Rule Law § 36(5)(e) unconstitutional as applied against them, directed that the clerk certify the voters' proposed question for placement on a ballot, and denied appellants' cross motion to dismiss the petition.


OVERVIEW: The voters submitted their ballot question, proposing to submit a local law that would create a charter commission to examine, among other things, the New York City charter as it related to class size in the public schools. The submission complied with all statutory mandates but it was "bumped" from the ballot when an already existing charter revision commission presented its own proposed city charter amendments. Section 36(5)(e) required the "bump." The court reversed the finding of unconstitutionality, granted the cross motion, and dismissed the petition. The trial court applied the wrong standard in determining the constitutionality of § 36(5)(e). It used the strict scrutiny test instead of the rationality test. The rationality test was the appropriate test for review of voting regulations in states that permitted ballot initiatives.


OUTCOME: The trial court's decision was reversed and the cross motion for dismissal of the petition was granted.

Barklee Realty Co. LLC v. Pataki


349


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


309 A.D.2d 310; 765 N.Y.S.2d 599; 2003 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10678



October 16, 2003, Decided  
October 16, 2003, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal dismissed by Barklee Realty Co. LLC v. Pataki, 1 N.Y.3d 622, 808 N.E.2d 1279, 2004 N.Y. LEXIS 267, 777 N.Y.S.2d 20 (2004)
Appeal denied by Barklee Realty Co. LLC v. Pataki, 2 N.Y.3d 707, 814 N.E.2d 460, 2004 N.Y. LEXIS 1367, 781 N.Y.S.2d 288 (N.Y., June 8, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; plaintiffs' motion denied; injunction vacated; the Governor's motion granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff limited liability companies sued, inter alia, defendant governor in the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), for a declaration that N.Y. Ltd. Liab. Co. Law § 206 was unconstitutional and to enjoin enforcement of the statute's publication and filing requirements. The trial court declared the statute unconstitutional and granted the injunction, and the governor appealed.


OVERVIEW: The companies had to publish notice of their formation for six weeks before they could sue. The appellate court held N.Y. Const. art. 10, § 4, did not give them a general right of access to the courts, but only the same right given to a natural person in a similar case, who had no general right. The statute did not violate substantive due process as it did not arbitrarily restrict access to the courts under state law. As to equal protection, the companies were not in a suspect class. Finding the statute violated equal protection because it did not enhance the adjudication of justice did not address whether the statute was rationally related to a legitimate state interest. Limiting access to the courts permissibly enforced the statute's goal and did not have to relate to the court system. The statute applied equally to all domestic limited liability companies, and its requirements were imposed on other limited liability business entities. Only the legislature could decide if its publication requirement best gave notice of the companies' formation. The cost of complying with the statute was not shown to be prohibitive or invidiously discriminatory.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was reversed, the companies' motion for an injunction was denied and the injunction was vacated.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional Law -- Validity of Statute -- Limited Liability Company Law

 Section 206 of the Limited Liability Company Law, which requires each limited liability company to publish its articles of organization or comparable specified information for six successive weeks in two local newspapers of the county where the limited liability company has its principal office as a precondition to "maintaining any action or special proceeding" in any New York court, is constitutional. The IAS court erred in declaring the publication requirement violative of due process for placing a restriction on a limited liability company's access to the courts that is not reasonably related to the objective of enhancing the adjudication of justice. The only relevant inquiry in applying the "rational basis" test is whether the requirements of section 206 are rationally related to the promotion of any legitimate state interest. Section 206 has no direct bearing on the court system or the adjudication of justice, but is merely one of several steps a limited liability company must take in order to enjoy the full scope of its privilege to do business. Barring the maintenance of court proceedings by limited liability companies that have not complied with the publication requirement is rationally related to the goal of ensuring that those companies actually publish the designated information. Furthermore, the issue of whether the publication requirement is "necessary" as one of a number of means of disseminating particular information concerning newly formed limited liability companies to members of the public can only be addressed by the Legislature, not the courts.
