Westbury Trombo, Inc. v. Bd. of Trs.


2002-08014


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


307 A.D.2d 1043; 763 N.Y.S.2d 674; 2003 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 9028


May 13, 2003, Argued  
August 25, 2003, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Supreme Court, Nassau County (New York), denied petitioner citizen's application for a special use permit, denied the citizen's application for a use variance and to invalidate Westbury, N.Y. Local Laws 10-2000 and 4-2001, and dismissed the case. The citizen appealed.


OVERVIEW: The local laws declared that it would be unlawful to operate a business between the hours of 11:00 P.M. and 6:00 A.M. on land zoned for any business, industrial, or residential parking district that either abutted, or was within 100 feet of any land zoned for residential or apartment use. The citizen's property was located in a business district; he proposed to operate a business that would be unlawful in accordance with the laws. In his petition, the citizen alleged, among other things, that the laws were unconstitutional and otherwise invalid. The trial court denied the petition and dismissed the proceeding. The appellate court concluded that the exercise of such power must be supported, at the very least, by evidence showing that the atmosphere of the surrounding area would be adversely affected by the presence of such an overnight business. There was insufficient evidence to support the conclusion that the existence of a retail business that operated 24 hours a day in the vicinity of a residential area had any detrimental impact on the health, safety, welfare, or morals of the community.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, the petition was granted, and the local laws were declared invalid.

 

645 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. Kings County DA's Office


2000-06046


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


308 A.D.2d 278; 763 N.Y.S.2d 635; 2003 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 8675


September 14, 2001, Argued  
August 11, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected November 12, 2003.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed as modified.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, police officers, prosecutors, and the city, appealed from an order of the Supreme Court, Kings County (New York), which denied their motion to dismiss for failure to state a claim in plaintiff private citizen's action seeking recovery for negligent investigation, false arrest, false imprisonment, malicious prosecution, abuse of process, and, under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, for constitutional violations.


OVERVIEW: Probably because another man was using his identification, a warrant was issued for the citizen by South Carolina authorities, although the citizen had never been there and did not resemble the physical description in the warrant. Nonetheless, the citizen was mistakenly detained for nearly a month, and it was not until extradition proceedings were well underway that a New York prosecutor finally contacted South Carolina authorities about the citizen's claims and discovered that they were true. The appellate court held that judicial immunity protected the prosecutors from liability for their acts within the judicial process and that, in any case, as the arrest itself was proper under N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 570.34, there could be no liability for such torts as false arrest and imprisonment, as well as malicious prosecution and abuse of process. The purported tort of negligent investigation did not exist. Constitutional torts were another matter. The citizen might recover compensatory, but not punitive, damages from the city under a theory of willful failure to train or supervise employees so as to prepare them for situations such as the citizen's plight.


OUTCOME: The court modified the order to delete that portion of the denial of the motion that related to the complaint against the prosecutors in their individual capacities as well as all the claims that did not relate to constitutional violations. It also deleted the denial of the motion to dismiss the punitive damages claim. The remainder of the challenged order was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Negligence - What Constitutes - Negligent Investigation

1. In an action by plaintiff, who was justifiably arrested pursuant to a valid out-of-state fugitive warrant but allegedly detained for an unreasonably long time, plaintiff's claim alleging defendants' negligent failure to correctly investigate whether plaintiff was the person identified by the warrant should have been dismissed since New York courts do not recognize claims for negligent or malicious investigation. A plaintiff seeking damages for an injury resulting from a wrongful arrest and detention may not recover under broad general principles of negligence but must proceed by way of the traditional remedies of false arrest and imprisonment.

District and Prosecuting Attorneys - Absolute Immunity

2. In an action by plaintiff, who was justifiably arrested pursuant to a valid out-of-state fugitive warrant but allegedly detained for an unreasonably long time, claims alleging false arrest and malicious prosecution against the District Attorney and Assistant District Attorneys should have been dismissed since district attorneys are absolutely immune from civil liability for activities "intimately associated with the judicial phase of the criminal process." Insofar as plaintiff alleges that after his arrest the District Attorney and Assistant District Attorneys failed to obtain his fingerprints and other identifying evidence in order to determine whether he was the fugitive sought, these activities fall within the District Attorney and Assistant District Attorneys' "judicial" capacity.

False Imprisonment - Wrongful Detention

3. In an action by plaintiff, who was justifiably arrested pursuant to a valid out-of-state fugitive warrant but allegedly detained for an unreasonably long time, plaintiff's claim alleging false imprisonment should have been dismissed since plaintiff's arrest was privileged. The information in the warrant provided probable cause for plaintiff's arrest, and such finding of justification pursuant to CPL 570.34 constitutes a complete defense to a claim for false arrest and imprisonment.

Malicious Prosecution - Probable Cause

4. In an action by plaintiff, who was justifiably arrested pursuant to a valid out-of-state fugitive warrant but allegedly detained for an unreasonably long time, plaintiff's cause of action for malicious prosecution should have been dismissed. Plaintiff's claim that probable cause was lacking because he differed in height from the actual fugitive by seven inches is without merit. Further, while out-of-state authorities may have been misled and erred in failing to accurately determine the true identity of the person they named in the fugitive warrant, defendants did not err in determining that plaintiff was the person actually named, and probable cause existed based on the warrant itself without the need for the police to first make further inquiries.

Process - Abuse of Process

5. In an action by plaintiff, who was justifiably arrested pursuant to a valid out-of-state fugitive warrant but allegedly detained for an unreasonably long time, plaintiff's cause of action alleging abuse of process should have been dismissed since it is premised on negligence and a claim of negligence cannot support this intentional tort.

Civil Rights - Federal Civil Rights Claim

6. Plaintiff, who was justifiably arrested pursuant to a valid out-of-state fugitive warrant but allegedly detained for an unreasonably long time, adequately pleaded a cause of action under 42 USC § 1983 by alleging that defendants' actions deprived him of his rights secured by the 4th, 5th and 14th Amendments to the United States Constitution. The District Attorney's Office and the City acted with deliberate indifference to his constitutional rights in failing to adequately train, supervise and discipline their prosecutors, police officers and personnel in matters involving the identification, processing and extradition of persons arrested pursuant to fugitive warrants, and this was the proximate cause of his injuries.

Civil Rights - Federal Civil Rights Claim

7. In an action by plaintiff, who was justifiably arrested pursuant to a valid out-of-state fugitive warrant but allegedly detained for an unreasonably long time, the issue of whether the plaintiff's prolonged detention rose to the level of a constitutional deprivation is a question of fact not properly disposed of on a motion to dismiss.

Civil Rights - Federal Civil Rights Claim

8. Plaintiff, who was justifiably arrested pursuant to a valid out-of-state fugitive warrant but allegedly detained for an unreasonably long time, may maintain a claim for damages for deprivation of his rights pursuant to 42 USC § 1983 against the City of New York for the conduct of the District Attorney's office, insofar as the District Attorney acted as a New York City policymaker. Although the District Attorney's office is immune from liability under 42 USC § 1983, the City may be subject to liability pursuant thereto for failure to train and supervise its municipal employees. Plaintiff adequately alleged and made a threshold showing that constitutional harm was caused by a failure by the District Attorney's office to train assistant district attorneys and other personnel with regard to proper procedures for determining whether persons detained by them pursuant to fugitive warrants are in fact the persons sought by out-of-state authorities. Moreover, the failure of the District Attorney's office to train for this situation could constitute deliberate indifference sufficient to give rise to municipal liability.

Damages - Punitive Damages

9. Plaintiff's claim against various municipal defendants for punitive damages should have been dismissed since defendant City, as a political subdivision of the State of New York, must be presumed immune from punitive damages, absent a clear statement of a contrary legislative intent.

 

646 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


N.Y. Pub. Interest Research Group Straphangers Campaign, Inc. v. Metro. Transp. Auth.


1508, 1509


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


309 A.D.2d 127; 763 N.Y.S.2d 13; 2003 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 8336



July 15, 2003, Decided  
July 15, 2003, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Appeal denied by N.Y. Pub. Interest Research Group Straphangers Campaign, Inc. v. Metro. Transp. Auth., 100 N.Y.2d 513, 799 N.E.2d 617, 2003 N.Y. LEXIS 2540, 767 N.Y.S.2d 394 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Order and judgment entered 5/13/2003 reversed and petition dismissed; order and judgment entered 6/3/2003 affirmed as modified and petition dismissed; motion denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In consolidated appeals, respondent transit authorities (collectively, the MTA), sought review of judgments from the Supreme Court, New York County (New York). The trial courts, upon motions of petitioners, a public interest group and an automobile club, declared invalid the MTA's notice of public hearings on its budget and vacated a vote of the MTA Board to increase fares and tolls and to close various token booths.


OVERVIEW: The MTA announced it was ending the 2002 fiscal year with a positive cash balance but that it faced a combined budget deficit for the 2003 and 2004 fiscal years. After holding 10 public hearings, the MTA Board voted to increase fares and tolls. Reports by state and city commissioners were critical of that decision, and petitioners, relying in part on the reports, challenged the notices of public hearings and the increases. Both trial courts vacated the vote of the MTA Board and remanded. The court dismissed the petitions. Petitioners were essentially arguing that the MTA should have stated in its notices that its financial plan allocated the 2002 cost savings to both the 2003 and 2004 fiscal years. However, neither N.Y. Pub. Auth. Law § 1205(7) nor N.Y. Pub. Auth. Law § 1263(9) required such detailed financial disclosures in a notice of public hearing. Despite petitioners' claim that allocating all the 2002 cost savings to 2003 would do away with the need to increase fare and toll increase in 2003, the MTA was not required to devise its budgets on a single-year basis. Moreover, allocating the entire savings to 2003 would only forestall fare and toll increases for a year.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed petitioners' requests for relief.


HEADNOTES

Public Authorities -- Metropolitan Transportation Authority -- Notice of Public Hearings on Proposed Changes in Services or Fares

Proceedings challenging the decisions of respondent Metropolitan Transportation Authority (MTA) to raise bus, subway and commuter fares, to close 62 subway token booths and increase bridge and tunnel tolls on the ground that the MTA's notices of public hearings contained incomplete, inaccurate or misleading information are dismissed. The MTA's notices of public hearings complied in all respects with statutory requirements. The governing statute does not require that the notice of hearing provide any financial information regarding proposed fare increases or station closings, only that it include the "range of amounts of fare changes under consideration" and a "clear graphic illustration depicting the nature of any closing for such station" (Public Authorities Law § 1263 [9]; see also § 1205 [7]). Respondent's notices informed the public that the MTA was facing a multibillion dollar deficit over the 2003 and 2004 fiscal years, that various internal measures would reduce that deficit to under $1 billion, and that the proposed fare and toll increases and token booth closures were intended to close the remaining deficit. The statute does not require respondent to disclose that its financial plan called for the allocation of all of the 2002 available cash balances to both the 2003 and 2004 fiscal years. Furthermore, the record does not support the determinations of the IAS courts that the MTA's 2003 and 2004 deficit was "fictional" or that the MTA notices were otherwise false and misleading. The MTA's failure to specifically inform the public in the notices that its budgetary planning had allocated the 2002 cost-savings to 2003 and 2004, not just to 2003, did not render the notices false or misleading, especially in vew of respondent's statutory obligation to establish five-year financial plans (see Public Authorities Law § 1269-d).

Town of Southampton v. N.Y. State Pub. Empl. Rels. Bd.


92576


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


307 A.D.2d 428; 763 N.Y.S.2d 338; 2003 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 7732



July 3, 2003, Decided  
July 3, 2003, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Motion denied by  Town of Southampton v. N.Y. State Pub. Empl. Rels. Bd., 100 N.Y.2d 639, 801 N.E.2d 420, 2003 N.Y. LEXIS 3433, 769 N.Y.S.2d 199 (2003)
Affirmed by  Town of Southampton v. New York State Pub. Empl. Rels. Bd., 2 N.Y.3d 513, 813 N.E.2d 602, 2004 N.Y. LEXIS 1313, 780 N.Y.S.2d 522 (N.Y., June 3, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Determination confirmed; petition dismissed; respondents' application to enforce the determination granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employer filed an action to challenge a decision from respondent New York State Public Employment Relations Board (PERB), which affirmed an administrative law judge's determination that the employer had committed an improper employer practice against respondent association.


OVERVIEW: An arbitration award included a clause concerning the calculation of hour and daily rates of overtime pay. After a dispute arose about the calculation, a grievance was filed. The parties signed a memorandum of agreement that expressly continued only those provisions of the award that were not in dispute. Later, the association filed an improper practice charge with PERB. An administrative law judge determined that, despite the fact that the award had expired, the clause concerning holiday pay defined that aspect of the status quo. After the judgment was affirmed by PERB, the employer filed an appeal. In confirming the decision, the court determined that PERB had jurisdiction over the parties' dispute. Further, the decision of PERB was entitled to deference on appeal because it was a matter resting peculiarly within PERB's expertise. It was not a matter of statutory construction. PERB was merely deciding whether the holiday pay provision in the arbitration award defined the status quo after a certain date. Further, PERB did not err by treating the agreed-upon language of the award no differently than if it had been a legislative resolution.


OUTCOME: The determination by PERB was confirmed. The application to enforce the determination was granted.

Notre Dame Leasing, LLC v. Rosario


2001-08540


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


308 A.D.2d 164; 761 N.Y.S.2d 292; 2003 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 7421


May 13, 2002, Argued  
June 23, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Motion granted by Notre Dame Leasing, LLC v. Rosario, 1 N.Y.3d 552, 807 N.E.2d 882, 2003 N.Y. LEXIS 4068, 775 N.Y.S.2d 771 (2003)
Motion granted by Notre Dame Leasing, LLC v. Rosario, 1 N.Y.3d 585, 808 N.E.2d 350, 2004 N.Y. LEXIS 34, 776 N.Y.S.2d 215 (2004)
Motion granted by Notre Dame Leasing, LLC v. Rosario, 1 N.Y.3d 608, 808 N.E.2d 856, 2004 N.Y. LEXIS 141, 776 N.Y.S.2d 535 (N.Y., Feb. 12, 2004)
Affirmed by, Certified question answered by Notre Dame Leasing, LLC v. Rosario, 2 N.Y.3d 459, 812 N.E.2d 291, 2004 N.Y. LEXIS 1034, 779 N.Y.S.2d 801 (N.Y., May 11, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Order of the appellate term affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant tenants sought review of a judgment from the Appellate Term for the 2nd and 11th Judicial Districts (New York). The appellate term reversed an order from the trial court, which held that the tenants had made a prima facie showing that the Spiegel Law defense under N.Y. Soc. Serv. Law § 143-b applied in an eviction action commenced by respondent landlord.


OVERVIEW: The landlord commenced a summary proceeding to evict the tenants for nonpayment of rent. The tenants relied on § 143-b(5)(a), which provided that it was a valid defense in an eviction proceeding against a welfare recipient to show existing violations in the building code as a basis for nonpayment of rent. The trial court held, among other things, that the tenants could raise the Spiegel law defense. The appellate term reversed and denied the tenants' summary judgment motion. The court affirmed. In light of the statutory language and legislative history, welfare recipients could only raise the Spiegel Law defense where the appropriate public welfare officials had first exercised the authority to withhold direct rent payments to the landlord based upon the existence of building violations. A contrary holding giving welfare recipients the right to withhold payment of rent for violations that did not directly affect the habitability of the recipient's apartment would unconstitutionally impair the landlord's contractual right to receive payment. The underlying policy goals of § 143-b would best be effectuated by encouraging the wider use of the statute by the proper state officials.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the judgment.


HEADNOTES

Landlord and Tenant - Summary Proceedings - Defense of Code Violations Unavailable to Welfare Recipient Where Social Services Agency Continues to Pay Portion of Rent

 Social Services Law § 143-b, which authorizes "public welfare officials" to withhold rent payments to landlords on behalf of welfare recipients if the building in which a recipient lives has code violations, and further provides in subdivision (5) that it is "a valid defense" in any nonpayment proceeding against a welfare recipient "to show existing violations" related to dangerous or hazardous conditions in the building where the recipient resides as a basis for the nonpayment, can be raised as a defense by a welfare recipient only where the appropriate social services agency has first acted to withhold direct rent payments to the landlord based upon the existence of code violations in the recipient's building. Consequently, respondent tenants may not assert the statute as a defense to a nonpayment summary proceeding where the New York City Human Resources Administration, which pays a portion of their rent directly to petitioner landlord as their shelter grant, has taken no steps to withhold its share of the rent because of code violations. The statutory scheme manifests a clear legislative intent to confer the right to withhold rent on social services officials rather than individual welfare recipients. Since only a social services official is permitted under the statute to withhold rent from a landlord who may be providing substandard housing, the statutory defense should apply only in cases where the appropriate official has first exercised this right. Furthermore, it would be an impermissible impairment of the landlord's contractual right to receive payment to permit individual welfare recipients, rather than welfare officials, to withhold rent payments under the statute.

Kraham v. Mathews


91678


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


305 A.D.2d 746; 761 N.Y.S.2d 102; 2003 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 5223

The appeal was from summary judgment for the judges entered in Broome County Supreme Court (New York).

There was no procedural necessity for entertaining the declaratory judgment action, as judicial review was not unavailable due to a refusal by defendants to issue a final administrative determination. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 22, § 127.2, the appellate court was still unable to review the determinations, as the county neither joined the administrative judge who reviewed the awards nor included that judge's decisions in the record.


OUTCOME: The lower court decision was reversed.

Astor Gardens Health Care Ctr., Inc. v. Novello


92829


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


304 A.D.2d 961; 758 N.Y.S.2d 428; 2003 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 3826



April 10, 2003, Decided  
April 10, 2003, Entered



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant nursing home brought a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding against respondent health department, seeking to vacate audits conducted by the health department. The Supreme Court, Albany County (New York), found that the health department was not required to provide the nursing home with notice and that applicable regulations were not unconstitutional or contrary to due process rights. The nursing home appealed.


OVERVIEW: After the health department began auditing the nursing home's Medicaid reimbursement rates, the nursing home sold the facility. The audits continued, and communications regarding the process were directed to the buyer of the facility. From the audits, the nursing home became liable for overpayment of $ 1 million. The appellate court ruled that when the nursing home sold the facility, it ceased being a "facility." As the regulations required the health department to communicate with "the facility," it acted reasonably and according to its regulations by working with the buyer. The nursing home had notice of the audits, and its own actions or inactions resulted in its failure to receive further notice. The nursing home had the chance to make submissions before the on-site review was complete, but relinquished that right by failing to keep apprised of the progress of the audit. Medicaid reimbursement rates were provisional, not vested, and where no constitutionally protected rights existed, there was no entitlement to a hearing when there was a deprivation of such property. The nursing home was afforded all the process it was due.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

652 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


In re Jessica Marie Q.


2002-07761, 2002-07762, 2002-07764


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


303 A.D.2d 512; 757 N.Y.S.2d 304; 2003 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 2311


February 18, 2003, Argued  
March 10, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Appeal denied by, Motion dismissed by In re Jessica Marie Q. (Anonymous), 100 N.Y.2d 507, 795 N.E.2d 1244, 2003 N.Y. LEXIS 1740, 764 N.Y.S.2d 235 (N.Y., July 1, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner Westchester County, New York, Department of Social Services (DSS), filed actions, pursuant to N.Y. Soc. Serv. Law § 384-b, seeking orders terminating respondent parents' parental rights. The Family Court, Westchester County (New York), terminated the parents' rights, and transferred custody of their children to DSS for purposes of placing the children for adoption. The children's law guardian appealed.


OVERVIEW: The law guardian appealed the family court judgments terminating the parental rights to the state supreme court, arguing that N.Y. Soc. Serv. Law § 384-b(3)(i) deprived permanently neglected children of their rights to substantive and procedural due process under U.S. Const. amends. V and XIV because it did not require a trial court to consider the likelihood that a child would be adopted before the court issued orders terminating the child's parents' parental rights. The state supreme court transferred the case to the intermediate appellate court on the ground that direct appeal to the supreme court was not appropriate. The intermediate appellate court held that (1) N.Y. Soc. Serv. Law § 384-b(3)(i) was narrowly tailored to serve the compelling interest of protecting children, and it was constitutional; and (2) evidence which showed that parents did not complete a substance abuse rehabilitation program or a parenting class, had barely any contact with their children, and failed to plan for their children's future supported the family court's finding that terminating the parents' parental rights, and freeing their children for adoption, was in the children's best interests.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

Peckham Materials Corp. v. Westchester County


2001-09308


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


303 A.D.2d 511; 756 N.Y.S.2d 594; 2003 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 2335


November 21, 2002, Argued  
March 10, 2003, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellee corporation petitioned the Supreme Court, Westchester County (New York), to annul certain air quality provisions of appellee county's sanitary code. The trial court converted the hybrid proceeding and action solely to an action for a declaratory judgment and denied the county's motion to dismiss the complaint. The county appealed.


OVERVIEW: The corporation operated facilities which were charged emission fees under Westchester County, N.Y., Sanitary Code art. 13, § 873.1301 et seq.; art. 21, § 873.2109. The corporation claimed that the fees were an illegal tax, unconstitutional, and inconsistent with the New York Environmental Conservation Law. On appeal, the court found that the trial court erred in converting the hybrid proceeding and action solely to an action for a declaratory judgment and in denying those branches of the county's motion to dismiss the first and third through ninth causes of action. The corporation's claims set forth in the first and third through ninth causes of action were clearly time-barred. Therefore, the county's motion to dismiss the proceeding as time-barred should have been granted with respect to all the causes of action except the second cause of action, the alleged failure to maintain the records required pursuant to N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 606. The trial court properly denied the county's motion insofar as it sought dismissal of the second cause of action.


OUTCOME: The order was modified by deleting the provision thereof converting the hybrid proceeding and action solely to an action for a declaratory judgment, by granting the motion to dismiss the first and the third through the ninth causes of action, by affirming the denial of the motion to dismiss as to the second cause of action, and, as so modified, the order was affirmed.

Hammer v. Am. Kennel Club


2095-2096


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


304 A.D.2d 74; 758 N.Y.S.2d 276; 2003 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 1805



February 27, 2003, Decided  
February 27, 2003, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Motion granted by Hammer v. Am. Kennel Club, 2003 N.Y. LEXIS 3337 (N.Y., Oct. 23, 2003)
Affirmed by Hammer v. Am. Kennel Club, 1 N.Y.3d 294, 803 N.E.2d 766, 2003 N.Y. LEXIS 4163, 771 N.Y.S.2d 493 (N.Y., Dec. 23, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed; appeal from the order dated 2/26/2002 dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff dog owner appealed from a judgment of the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), that granted the motions of defendants, various competitive dog associations, to dismiss the complaint. The associations moved to dismiss the complaint on the grounds that the dog owner did not have the legal capacity to sue, and that he had failed to state a cause of action pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 3211(a)(3), (7).


OVERVIEW: Specifically, the dog owner's amended complaint sought a declaratory judgment that the complained-of standard (1) unlawfully discriminated against the dog owner by effectively precluding him from entering his dog in breed competitions, (2) was arbitrary and capricious, (3) violated N.Y. Agric. & Mkts. Law § 353, and (4) was null and void as in derogation of law. He further sought an injunction prohibiting defendants from applying, enforcing, or utilizing the standard. The appellate court found that the claim was made that the associations adopted a standard that promoted, among the owners of Brittany Spaniels raised for competition, a practice that allegedly amounted to the unjustifiable, and therefore illegal, mutilation of the dogs. The appellate court agreed with the associations' contention that the dog owner lacked the standing to obtain any of the civil remedies he sought for the alleged violation of § 353. Because the owner had no individual right to seek civil enforcement of § 353, those portions of his complaint that sought a declaration that the associations' tail standard violated the statute were null and void.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Courts - Justiciable Questions - Challenge to Tail Standard for Dog Shows - Animal Cruelty

1. Plaintiff's action to preclude defendant kennel clubs from enforcing a tail standard for a certain dog breed that, for judging purposes in sponsored competitions, "severely" penalizes a dog with a tail "substantially more than four inches," on the ground that the standard promotes animal cruelty in violation of Agriculture and Markets Law § 353, and effectively excludes his dog, which has an undocked 10-inch long tail, from meaningfully competing in defendants' dog shows, presents a justiciable controversy. While generally the internal decision making and rule adoption of private organizations, involving the conduct of their members and their activities, are outside the realm in which courts exercise their authority, this general rule of noninterference in an organization's self-governance gives way upon a showing that its adopted rules violate state law.

Animals - Animal Rights - Dog Tail Docking for Dog Shows - No Private Right of Action to Enforce Animal Cruelty Laws

2. Plaintiff's action to preclude defendant kennel clubs from enforcing a tail standard for a certain dog breed that, for judging purposes in sponsored competitions, "severely" penalizes a dog with a tail "substantially more than four inches," on the ground that the standard promotes animal cruelty in violation of Agriculture and Markets Law § 353, and effectively excludes his dog, which has an undocked 10-inch long tail, from meaningfully competing in defendants' dog shows, is dismissed for failure to state a cause of action. Even if dog tail docking constitutes an unjustified procedure that falls within the statutory animal cruelty prohibition, plaintiff lacks standing to obtain any civil remedy. Agriculture and Markets Law § 353 is a criminal statute that can only be enforced by law enforcement agencies, and not private individuals. Moreover, civil remedies, such as injunctive relief, are not generally available to private individuals to prevent violations of penal statutes.

Animals - Animal Rights - Challenge to Tail Standard for Dog Shows - Discrimination

3. Plaintiff's allegation that defendant kennel clubs' promulgation of standards for canine tail length constitutes illegal discrimination, lacks merit. Dog tail length is not a consideration protected by state or federal antidiscrimination laws, and neither plaintiff nor his dog is a member of a protected class.

Animals - Animal Rights - Challenge to Tail Standard for Dog Shows

4. Defendant kennel clubs' promulgation of standards for canine tail length is not actionable as arbitrary and capricious conduct, since defendants do not qualify as governmental agencies answerable for the evenhandedness of their procedures.

 

655 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


People v. Mannix


263


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


302 A.D.2d 297; 756 N.Y.S.2d 33; 2003 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 1719



February 25, 2003, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Motion granted by People v. Mannix, 2003 N.Y. LEXIS 1375 (N.Y., June 5, 2003)
Appeal denied by People v. Mannix, 100 N.Y.2d 622, 799 N.E.2d 629, 2003 N.Y. LEXIS 3816, 767 N.Y.S.2d 406 (2003)
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Mannix v. Phillips, 2005 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 9857 (S.D.N.Y., May 25, 2005)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted in the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), of second degree murder and third degree criminal possession of a weapon. He appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court held "depraved indifference" murder, under N.Y. Penal Law § 125.25(2), was not unconstitutionally vague as it was separate, facially and as interpreted, from second-degree manslaughter, and defendant's act violating two statutes could be prosecuted under either. When defendant deliberately fired through a door into a small, enclosed space containing the victim and a bystander, and said "Good," when told he had hit someone, his depraved indifference murder conviction was sufficiently supported. The jury's rejection of lesser-included second-degree manslaughter made an instruction on the more remote criminally negligent homicide unnecessary. Refusing to require a prosecution witness, on cross-examination, to state names of bar patrons where the shooting occurred was proper because collateral to defendant's defense, and defendant could impeach the witness. The People's impeachment of their own witness was proper, under N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 60.35(1), as the witness's unfavorable testimony was on direct. A nontestifying declarant's statement was properly admitted to complete a narrative and did not prejudice defendant.


OUTCOME: Defendant's convictions were affirmed.

 

656 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


People v. Parker


KAD 00-02506


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FOURTH DEPARTMENT


304 A.D.2d 146; 755 N.Y.S.2d 521; 2003 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 952



February 7, 2003, Decided  
February 7, 2003, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1]
Appeal denied by People v. Parker, 100 N.Y.2d 585, 796 N.E.2d 488, 2003 N.Y. LEXIS 3156, 764 N.Y.S.2d 396 (2003)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Parker v. Phillips, 2010 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 55844 (W.D.N.Y., June 8, 2010)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Erie County Court (New York) that convicted defendant of murder in the first degree, attempted murder in the first degree, aggravated assault on a police officer, criminal possession of a weapon in the second degree, and criminal possession of a weapon, in violation of N.Y. Penal Law §§ 125.27(1)(a)(i), 110.00, 120.11, former § 265.03(2), and 265.02.


OVERVIEW: In reviewing defendant's convictions, the appellate court found that defendant was convicted and sentenced before the court of appeals issued its decision in Hynes. However, defendant was not affected by the constitutional infirmity of the statutory provisions at issue in Hynes and Harris. Defendant risked death, but suffered no detriment as a result of that risk. Consequently, he could not now raise the issue as to what might have occurred had the jury recommended death. Further, upon examining the individual statements of a prospective juror, in context and as a whole, the appellate court concluded that she gave an unequivocal assurance of impartiality. Additionally, while the appellate court agreed with defendant that two prospective jurors initially seemed confused about the burdens of proof, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's challenges for cause with respect to those prospective jurors. Finally, in denying defendant's Batson challenges, the court thereby implicitly determined that the race-neutral explanations given by the prosecutor for exercising peremptory challenges with respect to those prospective jurors were not pretextual.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed with the exception of a minor technical modification to defendant's sentence.


HEADNOTES

Crimes - Murder - Capital Murder - Constitutional Challenges to Death Penalty Statutes 

1. In defendant's capital murder prosecution for killing a police officer, defendant's general constitutional challenges to New York's death penalty statutes (Penal Law § 125.27; CPL 400.27) need not be addressed inasmuch as the jury sentenced defendant to life imprisonment without parole. Courts should not address a constitutional issue if the case may be disposed of in another way.

Crimes - Murder - Capital Murder

2. Defendant's specific constitutional challenge to CPL 270.20 (1) (f) for permitting a "death-qualified" jury to determine a capital defendant's guilt or innocence lacks merit. There is no constitutional prohibition against "death-qualifying" juries in capital cases.

Crimes - Murder - Capital Murder

3. Defendant's capital murder prosecution was not affected by the constitutional infirmity of certain plea bargain provisions of the death penalty statutes (CPL 220.10 [5] [e]; 220.30 [3] [b] [vii]), which were declared unconstitutional after defendant was convicted and sentenced (see Matter of Hynes v Tomei, 92 NY2d 613, 706 N.E.2d 1201, 684 N.Y.S.2d 177, cert denied 527 US 1015, 144 L. Ed. 2d 254, 119 S. Ct. 2359). Here, defendant risked death, but suffered no detriment as a result of that risk. The sentence of life imprisonment without parole may also be imposed upon a defendant who pleads guilty. Consequently, the imposition of that sentence has not unconstitutionally penalized the exercise of defendant's right to trial.

Crimes - Jurors - Challenge to Jury - Capital Murder

4. Defendant's conviction of murder in the first degree for killing a police officer (Penal Law § 125.27), for which he received a sentence of life imprisonment without parole, is not subject to reversal because of alleged defects in the jury selection process. Defendant failed to establish an unconstitutional underrepresentation of African-Americans and young people from the lists from which the jury panel was drawn. In addition, the trial court properly denied defendant's Batson challenges. The court did not abuse its discretion in determining that the prosecutor presented race-neutral explanations for exercising the peremptory challenges with respect to the prospective jurors at issue. Furthermore, the trial court properly denied several of defendant's challenges of prospective jurors for cause pursuant to CPL 270.20 (1). Defendant was not "forced" to accept a certain prospective juror when he opted to use his last peremptory challenge to exclude another prospective juror. The court properly granted the People's challenge for cause with respect to four prospective jurors who stated that they would have difficulty taking an active role in imposing the death penalty, and with respect to a prospective juror who failed to disclose a prior conviction of driving while intoxicated and who further stated that she believed that law enforcement officers planted illegal drugs in her vehicle. The court also properly determined that a sworn juror's expressed conscientious opinion against the death penalty after being sworn rendered her grossly unqualified (CPL 270.35 [1]), thereby warranting her discharge for cause.

Crimes - Identification of Defendant - Capital Murder - Harmless Error

5. In defendant's capital murder prosecution for killing a police officer (Penal Law § 125.27), any error in the admission of the identification testimony of a police officer who was also shot during the incident is harmless beyond a reasonable doubt. There is overwhelming evidence of defendant's guilt, including the identification testimony of two eyewitnesses who personally knew defendant, and the testimony of a witness who saw defendant running down the street seconds after the witness had heard gunshots. Moreover, although the court erred in allowing the People to use classic front and side profile mugshots of defendant in a photographic array in connection with the testimony of the officer, the error is likewise harmless beyond a reasonable doubt in light of the overwhelming evidence of defendant's guilt. Similarly, any error in the admission of "resemblance testimony" from a witness for the People is also harmless beyond a reasonable doubt in view of the overwhelming evidence of defendant's guilt.

Crimes - Murder

6. Defendant's conviction of murder in the first degree and attempted murder in the first degree is supported by legally sufficient evidence and the verdict is not against the weight of the evidence. Defendant's intent may be inferred from his actions, as described in the testimony of the People's witnesses.

Crimes - Appeal - Preservation of Issue for Review

7. Defendant's contention that the trial court erred in failing to inform him of the contents of two jury notes is not preserved for appellate review where defense counsel failed to object at a time when the court could have corrected the alleged error.

Crimes - Evidence

8. Defendant's contention that the admission of testimony concerning DNA population statistics was without proper foundation and constituted reversible error is rejected. Defendant's challenges go not to the admissibility but to the weight of the evidence, which should be left to the trier of fact.

Crimes - Instructions

9. In a capital murder prosecution for the murder of a police officer, the court did not err in denying defense counsel's request to recharge the jury with respect to the difference between depraved indifference murder and murder in the first degree. The court properly explained the difference between the requisite states of mind for those crimes, and the charge as a whole conveyed the proper standard to the jury.

Crimes - Fair Trial - Capital Murder - Admission of Prior Plea Transcript

10. In defendant's capital murder prosecution for killing a police officer (Penal Law § 125.27) and wounding another, the admission of the plea transcript in a prior proceeding did not deprive defendant of a fair trial. The People's theory for defendant's motive in shooting at the officers was that defendant was awaiting sentencing on the crimes covered by his guilty plea and wanted to avoid being apprehended for possessing a loaded weapon. The transcript of the prior plea proceeding, which the prosecutor agreed should exclude any mention of the crimes to which defendant pleaded guilty, established that the court had informed defendant that it would not be bound by its sentencing commitment if defendant were arrested between the time of his plea and sentencing. Sentencing in that case was scheduled for two weeks after the shooting herein occurred. Thus, the plea transcript was admissible on the issue of defendant's motive for shooting at the officers, and the court minimized any prejudice to defendant by instructing the jury that the plea transcript was to be considered only with respect to that issue.

Kwang L. (Anonymous) v. Martin


2001-02263


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Supreme Court, Queens County, New York, granted a petition filed by respondent doctor to authorize the assisted outpatient treatment of appellant patient for a period of 180 days. The patient appealed.


OVERVIEW: The patient challenged the judgment entered. The appeals court concluded that N.Y. Mental Hyg. Law § 9.60 was constitutional, because the brief detention of a noncompliant assisted outpatient for a psychiatric evaluation did not constitute a substantial deprivation of liberty, and the additional safeguard of a judicial hearing would not significantly reduce the possibility of an erroneous removal decision. Moreover, the government had a strong interest in avoiding time-consuming judicial hearings, which required mental health professionals to defend their clinical decisions and divert scarce resources from the diagnosis and treatment of the mentally ill. Similarly, N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 330.20(14) gave criminal defendants, who were found not guilty by reason of mental disease or defect and released subject to an order of conditions, notice and an opportunity to be heard before their recommitment to a secure psychiatric facility. Furthermore, N.Y. Mental Hyg. Law § 9.60(n) did not require a finding that there was probable cause to believe that an assisted outpatient who failed to comply with an assisted outpatient treatment order was dangerous to himself or others.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Bazin v. Novello


90906


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner doctor filed an action against respondent New York State Commissioner of Health and others, pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, seeking judicial review of a decision by the New York State Administrative Review Board for Professional Medical Conduct which found that the doctor violated the terms of probation and engaged in professional misconduct, revoked the doctor's license to practice medicine, and imposed a $ 5,000 fine.

People v. Williamson


10569, 13608


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT

Writ of habeas corpus denied, Certificate of appealability denied Williamson v. Smith, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 13964 (N.D.N.Y, Feb. 24, 2009)
Post-conviction relief denied at People v. Williamson, 72 A.D.3d 1339, 900 N.Y.S.2d 165, 2010 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 3168 (N.Y. App. Div. 3d Dep't, 2010)
Related proceeding at Matter of Williamson v. Fischer, 72 A.D.3d 1366, 898 N.Y.S.2d 736, 2010 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 3180 (N.Y. App. Div. 3d Dep't, 2010)

DISPOSITION: Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant pled guilty in the County Court of Rensselaer County (New York) to first degree murder. He appealed his conviction and the trial court's denial, without a hearing, of his motion to vacate the judgment of conviction.


OVERVIEW: An appellate decision issued after defendant's plea held a defendant could not plead guilty to first degree murder when a notice of intent to seek the death penalty was pending. Before defendant pled guilty, the notice of intent to seek the death penalty was orally withdrawn, but not in writing. The appellate court held defendant's plea was valid if otherwise knowingly, voluntarily, and intelligently made. Penal Law § 125.27(1)(a)(ix), with first degree murder after a previous conviction of murder equivalent to N.Y. Penal Law §§ 125.25 or 125.27, in another state. The previous conviction was of second degree murder. If it was not a predicate conviction under N.Y. Penal Law § 125.27(1)(a)(ix), and the indictment was not jurisdictionally defective, as it informed defendant he was charged with first degree murder due to a previous murder conviction and informed him of the prior conviction being relied on. Defendant waived any defect in the indictment when he pled guilty.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and the denial of his motion to vacate the conviction were affirmed.

 

660 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


N.Y. City Health & Hosps. Corp. v. Council of N.Y.


2237


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


303 A.D.2d 69; 752 N.Y.S.2d 665; 2003 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 244



January 14, 2003, Decided  
January 14, 2003, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal withdrawn by N.Y. City Health & Hosps. Corp. v. Council of N.Y., 1 N.Y.3d 539, 2003 N.Y. LEXIS 4785 (2003)
Appeal withdrawn by N.Y. City Health & Hosps. Corp. v. Council of City of N.Y., 1 N.Y.3d 539, 2003 N.Y. LEXIS 4786 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed; City Council's cross motion denied; plaintiff's motion for summary judgment and other relief granted; local law declared invalid.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant health and hospitals corporation sued respondent city council in the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), seeking to declare a local law passed by the city council invalid. Both parties moved for summary judgment, the trial court granted the city council's summary judgment motion, and the corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: The corporation wanted to save money by using private security guards in its facilities, rather than licensed peace officers, as the local law required. The appellate court held the legislature impliedly and expressly evinced an intent to preempt the subject matter of the local law. The New York City Health and Hospitals Corporation Act was a comprehensive and detailed regulatory scheme to govern the city's health care system. Under § 7405 of the Act, its provisions were controlling over any inconsistent laws, and § 7385(11), (12) of the Act gave the New York City Health and Hospitals Corporation (HHC) autonomy to fix the guards' qualifications. The local law impermissibly prohibited what would have been permissible under state law or, at a minimum, restricted the HHC's rights under state law. The local law was not one of general applicability because it only applied to the HHC, and not to other hospitals in the city, so it did not fit in the "generally applicable" exception to the preemption rule. The local law did not have only a tangential or incidental impact because it affected only security guards who were not health care personnel.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed, and the corporation's summary judgment motion was granted to the extent of declaring the local law invalid.


HEADNOTES

Local Laws - Preemption by State - Local Law Requiring New York City Health and Hospitals Corporation to Utilize "Peace Officers" as Security Guards

A local law of the City of New York, which mandates that plaintiff New York City Health and Hospitals Corporation (HHC) utilize "peace officers" appointed pursuant to CPL 2.10 (40) as security guards (Administrative Code of City of NY § 17-182), is invalid as an unconstitutional interference with HHC's right, as established by the New York City Health and Hospitals Corporation Act (McKinney's Uncons Laws of NY § 7381 [L 1969, ch 1016, § 1, as amended]), to operate autonomously. The State has both impliedly and expressly evinced an intent to preempt the entire field with regard to the City's hospital system (see Uncons Laws § 7405 [Health and Hospitals Corporation Act § 24]), thereby precluding any further local regulation, regardless of whether the local regulation bears a reasonable and substantial relationship to the legitimate purpose of furthering public safety. Even a rational exercise of police power that contravenes controlling state law or is preempted thereby is invalid. The Health and Hospitals Corporation Act gives HHC complete autonomy to fix the security guards' qualifications and replace them (see Uncons Laws § 7385 [11], [12] [Health and Hospitals Corporation Act § 5 (11), (12)]). The requirement that security personnel qualify as peace officers intrudes on HHC's managerial flexibility. Moreover, the local law does not qualify as an exception to the preemption rule for "generally applicable" local laws that only "incidentally infringe" upon the powers of state created entities. The local law is not a law of general applicability, nor can it be said that it has only a tangential or incidental impact because it affects only security guards who are not health care personnel.

 

661 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Mitchell v. Fischer


2001-08649


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


300 A.D.2d 490; 752 N.Y.S.2d 97; 2002 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 12278


November 19, 2002, Submitted  
December 16, 2002, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, a prisoner, filed a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 to review a determination of respondent, which confirmed a determination of a hearing officer that found the prisoner guilty of violating prison disciplinary rules and imposed a penalty.


OVERVIEW: Contrary to the prisoner's contention, the appellate court held there was substantial evidence in the record as a whole, pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 7803(4), to support the determination finding him guilty of violating N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 7, § 270.2(B)(19)(iv) and N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 7, § 270.2(B)(8)(i). The prisoner challenged the constitutionality of N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 7, § 270.2(B)(8)(i), which mandated that an inmate could not physically or verbally obstruct or interfere with an employee at any time, on vagueness grounds. However, an inmate rule was not unconstitutionally vague, if it informed a reasonable person of the nature of the offense prohibited and what was required of him or her. The appellate court held that a reasonable man would have concluded that an inmate's action of throwing a liquid substance on a corrections officer, even if it was only faucet water, would violate N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 7, § 270.2(B)(8)(i), as it would likely have physically interfered with a corrections officer's duties. This rule informed the prisoner of the nature of the offense that was prohibited and what was required of him.


OUTCOME: The determination was confirmed, and the petition was dismissed on the merits, without costs or disbursements.

 

662 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Town of Johnsburg v. Town of Johnsburg Zoning Bd. of Appeals


92045


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


299 A.D.2d 796; 751 N.Y.S.2d 85; 2002 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 11449



November 27, 2002, Decided  
November 27, 2002, Entered



DISPOSITION: Judgment entered M/23/2000 affirmed without costs; amended judgment entered 3/15/2002 reversed without costs; petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In two proceedings, the Supreme Court, Warren County (New York), granted petitioner corporation's applications, pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, to annul determinations of respondent zoning board of appeals, regarding whether the corporation's non-conforming use had been abandoned. The town appealed, and the corporation cross-appealed. The proceedings were consolidated on appeal.


OVERVIEW: As to the first proceeding, the town's zoning officer informed the corporation's predecessor by letter that its batch plant was a permitted use. The zoning ordinance was amended and the property was rezoned residential, with a provision that if a preexisting nonconforming use was abandoned for a year, subsequent uses had to comply with the ordinance. The town alleged the corporation ceased operations for one year. The appellate court held that as the town did not rescind the zoning officer's letter, the corporation was in compliance with the ordinance as it existed when the letter was written. While the corporation's use was legally created, there was no support in the ordinance for the zoning board of appeals' ruling that any abandonment of the nonconforming use had to occur during a certain 12-month period. As to the second proceeding, the trial court erroneously substituted its judgment for that of the zoning board of appeals' finding activities at the site were insufficient to show continued operation of the batch plant for a different 12-month period. Substantial evidence supported the board's finding.


OUTCOME: As to the first proceeding, the trial court's judgment was affirmed. As to the second proceeding, the trial court's judgment was reversed.

 

663 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Troy Police Benevolent & Protective Ass'n v. City of Troy


91753


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


299 A.D.2d 710; 750 N.Y.S.2d 352; 2002 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10746



November 14, 2002, Decided  
November 14, 2002, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended March 4, 2003. As Amended March 7, 2003.
Appeal denied by Troy Police Benevolent & Protective Ass'n v. City of Troy, 2003 N.Y. LEXIS 1693 (N.Y., June 26, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant police officers moved for summary judgment, arguing that N.Y. Pub. Off. Law §§ 3(12), 30(6), precluded respondent city from enacting a local code imposing a requirement that public officers employed by the city were to live within the city limits. The city cross-moved for summary judgment dismissing the complaint. The Supreme Court, Rensselaer County, New York, granted the city's cross-motion. The officers appealed.


OVERVIEW: At the time of one police officer's reappointment, he lived in an apartment in the city. The officer purchased a house outside the city limits with the intention of living there. N.Y. Pub. Off. Law §§ 3(12), 30(6) required police officers to reside within the city limits. The city adopted Troy, N.Y., Code § 24-4 to enforce the requirement. The officer was advised that the failure to abide by the requirement could result in his dismissal. The officers argued that because police officers were public officers, N.Y. Pub. Off. Law §§ 3(12), 30(6) exempted them from being compelled to reside within the city limits despite the authority under N.Y. Pub. Off. Law § 30(4)(3). The appellate court held that N.Y. Pub. Off. Law § 30(4)(3) regulated the residency of police officers, while N.Y. Pub. Off. Law §§ 3(12), 30(6) regulated generally the class of all other public officers. There was no conflict among N.Y. Pub. Off. Law §§ 3(12), 30(6), and § 30(4)(3). The enactment of Troy, N.Y., Code § 24-4 was not inconsistent with N.Y. Pub. Off. Law §§ 3(12), 30(6). The city was not precluded from enacting N.Y. Pub. Off. Law §§ 3(12), 30(6) to impose the residency requirement on its police officers.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

 

664 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Clements v. Vill. of Morristown


89756


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


298 A.D.2d 777; 750 N.Y.S.2d 137; 2002 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10343



October 31, 2002, Decided  
October 31, 2002, Entered



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Supreme Court, St. Lawrence County (New York), dismissed an application by petitioners, property owners, in a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, to review a determination of respondents, a town and others, denying the property owners' request for a variance. The property owners appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The property owners' only challenge to the determination denying their application for a variance permitting the construction of a six-foot-high privacy fence along their property sideline was that the operative provision of the city land use code, which provided that no property line fence, wall, or other divider could be constructed of a material or to a height that would interfere with the view or useful enjoyment of an adjoining property, was unconstitutionally vague. The appellate court held that in order to withstand a due process challenge, it sufficed that the language of an ordinance provided a reasonable degree of certainty so that individuals of ordinary intelligence were not forced to guess as to its meaning. The appellate court held that the provision at issue satisfied that test. The tall solid wood fence constructed by the property owners could be reasonably expected to, and in fact did, interfere with the adjoining neighbor's view of a river, thereby diminishing the value and interfering with the useful enjoyment of the adjoining property. Under the circumstances, the ordinance could be reasonably viewed as prohibiting the property owners' actions.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed, without costs.

 

665 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Moerdler v. Tax Appeals Tribunal


90085


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


298 A.D.2d 778; 750 N.Y.S.2d 329; 2002 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10356



October 31, 2002, Decided  
October 31, 2002, Entered



DISPOSITION: Determination confirmed without costs; petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayer paid sales tax pursuant to N.Y. Tax. Law § 1111(i)(A) on the total sum due under a 36-month lease for an automobile. After the vehicle was stolen and the lease was terminated prematurely, the New York Division of Taxation denied the taxpayer's claim for a refund. Respondent Tax Appeals Tribunal (New York) sustained the disallowance of the refund claim. The taxpayer sought review in a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding.


OVERVIEW: The Division of Taxation had found that there was no provision in New York's Tax Law allowing a refund of sales tax paid on a vehicle lease that was prematurely terminated. The appellate court held that the Tribunal's decision was not arbitrary or capricious. N.Y. Tax Law §§ 1101(b), 1105(a) required the collection of sales tax on the transaction since it involved a transfer of possession of tangible personal property for consideration, and the payment up front of the tax for the entire term of the lease was in accordance with N.Y. Tax Law § 1111(i)(A). Finally, N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 20, § 527.15(e) specifically provided that no refund or credit was allowed based upon the fact that receipts were not actually paid as in the case of early termination of a lease, since, under N.Y. Tax Law § 1111(i), such receipts were deemed to have been paid. Thus, a refund was not allowed. The taxpayer's reliance on N.Y. Tax Law § 1132(e) and regulations promulgated under it was misplaced, as § 1132(e) did not deal with leases or their early termination. Nor was the sales tax erroneously, illegally, or unconstitutionally collected or paid for purposes of N.Y. Tax Law § 1139(a).


OUTCOME: The appellate court confirmed the determination, without costs, and dismissed the petition.

A.R.E.B.A. Casriel, Inc. v. Novello


1730


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


298 A.D.2d 134; 748 N.Y.S.2d 547; 2002 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 9256



October 3, 2002, Decided  
October 3, 2002, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal denied by A.R.E.B.A. Casriel, Inc. v. Novello, 2003 N.Y. LEXIS 1472 (N.Y., June 12, 2003)
Motion granted by A.R.E.B.A. Casriel, Inc. v. Novello, 2003 N.Y. LEXIS 1476 (N.Y., June 12, 2003)


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an original proceeding transferred from the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), petitioner treatment provider sought review of respondent health commissioner's determination directing the provider to make restitution for Medicaid overpayments.


OVERVIEW: The provider, in violation of applicable regulations, sought and received Medicaid payments for inpatient alcoholism rehabilitation treatment rendered in beds not certified for such treatment. The provider was liable for reimbursement of any overpayment, under N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 18, § 518.3, and, under N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 18, § 518.1(c), an overpayment included any amount not authorized to be paid under the medical assistance program. Payments to the provider were only authorized when it was in compliance with all applicable statutes, rules and regulations, under N.Y. Soc. Serv. Law § 365-1(2)(n) and N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 18, § 504.3. It was irrelevant whether the provider competently administered the services. The commissioner did not have to consider the enumerated factors in N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 18, § 515.4(b), when directing repayment, as reimbursement was not a sanction or penalty, but a remedy in the nature of recoupment.


OUTCOME: The commissioner's determination was confirmed.

Latham v. N.Y. State Dep't of Corr. Servs.


90380


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


296 A.D.2d 675; 745 N.Y.S.2d 136; 2002 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 7354



July 11, 2002, Decided  
July 11, 2002, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal dismissed by, Motion dismissed by Latham v. N.Y. State Dep't of Corr. Servs., 99 N.Y.2d 531, 782 N.E.2d 568, 2002 N.Y. LEXIS 3481, 752 N.Y.S.2d 590 (2002)
Appeal denied by Latham v. N.Y. State Dep't of Corr. Servs., 99 N.Y.2d 508, 787 N.E.2d 1164, 2003 N.Y. LEXIS 204, 757 N.Y.S.2d 818 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate appealed from a judgment of the Supreme Court, Albany County, New York, which dismissed the inmate's application to review a determination of respondent department of correctional services computing the inmate's conditional release and maximum sentence expiration dates.


OVERVIEW: In 1991, the inmate was convicted of attempted murder and was sentenced to an indeterminate prison term of 7 1/2 to 22 1/2 years. Shortly thereafter, the victim died of her injuries, and the inmate was prosecuted for murder in the second degree under the delayed death exception to New York's statutory double jeopardy prohibition. The inmate was convicted after a jury trial of manslaughter, and in 1995, was sentenced to a concurrent indeterminate prison term of 8 1/3 to 25 years. The inmate argued that his conditional release and maximum expiration dates should have reflected credit for the time he served between 1991 and 1995. The appellate court held that the 1995 sentence was controlling. Thus, the department of corrections correctly credited the inmate's time served from 1991 to 1995 against the minimum period of the 1995 sentence to arrive at his parole eligibility date and properly refused to credit that time against the maximum 25-year term of that sentence. As N.Y. Penal Law § 70.30(3) did not allow the time served on the inmate's previously imposed 1991 sentence to be credited against the maximum term of his 1995 sentence, there was no error in the computation.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was affirmed.

OVERVIEW: A Delaware corporation that did business in New York State decided to expand into foreign markets and decided that its foreign businesses should be organized under foreign laws and held by viable corporate subsidiaries created for that purpose. The appellate court held that N.Y. Tax Law § 208(9)(b)(6) was not void for vagueness and there was no valid basis for disturbing the Tribunal's judgment.

Hason v. Dep't of Health


88460


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


295 A.D.2d 818; 744 N.Y.S.2d 86; 2002 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 6789



June 27, 2002, Decided  
June 27, 2002, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Related proceeding at Hason v. Office of Prof'l Med. Conduct, 2004 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 8202 (S.D.N.Y., Apr. 19, 2004)



DISPOSITION: Determination modified in part and confirmed in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a mandamus proceeding pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, petitioner doctor sought review a determination of the administrative review board which suspended the doctor's license to practice medicine in New York.


OVERVIEW: The doctor was licensed to practice medicine in New York in 1993. In 1995, he applied for a license to practice medicine in California, an application which was ultimately denied. The California board considered a 1996 psychiatric examination of the doctor, and, following an evidentiary hearing, found that his ability to practice medicine was impaired because he suffered from mental illness. The doctor was charged with professional misconduct based upon the California license refusal, alleging that the conduct underlying it would, if committed in New York, constitute professional misconduct. The hearing committee sustained the charge, and revoked the doctor's license to practice medicine. The administrative review board conducted a referral hearing, and correctly gave collateral estoppel effect to the California decision. The appellate court found that neither the fact that the California proceeding involved a license denial as compared to the suspension of a license, nor the fact that the doctor bore the burden of proof in the California proceeding, but not in the New York proceeding, precluded according collateral estoppel effect to the California determination.


OUTCOME: The judgment was modified to annul that portion that imposed a penalty, and the matter was remitted to the administrative review board for imposition of a penalty. As modified, the judgment was affirmed.

Campaign for Fiscal Equity v. State


5330


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


295 A.D.2d 1; 744 N.Y.S.2d 130; 2002 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 7252



June 25, 2002, Decided  
June 25, 2002, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Motion granted by Campaign for Fiscal Equity, Inc. v. State, 2003 N.Y. LEXIS 228 (N.Y., Feb. 25, 2003)
Motion granted by Campaign for Fiscal Equity, Inc. v. State, 2003 N.Y. LEXIS 264 (N.Y., Mar. 27, 2003)
Motion granted by Campaign for Fiscal Equity, Inc. v. State, 2003 N.Y. LEXIS 268 (N.Y., Mar. 27, 2003)
Motion granted by Campaign for Fiscal Equity, Inc. v. State, 2003 N.Y. LEXIS 276 (N.Y., Mar. 27, 2003)
Motion granted by Campaign for Fiscal Equity, Inc. v. State, 2003 N.Y. LEXIS 277 (N.Y., Mar. 27, 2003)
Motion granted by Campaign for Fiscal Equity, Inc. v. State, 2003 N.Y. LEXIS 289 (N.Y., Mar. 27, 2003)
Motion granted by Campaign for Fiscal Equity, Inc. v. State, 2003 N.Y. LEXIS 282 (N.Y., Mar. 27, 2003)
Motion granted by Campaign for Fiscal Equity, Inc. v. State, 2003 N.Y. LEXIS 364 (N.Y., Apr. 3, 2003)
Motion granted by Campaign for Fiscal Equity, Inc. v. State, 2003 N.Y. LEXIS 375 (N.Y., Apr. 3, 2003)
Motion granted by Campaign for Fiscal Equity, Inc. v. State, 2003 N.Y. LEXIS 376 (N.Y., Apr. 3, 2003)
Motion granted by Campaign for Fiscal Equity, Inc. v. State, 2003 N.Y. LEXIS 402 (N.Y., Apr. 3, 2003)
Motion granted by Campaign for Fiscal Equity, Inc. v. State, 2003 N.Y. LEXIS 911 (N.Y., May 1, 2003)
Motion granted by Campaign for Fiscal Equity, Inc. v. State, 2003 N.Y. LEXIS 914 (N.Y., May 1, 2003)
Motion denied by N.Y. City Coalition to End Lead Poisoning, Inc. v. Vallone, 2003 N.Y. LEXIS 920 (N.Y., May 1, 2003)
Affirmed in part and modified in part by, Remitted by Campaign for Fiscal Equity, Inc. v. State, 2003 N.Y. LEXIS 1678 (N.Y., June 26, 2003)



DISPOSITION: Order and judgment entered 1/31/2001 reversed without costs; declaration made in favor of the State of New York; claims made under the DOE implementing regulations and under 42 USC § 1983 dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant State appealed the judgment of the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), that declared the State's method of funding education violated the Education Article of the New York Constitution and the United States Department of Education's implementing regulations under Title VI of the Civil Rights Act of 1964, 42 U.S.C.S. § 2000(d) et seq., and directed the State to implement various reforms of school financing and governance.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs, students, parents, and organizations concerned with education issues, commenced an action for a declaratory judgment and injunctive relief, on the ground that the State's public school financing system violated N.Y. Const. art. XI, § 1; U.S. Const. amend. XIV; N.Y. Const. art. I, § 11; N.Y. Const. art. I, § 11; Title VI of the Civil Rights Act of 1964, 42 U.S.C.S. § 2000(d) et seq.; and 34 C.F.R. § 100.3(B)(2)(p). Originally, the appellate court dismissed the claim under Title VI, since there was no showing of intentional discrimination; however, the appellate court reinstated the claim for violations of Title VI's implementing regulations. On appeal, the appellate court found that there was no evidence that students were unable to perform basic mathematical calculations, and allowing that some amount of history, civics, science, and technology were components of a sound basic education, there was no evidence concerning what that amount should be or what amount was actually being provided. Accordingly, plaintiffs failed to establish that New York City public school children were not receiving the opportunity for a sound basic education.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed, and the claim was dismissed.


HEADNOTES

Schools - State Aid to School Districts - Constitutionality of State's Public School Financing System

1. The State's educational funding system does not contravene the Education Article of the New York State Constitution (NY Const, art XI, § 1). The "sound basic education" standard enunciated by the Court of Appeals in Campaign for Fiscal Equity v State of New York (86 NY2d 307) requires the State to provide a minimally adequate educational opportunity, but not to guarantee some higher, largely unspecified level of education, as laudable as that goal might be. A "sound basic education" should consist of the skills necessary to obtain employment, and to competently discharge one's civil responsibilities. Plaintiffs failed to establish that the New York City public school children are not receiving the opportunity for a sound basic education. Even if New York City schools do not provide a sound basic education, plaintiffs failed to prove that deficiencies in the City's school system are caused by the State's funding system.

Schools - State Aid to School Districts - Discrimination Cause of Action under Implementing Regulations of Title VI of Civil Rights Act

2. The State's educational funding system does not violate the United States Department of Education's implementing regulations under title VI of the Civil Rights Act of 1964 (42 USC § 2000d) which prohibit a recipient of federal financial assistance from "utilizing criteria or methods of administration which have the effect of subjecting individuals to discrimination because of their race, color, or national origin" (34 CFR 100.3 [b] [2]). Title VI prohibits intentional discrimination, which is not alleged in the instant case, and there is no private right of action under the implementing regulations, since the empowering statute reveals no congressional intent to create one. Plaintiffs may not enforce the regulations through 42 USC § 1983, which provides a cause of action for "the deprivation of any rights, privileges, or immunities secured by the Constitution and laws" by anyone acting "under color of any statute, ordinance, regulation, custom, or usage, of any State," and regulations, standing alone, are not "laws" within the meaning of section 1983.

Coleman ex rel. Thomas v. Thomas


2001-02623


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant father appealed from an order of the Family Court, Queens County (New York), that denied his objections to a previous order denying his application to terminate his child support obligation after the death of plaintiff grandmother of his child, to whom the child support had been payable.


OVERVIEW: The father was subject to a child support order. Payments were to be made to the child's grandmother, who had custody of the daughter. The grandmother commenced an enforcement proceeding under New York's version of the Uniform Interstate Family Support Act, N.Y. Fam. Ct. Act art. 5-B. Fam. Ct. Act § 580-401(c) did guarantee a hearing and the father had received two such hearings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

Williams v. Nicoletti


2001-06374


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT

April 15, 2002, Submitted  
June 3, 2002, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a hearing, a hearing officer found petitioner employee guilty of misconduct in failing a drug test while on the job, and recommended his dismissal. Respondent commissioner of the department of public works adopted the hearing officer's recommendation. The employee appealed.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court found that the evidence at the hearing consisted of, among other things, testimony of two medical and scientific experts from the testing company concerning the validity of the drug tests, complete documentation of the test results showing the employee's drug use, testimony of the deputy commissioner of the department of public works who explained the city's random drug test program, and the employee's signed certification that the sample had been properly collected and sealed, which certification he did not controvert. Thus, it was clear that the hearing officer's determination of drug use was supported by substantial evidence. The federal statute involved was not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

Associated Int'l Brokers, Inc. v. Levin


1242N


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


294 A.D.2d 317; 743 N.Y.S.2d 93; 2002 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 5583



May 30, 2002, Decided  
May 30, 2002, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner excess line brokers sought review of a determination of respondent agency finding the brokers violated provisions of the insurance law and applicable regulations by failing to file affidavits and premium tax statements with the Excess Line Association of New York and by failing to pay excess line premium taxes on the transportation coverage component of 248 policies placed by them.


OVERVIEW: It was undisputed that in 248 instances the excess line brokers issued separate transportation policies rather than include transportation coverage in the insureds' jeweler's block coverage. It was also undisputed that, had transportation coverage been placed by the brokers under the rubric of jeweler's block coverage, the brokers would have been subject to excess line filing requirements and liable for excess line premium taxes on the placed coverage. The jeweler's block coverage comprised inland marine coverage for items transported by the insured, and it was not a proper practice to issue such transportation coverage under a separate policy and thereby avoid regulatory oversight and payment of excess line premium taxes. The policies in question did not, in fact, extend ocean marine coverage, but rather extended coverage of the inland marine sort properly included within a jeweler's block policy. The insurance was not exclusively of the kind qualifying for the exemption set forth in N.Y. Ins. Law § 2117(b)(3). The penalty imposed in lieu of license revocation did not shock the judicial conscience and thus could not be disturbed.


OUTCOME: The determination was confirmed. The petition was denied.
