Roebling Liquors v. Comm'r of Taxation & Fin.


86792


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


284 A.D.2d 669; 728 N.Y.S.2d 509; 2001 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 6236



June 14, 2001, Decided  
June 14, 2001, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended November 19, 2001. Writ of certiorari denied: Roebling Liquors, Inc. v. Comm'r of Taxation & Fin., 2002 U.S. LEXIS 5527 (U.S. Oct. 7, 2002) 



DISPOSITION: The determination is confirmed, without costs, and petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner liquor store appealed a determination by respondent tax appeals tribunal that sustained an assessment of sales and use tax by respondent revenue department.


OVERVIEW: Department sent letters to wholesalers of alcoholic beverages requesting copies of sales tax records. It then conducted an audit of liquor store's records and assessed additional taxes, interest, and penalties. A conferee and an administrative law judge approved the assessment. Tribunal upheld the basic decision, and liquor store appealed. The appellate court rejected liquor store's constitutional claims since liquor store was required to maintain the records and only had a limited expectation of privacy in them. Department had authority to inspect and examine the records on demand. Liquor store failed to overcome the presumption of receipt of the mailed notices. The conciliation orders were timely made. Department's use of outside date was permissible because the audit exposed irregularities in liquor store's records. Liquor store did not prove that the audit method was unreliable.


OUTCOME: The determination was confirmed, and the petition was dismissed.

 

702 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Bowden v. Iona Grammar Sch.


2000-08191


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


284 A.D.2d 357; 726 N.Y.S.2d 685; 2001 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 6124


May 18, 2001, Argued  
June 11, 2001, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, student and others, sued defendants, school and another, to recover damages for, inter alia, breach of contract. The Supreme Court of Westchester County, New York, granted plaintiffs a preliminary injunction, and denied the parts of defendants' cross motion which sought dismissal of the first, second, third, seventh, and eighth causes of action in the complaint insofar as asserted against them. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: School barred student from attending classes because he had not received the immunizations required by N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 2164. Plaintiffs claimed a religious exemption under N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 2164(9) and submitted to the school a sworn statement that they were members of a religion that opposed immunizations. Defendants denied the exemption on the ground that plaintiffs were not members of a bona fide recognized religious organization. Defendants argued on appeal that the religious exemption was not applicable to private or parochial schools and that § 2164(9) did not allow plaintiffs an action to enforce exemption rights. The appellate court held that (1) the exemption applied to private and parochial schools; (2) plaintiffs could assert their cause of action under the statute despite the fact the statute did not specifically authorize such an action; and (3) the trial court properly granted the preliminary injunction because plaintiffs established a likelihood of success on the merits given that defendants denied the exemption using a criterion that was no longer in the statute and because the loss of First Amendment freedoms could show irreparable injury.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's order insofar as appealed from, with costs.

 

703 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


St. Lucia v. Novello


87164


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


284 A.D.2d 591; 726 N.Y.S.2d 488; 2001 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 6001



June 7, 2001, Decided  
June 7, 2001, Entered



DISPOSITION: Determination confirmed, without costs, and petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A hearing committee of respondent State Board for Professional Medical Conduct (New York) revoked petitioner doctor's license to practice medicine in New York after sustaining most of the 11 specifications of misconduct with which doctor was charged relating to his treatment of certain patients. Doctor initiated a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 and N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 230-c(5), seeking review of that determination.


OVERVIEW: Among the specifications of professional misconduct that were sustained were three that charged moral unfitness for engaging in sexual relationships with patients. On review, doctor asserted, inter alia, that N.Y. Educ. Law § 6530(20) and N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 8, § 29.1(b)(5), which defined "professional misconduct" to include conduct that evidenced moral unfitness, were unconstitutionally vague; that he was denied due process in two respects at his hearing; and that the underlying determination was not supported by substantial evidence. The reviewing court held that (1) the two statutes cited by doctor were not unconstitutionally vague as they give fair notice of the proscribed conduct; (2) doctor was not denied due process with respect to his cross-examination of one patient due to his inability to obtain that patient's counseling records as her psychological status was not in issue, and he was not denied due process due to the admission of certain hearsay testimony, as the hearing committee was not bound by the strict rules of evidence; and (3) the hearing committee's determination was supported by substantial evidence from the witnesses against doctor.


OUTCOME: The reviewing court confirmed the determination, without costs, and dismissed the petition.

 

704 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Moran Towing Corp. v. Urbach


87765


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


283 A.D.2d 78; 726 N.Y.S.2d 748; 2001 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 6005



June 7, 2001, Decided  
June 7, 2001, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Name of this Case, Counsel, and Opinion Text has been Corrected by the Court September 21, 2001.
Appeal dismissed by Moran Towing Corp. v. Urbach, 96 N.Y.2d 937, 759 N.E.2d 375, 2001 N.Y. LEXIS 3196, 733 N.Y.S.2d 376 (2001)
Reversed by, Remitted by Moran Towing Corp. v. Urbach, 99 N.Y.2d 443, 787 N.E.2d 624, 2003 N.Y. LEXIS 279, 757 N.Y.S.2d 513 (2003)



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed, on the law, with costs, motion denied and it is declared that the New York fuel consumption tax found in Tax Law § 301 (a) (1) (ii) and § 301-a (b) (2) and (c) (1) (B) is unconstitutional.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants towing companies appealed the Albany County Supreme Court's (New York) grant of respondent tax commissioner's motion to dismiss, claiming that N.Y. Tax Law §§ 301(a)(1)(ii), 301-a(b)(2), (c)(1)(B), were unconstitutional, and they did not have to exhaust their administrative remedies.


OVERVIEW: Tax commissioner created tax on vessels engaged in petroleum business based on gallons of fuel sold or consumed. Towing companies challenged the tax because it applied to fuel in the vessels' engines used solely during their intrastate movement. Trial court granted tax commissioner's motion to dismiss because towing companies failed to exhaust their administrative remedies. On appeal the appellate court held that the tax was facially unconstitutional because it violated the Commerce Clause. Towing companies were being taxed on fuel purchased outside the state, used solely in the vessel's engines, and never removed from the flow of interstate commerce, or coming to rest in the state. The tax had no substantial nexus with the state. As a result, towing companies did not have to exhaust their administrative remedies.


OUTCOME: The judgment granting tax commissioner's motion to dismiss was reversed. N.Y. Tax Law §§ 301(a)(1)(ii), 301-a(b)(2), (c)(1)(B), were declared unconstitutional.


HEADNOTES

Administrative Law - Failure to Exhaust Administrative Remedies - Challenge to Petroleum Business Tax - Facial Unconstitutionality 

1. Petitioners need not exhaust administrative remedies before challenging, as violative of the Commerce Clause, that portion of New York's Petroleum Business Tax, which deems vessels which merely enter New York waters, propelled by petroleum in their fuel tanks, to be a "petroleum business" within the State sufficient to establish the requisite nexus for the purpose of taxation even though the fuel consumed during such interstate voyage never comes to rest in the State (see, Tax Law § 301-a). While a party seeking judicial review of a tax determination must ordinarily first exhaust administrative remedies, where, as here, the taxing statute is challenged as facially unconstitutional, a basis which is not fact dependent, the development of a factual record at the administrative level serves no purpose and thus constitutes an exception to the exhaustion requirement.

Taxation - Motor Fuel Taxes - Constitutionality of Petroleum Business Tax - Commerce Clause

2. That portion of New York's Petroleum Business Tax (PBT), which deems vessels which merely enter New York waters, propelled by petroleum in their fuel tanks, to be a "petroleum business" within the State sufficient to establish the requisite nexus for the purpose of taxation even though the fuel consumed during such interstate voyage never comes to rest in the State (see, Tax Law § 301-a), is facially unconstitutional as violative of the Commerce Clause (US Const, art I, § 8, cl [3]). Under established Commerce Clause jurisprudence, a substantial nexus with a taxing state must exist before a tax may be imposed on an activity or business. The PBT artificially imposes such nexus by taxing petitioners for being engaged in a "petroleum business" on fuel purchased outside of New York which is brought into New York in their vessels' engines and consumed through their intrastate movings while in New York, without having been removed from the stream of interstate commerce. Consequently, the PBT is an unauthorized exercise of the State's power over an instrumentality of interstate commerce. Moreover, since there is no set of circumstances under which the challenged portions of the PBT would be valid, no savings analysis need be employed.

 

705 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Cummins v. N. Med. Family Physicians


88666


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


283 A.D.2d 861; 726 N.Y.S.2d 163; 2001 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 5420



May 24, 2001, Decided  
May 24, 2001, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, filed a claim for continued medical benefits for a work-related back injury. After a hearing, a workers' compensation law judge authorized continued medical treatment for her but, despite finding that appellant's attorney rendered excellent service, denied counsel's request for a monetary fee. Respondent New York Workers' Compensation Board upheld the decision. Appellant filed an appeal.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court rejected appellant's argument that respondent erred in finding that counsel fees could only be paid from lost wages and not from, or as a result of, an award of medical benefits. Under N.Y. Workers' Comp. Law § 24, counsel fees had to be paid from compensation, which was statutorily defined as the money allowance payable to an employee or to his dependents. N.Y. Workers' Comp. Law § 2(6). No such economic benefit was paid to appellant. Since respondent determined that an award of medical benefits was not an award of compensation subject to a lien for counsel fees, there was no abuse of discretion in respondent's refusal to award counsel fees. The lack of statutory authority to do so provided a rational basis for respondent's decision.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

 

706 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Counties of Warren & Wash. Indus. Dev. Agency v. Adirondack Res. Recovery Assocs.


88566


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


283 A.D.2d 846; 726 N.Y.S.2d 478; 2001 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 5436



May 24, 2001, Decided  
May 24, 2001, Entered



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff public benefit corporation sued defendant, project contractor, seeking declaratory relief and damages allegedly owed by project contractor. The Supreme Court in Washington County (New York) entered an order which partially granted project contractor's motion for partial summary judgment, dismissing the complaint and upon reconsideration, entered an order which adhered to its prior decision. Public benefit corporation appealed.


OVERVIEW: Public benefit corporation contracted with project contractor to design, construct, operate and own a resource recovery facility. Certain floor beams in the facility were damaged and replaced by project contractor. The insurance carrier paid the claim, less a deductible under the policy. Also, as a result of federal legislation, new equipment was required at the facility. The public benefit corporation's complaint asserted six separate causes of action, and specifically sought: (1) a declaration that project contractor was not entitled to be reimbursed for the deductible associated with the property damage insurance claim, (2) damages for legal costs, and (3) a declaration that the cost of the new equipment be allocated between the parties. The appellate court found that under the agreement, the insurance deductible amount was properly passed through by project contractor to public benefit corporation. The contract required public benefit corporation to finance the new equipment. Finally, as public benefit corporation was not a political subdivision, the financing arrangements did not violate any constitutional provision.


OUTCOME: The orders were affirmed.

 

707 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Bd. of Educ. v. Bd. of Trustees


88421


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


282 A.D.2d 166; 723 N.Y.S.2d 262; 2001 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 3958



April 19, 2001, Decided  
April 19, 2001, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended August 20, 2001.



DISPOSITION: Judgment modified, on the law, without costs, by reversing so much thereof as granted respondents' motion dismissing petitioner Board of Education of the Roosevelt Union Free School District as a party in the CPLR article 78 proceeding; deny the motion to that extent; and, as so modified, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent school's application to be a charter school was approved by respondent state university, and deemed approved by respondent state regents. A Supreme Court, Albany County (New York) judgment denied petitioner local school district's petition for a preliminary injunction to enjoin the respondent school's opening and operation, and granted school's motions to dismiss respondent regents and petitioner district. Petitioner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The proceeding was a combined appeal of the judgment and the determinations of respondent trustees and regents. Petitioner argued the school would impair its financial ability to deliver state mandated education, and claimed the Charter Schools Act of 1998 was either unconstitutional or not followed. The appeals court determined (1) petitioner did not have standing to contest constitutionality, as the act was created by the state, and the act was followed to approve the application for the charter school; (2) petitioner was a proper party to the N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding, since it was granted the power, authority, and responsibility to administer educational affairs of the district, and there was no clear legislative intent to deprive it of capacity to sue; and (3) respondent regents were not necessary parties, since in actuality they were powerless to reject or veto a proposed charter submitted to them by respondent trustees. Petitioner did not prove the act adversely affected its proprietary interest in a specific fund of moneys or any of the other three exceptions to the constitutional challenge rule, or that respondent trustees acted arbitrarily or capriciously.


OUTCOME: The portion of the judgment that dismissed petitioner school district as a party was reversed. The remainder of the judgment was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Schools - Board of Education - Capacity to Challenge Administrative Determination Approving Charter School Application

1. Petitioner Board of Education has the legal capacity to maintain a CPLR article 78 proceeding to challenge as arbitrary and capricious the administrative determination of the State University of New York Trustees approving the operation of a charter school within the boundaries of the school district. The right of a board of education of a school district to commence a CPLR article 78 proceeding challenging an administrative determination to approve a charter school application and issue a charter within a school district's boundaries (Education Law § 2851 et seq.) can be inferred as part of the school board's duty and responsibility to provide a system of public education to all children within its district (see, Education Law §§ 1709, 3202), particularly where, as here, a school board claims that its ability to provide education to all students within its district's boundaries is jeopardized by the determination, and the charter entity allegedly gave insufficient consideration to the issue of economic impact on the school district. Absent a clear legislative intent to negate judicial review, a school district or school board should not be prohibited from seeking review of the determination to grant an application and issue a charter.

Schools - Board of Education - Capacity to Challenge Constitutionality of Charter Schools Act

2. Although petitioner Board of Education has the legal capacity to maintain a CPLR article 78 proceeding to challenge as arbitrary and capricious the administrative determination of the State University of New York Trustees approving the operation of a charter school within the boundaries of the school district, the Board lacks the capacity to sue to invalidate the charter school statutory scheme (Education Law § 2851 et seq.) on constitutional grounds. Petitioner has not demonstrated that the Charter Schools Act affects any proprietary interest in a specific sum of money as to allow it to mount a constitutional challenge to invalidate the statutory scheme. Even though the Charter Schools Act contemplates that the State will initially fund money to the school district which, in turn, will distribute it to the subject charter school depending on the number of students enrolled in that school (see, Education Law § 2856 [1]), there is nothing in this funding mechanism which creates a proprietary interest in the school district to a specific sum of money where none otherwise existed. Rather, the funding follows the child and if the child does not attend one of its public schools, the school district has no right to the funds.

Parties - Necessary Parties - Dismissal of Board of Regents as Party Respondent in Proceeding Challenging Approval of Charter School Application

3. Supreme Court properly dismissed the Board of Regents as a party respondent in petitioner Board of Education's CPLR article 78 proceeding challenging the administrative determination of the State University of New York (SUNY) Trustees approving the operation of a charter school within the boundaries of the school district pursuant to the Charter Schools Act (see, Education Law § 2851 et seq.). Although the Board of Regents is designated as the "only" body authorized to issue a charter, in actuality the Board of Regents is powerless under the Charter Schools Act to reject or to veto a proposed charter submitted to it by the SUNY Trustees. Once a proposed charter is entered into between an applicant and the SUNY Trustees, the issuance of the charter itself is a fait accompli even where, as here, the Board of Regents may initially disapprove of some aspects of the application. Furthermore, no factual allegation or showing has been made that the Board of Regents played a substantial role in the injury to petitioners or that the Board of Regents was primarily responsible for the determination to approve the subject application or issue the charter. Moreover, notwithstanding its role in the process, there has not been a sufficient showing that the Board of Regents' participation is necessary for a complete resolution of the matter or that it will be inequitably affected by any possible resolution (see, CPLR 1001).

 

708 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Finch, Pruyn & Co. v. Kearns


88300


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


282 A.D.2d 858; 722 N.Y.S.2d 838; 2001 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 3663



April 12, 2001, Decided  
April 12, 2001, Entered



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner brought a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 action to review a determination of respondent school district approving expenditures for capital improvements. Petitioner appealed the judgment of the Supreme Court, Essex County (New York), which dismissed petitioner's application.


OVERVIEW: The capital improvements were to be funded by real property tax adjustments. Five percent of the taxes was to be levied upon homestead property, and 95 percent was to be levied on non-homestead property. The proposal had been approved by the voters of respondent town. Petitioner, who owned non-homestead property, challenged respondent district's decision to approve the construction of a heated swimming pool. He appealed only the dismissal of his cause of action alleging that respondent's board's action was unconstitutional as applied to petitioner and other similarly situated owners of non-homestead property. The appellate court held that the New York Commissioner of Education generally had exclusive jurisdiction over the type of claim at issue. Such a claim required the resolution of factual issues best addressed initially to the administrative agency.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

709 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Citizens for the Hudson Valley v. N.Y. State Bd. on Elec. Generation Siting


87928


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


281 A.D.2d 89; 723 N.Y.S.2d 532; 2001 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 3664



April 12, 2001, Decided  
April 12, 2001, Entered


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended July 30, 2001.



DISPOSITION: Determination confirmed, without costs, and petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, neighbors and environmental activists, sought review of a determination of respondent New York State Board on Electric Generation Siting and the Environment in the Hudson Valley, arguing inadequacy of compliance with N.Y. Pub. Serv. Law art. X.


OVERVIEW: N.Y. Pub. Serv. Law art. X required respondent agency to perform a comprehensive review before certifying any site as appropriate for a new electricity generating facility. When respondent certified a site in a scenic area of the Hudson Valley, petitioners challenged the review's compliance with the statute. The court found substantial evidence in the record supporting each of respondent's determinations that statutory requirements had been met, particularly that appropriate procurement standards had been used and that waiver of local zoning laws was appropriate. Because the utility lacked eminent domain powers, respondent could not have required it to consider all alternative sites, but there was plenty of evidence that respondent took care to determine that the siting decision would not affect the view from a nearby historic site, the estate of the painter.


OUTCOME: The court confirmed the administrative determination, finding substantial evidence in the record supporting each of respondent's findings.


HEADNOTES

Appeal - Preservation of Issue for Review - Siting of Major Electric Generating Facility - Exception Taken to Administrative Decision

1. In a proceeding challenging the determination of respondent New York State Board on Electric Generation Siting and the Environment under Public Service Law article X issuing a certificate of environmental compatibility and public need to allow construction of a major electric generating facility on industrially zoned land located along the banks of the Hudson River, those claims that were not effectively raised by petitioners in the administrative forum have not been preserved for appellate review. Public Service Law § 170 (1), which establishes an application for rehearing as a prerequisite for judicial review, does not automatically make every issue raised in the petition for rehearing subject to appellate review. There is still the regulatory requirement that a party take exception to the recommended decision as a prerequisite to raising arguments in a petition for rehearing (see, 16 NYCRR 4.10 [d] [2]).

Public Utilities - Siting of Major Electric Generating Facility - Waiver of "Unreasonably Restrictive" Local Zoning Requirements

2. In a proceeding challenging the determination of respondent New York State Board on Electric Generation Siting and the Environment under Public Service Law article X issuing a certificate of environmental compatibility and public need to allow construction of a major electric generating facility on industrially zoned land located along the banks of the Hudson River, the Siting Board's waiver of certain "unreasonably restrictive" requirements of the Town zoning ordinance pursuant to Public Service Law § 168 (2) (d) did not violate the home rule provisions of the State Constitution (NY Const, art IX, § 2 [b] [2]), which empower the Legislature to enact general laws "affecting the property, affairs or government of any local government." A statute qualifies as a "general law" if it in terms and in effect applies alike to all localities. The comprehensive regulatory scheme relating to the siting of public utilities qualifies as a "general law" preempting local zoning ordinances whether or not a particular new power facility fulfills a State-wide interest. Furthermore, the phrase "unreasonably restrictive" contained in Public Service Law § 168 (2) (d) is not unconstitutionally vague when read with the qualifying language of the statute regarding "the existing technology or the needs of or costs to ratepayers." As so qualified, the statutory language provides a sufficient objective standard for making a determination as to whether a local ordinance is "unduly restrictive."

Public Utilities - Siting of Major Electric Generating Facility - Selection Pursuant to "Approved Procurement Process"

3. In a proceeding challenging the determination of respondent New York State Board on Electric Generation Siting and the Environment under Public Service Law article X issuing a certificate of environmental compatibility and public need to allow construction of a major electric generating facility on industrially zoned land located along the banks of the Hudson River, the Siting Board had a rational basis for determining that the facility was selected pursuant to an "approved procurement process" (Public Service Law § 160 [7]; § 168 [2] [a] [i], [ii]). Pursuant to its statutory authority (see, Public Service Law § 66-i), the Department of Public Service issued rulings declaring that competition in the electricity supply market is an "approved procurement process" consistent with the State Energy Plan in effect at the time of the current application. Petitioners' belated attack on those rulings lacks merit.

Public Utilities - Siting of Major Electric Generating Facility - Evaluation of Alternative Locations

4. In a proceeding challenging the determination of respondent New York State Board on Electric Generation Siting and the Environment under Public Service Law article X issuing a certificate of environmental compatibility and public need to allow construction of a major electric generating facility on industrially zoned land located along the banks of the Hudson River, the Siting Board properly determined that the applicant was not required to describe and evaluate alternative sites pursuant to Public Service Law § 164 (1) (b). The Siting Board rationally determined that a private applicant, lacking the power of eminent domain, cannot be required to present alternative sites that it neither owns nor has an option to purchase (see, 16 NYCRR 1001.2 [d] [2]). Further, although the Siting Board permitted petitioner to offer evidence of alternative sites on the issue of whether the plant is in the public interest, the record supports the Board's conclusion that the alternatives offered by petitioner had problems of their own and that there was "no showing that there is an available, preferable site that should be developed" instead of the proposed site.

Public Utilities - Siting of Major Electric Generating Facility - Visual Impact of Proposed Facility

5. In a proceeding challenging the determination of respondent New York State Board on Electric Generation Siting and the Environment under Public Service Law article X issuing a certificate of environmental compatibility and public need to allow construction of a major electric generating facility on industrially zoned land located along the banks of the Hudson River, there is substantial evidence in the record to support the Siting Board's conclusion that, considering the environmental impacts, the construction and operation of the facility is in the public interest (Public Service Law § 168 [2] [e]). The record does not support petitioner's contention that construction of the facility will unreasonably impact renowned views of the Hudson River Valley. The visual impact study commissioned by the applicant resulted in the reduction of the height of the plant's three emission stacks to 180 feet, a height that eliminates the need for obtrusive aviation warning lights and substantially reduces the degree to which the facility could be seen from distant points. In addition, the ultimate decision to utilize dry cooling technology not only minimized impacts on the Hudson River but provided the further benefit of essentially eliminating visible stack plumes, a very significant mitigation measure in light of the focus groups' conclusion that stack plumes represented the most significant visual impact of the facility.

Public Utilities - Siting of Major Electric Generating Facility - Lower Electricity Prices

6. In a proceeding challenging the determination of respondent New York State Board on Electric Generation Siting and the Environment under Public Service Law article X issuing a certificate of environmental compatibility and public need to allow construction of a major electric generating facility on industrially zoned land located along the banks of the Hudson River, the record supports the Siting Board's determination that the plant would contribute to competition, thereby lowering electricity prices, displace less efficient plants, provide a reliable source of electricity at a time when there are projected energy shortfalls and relieve transmission constraints. Evidence also established that, as a modern natural gas fueled facility, certain noxious gas levels would be reduced and the use of dry cooling technology would result in fewer fish kills because production will be displaced from other Hudson River power plants that draw more water and, therefore, kill more fish. Further, the record indicates that the plant was required as a condition of approval to submit to the New York Independent System Operation (NYISO) for the dispatch of electricity. Therefore, even if the plant's electricity were to be sold outside the State, transmission of the electricity through NYISO would commit generators to minimize costs and maintain reliability and the overall amount of electricity produced in the State would be increased, thereby resulting in lower electricity prices.

People v. Trammel


11793


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


282 A.D.2d 829; 723 N.Y.S.2d 545; 2001 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 3681



April 12, 2001, Decided  
April 12, 2001, Entered



DISPOSITION: Judgment is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by the County Court of Sullivan County (New York) upon defendant's plea of guilty to the crime of aggravated harassment of an employee by an inmate, N.Y. Penal Law § 240.32. Defendant appealed his conviction, arguing that the statute constituted an unconstitutional ex post facto law as applied to defendant.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's conviction arose from an incident in which defendant threw his urine on a correction officer. When the defendant was not a juvenile, an element of the crime of aggravated harassment of an employee by an inmate was that, at the time of the commission of the prohibited conduct, the defendant had to be an inmate as that term was defined in N.Y. Penal Law § 240.32. Defendant argued that the statute violated the ex post facto prohibition because defendant achieved the necessary inmate status prior to the effective date of the statute. Thus, he argued that N.Y. Penal Law § 240.32 was unconstitutional, as applied to him, because it rendered his conduct criminal based on an event, his incarceration, which predated the statute's enactment. The appellate court held defendant did not commit the crime of aggravated harassment of an employee until he engaged in the prohibited conduct in February 1998, well after N.Y. Penal Law § 240.32 was enacted. The appellate court held defendant clearly had fair warning that his throwing of urine would result in criminal liability. Defendant's preexisting condition or status as an inmate did not result in an ex post facto violation.


OUTCOME: The decision was affirmed.

In re Anthony "S"


86544


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT

April 5, 2001, Decided  
April 5, 2001, Entered



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent mother appealed the order of the Family Court of Schuyler County (New York) granting petitioner county social services department's application to adjudicate the mother's children to be permanently neglected and terminating the mother's parental rights.


OVERVIEW: The department sought to have the mother's children adjudicated permanently neglected. The dispositive issue was whether the mother had failed to plan for her children's future. Evidence relevant to the department's burden to demonstrate that it exercised diligent efforts to encourage and strengthen the parental relationship was properly admitted. The family court properly weighed all dispositional alternatives for the children in determining that it would be in their best interests to be freed for adoption. Evidence supported the family court's finding that the mother failed to plan for the future of her children.


OUTCOME: The order was affirmed.

People v. Falcon


3682


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


281 A.D.2d 368; 722 N.Y.S.2d 538; 2001 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 3207



March 29, 2001, Decided  
March 29, 2001, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed judgment of Supreme Court, New York County (New York), convicting him, after jury trial, of murder, attempted murder, criminal use of firearm, assault, and criminal possession of weapon, and sentencing him to consecutive terms of 25 years to life and 5 to 15 years on murder and attempted murder convictions, to be served concurrently with three concurrent terms of 5 to 15 years on remaining convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's contention that the trial court improperly denied his motion to suppress his statements to the police was moot since those statements were never introduced at trial. Defendant's claim that the trial court improperly precluded him from introducing the very statements he sought to have suppressed was unavailing, since the prosecution never offered to introduce the inculpatory portions of those statements, and the exculpatory portions of the statements did not qualify as declarations against penal interest. Defendant's claim of unconstitutional delay in prosecution was unpreserved. The trial court properly denied, as untimely, defendant's request to dismiss certain counts of the indictment on statute of limitations grounds. Since the trial court submitted the lesser included offense of manslaughter in the first degree to the jury, which never reached that charge, defendant's claim that the trial court should have also submitted the more remote charge of manslaughter in the second degree was foreclosed.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Bloomfield v. Bloomfield


1274


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


281 A.D.2d 301; 723 N.Y.S.2d 143; 2001 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 2991



March 22, 2001, Decided  
March 22, 2001, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, husband, sued defendant, wife, for divorce. Wife filed a counterclaim demanding, inter alia, equitable distribution of marital property. The Supreme Court, Bronx County (New York) held that a prenuptial agreement which husband and wife signed was unenforceable and directed husband to pay counsel, appraisal, and accountant's fees. Husband appealed.


OVERVIEW: Husband and wife signed a prenuptial agreement in 1969. Under that agreement, which wife signed without the benefit of counsel, wife waived all present and future rights in real, personal, or mixed property husband owned at the time of marriage or would acquire in the future. At the time the agreement was signed, New York law gave a wife no rights in or to her husband's property, other than the right to spousal support, but also prohibited a wife from waiving her right to support. The law was changed after husband and wife were married and the change permitted courts to divide the marital estate. The appellate court held that husband and wife's prenuptial agreement was void on its face because it attempted to relieve husband of his obligation to provide spousal support, and that the six-year statute of limitations that applied to prenuptial agreements was tolled during the period of the parties' marriage. The court also stated that if the agreement had not been not void, the court would have found that it was unconscionable, invalidating it on that basis.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Pleakis v. Peterson


271, CA 00-02653


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FOURTH DEPARTMENT

March 21, 2001, Decided  
March 21, 2001, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The case was an appeal of a decision of the Supreme Court, Cattaraugus County (New York).


OVERVIEW: Respondents challenged a decision of the lower court which held that the time in which petitioner acted as an investigator prior to the passage of N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law §§ 58(4)(c), 59-a should have been included in the 18-month period necessary for permanent designation as detective/investigator. Respondents also challenged the lower court's finding that demotion of petitioner from detective to uniform officer was a demotion. The appellate court found Civil Service Law § 58(4)(c)(iv) retroactively applied to those individuals who were designated detectives during the period between the passage of N.Y. Civ. Serv. Law § 58(4)(c) and the decision which held the original statute unconstitutional. Respondents also argued petitioner's reassignment was not a demotion. The appellate court found after reassignment to a uniform officer, the officer would be compensated at a lower rate of pay. Thus, respondents' reassignment of petitioner constituted a demotion. The appellate court found, though, that the assignment of mileage compensation was not an incidental expense that a court could award as part of a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 judgment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision on all matters except those concerning costs. The court found the lower court could not order compensation for mileage costs as an incidental expense.

Schulz v. N.Y. State Legislature


87940


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


281 A.D.2d 682; 721 N.Y.S.2d 686; 2001 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 2039



March 1, 2001, Decided  
March 1, 2001, Entered



DISPOSITION: Affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action, brought pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 3001 and N.Y. State Fin. Law art. 7A, seeking a declaration that 1998 N.Y. Laws chs. 5, 124, were unconstitutional, plaintiffs appealed the order of the Albany County Supreme Court (New York) which granted defendants' motions to dismiss the complaint for lack of standing and failure to state a cause of action.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to 1998 N.Y. Laws chs. 5, 124, revenue bonds were sold or authorized to be sold by the involved public authorities. Thereafter, plaintiffs commenced an action seeking a declaration that 1998 N.Y. Laws chs. 5, 124, were unconstitutional. The trial court granted defendants' motions to dismiss. On appeal, plaintiffs argued, inter alia, that N.Y. Const. art. VII, § 16, required a finding that the financial obligations arising from the implementation of 1998 N.Y. Laws chs. 5, 124, were legally enforceable debts of the state, thus making both statutes violative of N.Y. Const. art. VII, § 11, which prohibited the contracting of state debts without a public referendum. The appellate court affirmed the order, determining that even when scrutinizing 1998 N.Y. Laws chs. 5, 124, in light of the mandates of N.Y. Const. art. VII, § 16, the appellate court found that those laws created no debt on behalf of the state which may ripen into an enforceable right against the state on the part of any bondholder. Accordingly, the appellate court concluded that their enactment did not violate that constitutional provision or any of the debt-limiting provisions of the New York Constitution.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed the order because the challenged laws created no debt on behalf of the state which could ripen into an enforceable right against the state on the part of any bondholder. Thus, their enactment did not violate that constitutional provision or any of the debt-limiting provisions of the New York Constitution.

Mary A. C. v. John J. G.


(114), CAF 00-00263


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FOURTH DEPARTMENT

717 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


People v. Mower


10365, 12171


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


280 A.D.2d 25; 719 N.Y.S.2d 780; 2001 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 983



February 1, 2001, Decided  
February 1, 2001, Entered



DISPOSITION: Judgment and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a consolidated appeal, defendant appealed the judgment and order of the Supreme Court, Otsego County (New York), which convicted him upon his plea of guilty of murder in the first degree and denied his N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 440.10 motion to vacate the judgment of conviction. The court granted permission to appeal the order denying the motion.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to first-degree murder for killing his parents a month before he was to turn 19 years old. He appealed the conviction. He also challenged the denial of his motion under N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 440.10 to vacate the conviction. The appellate court affirmed, finding that the trial court had the statutory authority to sentence defendant to life imprisonment without parole. Defendant had concluded his first 18 years of life on his 18th birthday for purposes of N.Y. Penal Law § 125.27. Defendant's reliance on U.S. Const. amend. VIII was misplaced because at the guilt phase of the trial he had not yet been convicted, and thus was not exposed to, a death sentence.


OUTCOME: The judgment and order were affirmed. The plea of guilty was not the result of a mistake of law and the integrity of the grand jury process had not been impaired.


HEADNOTES

Crimes - Murder - Validity of Plea under Death Penalty Statute and Imposition of Life Sentence without Parole

1. Defendant's counseled plea of guilty to one count of murder in the first degree (Penal Law § 125.27 [1] [a] [viii]) in satisfaction of all charges arising from the shooting deaths of his parents, and his sentence to life imprisonment without parole, are lawful and should not be vacated on direct appeal or on defendant's motion pursuant to CPL 440.10 where the prosecutor did not file a notice of intent to seek the death penalty. Under these circumstances, the capital plea provisions invalidated in Matter of Hynes v Tomei (92 NY2d 613, cert denied 527 US 1015) during the pendency of a death penalty notice (see, CPL 220.10 [5] [e]; 220.30 [3] [b] [vii]) are not implicated. Rather, Supreme Court had the statutory authority to sentence defendant to life imprisonment without parole pursuant to CPL 400.27, which, in addition to setting forth the procedure for a separate proceeding for the jury to consider the death penalty where a defendant was convicted by a jury and the prosecution had timely filed a notice of intent to seek the death penalty, specifically provides that "[n]othing in this section shall be deemed to preclude the people at any time from determining that the death penalty shall not be sought in a particular case, in which case the separate sentencing proceeding shall not be conducted and the court may sentence such defendant to life imprisonment without parole" (CPL 400.27 [1]).

Crimes - Murder - Death Penalty - "Same Criminal Transaction"

2. Defendant's counseled plea of guilty to one count of murder in the first degree (Penal Law § 125.27 [1] [a] [viii]) in satisfaction of all charges arising from the shooting deaths of his parents, and his sentence to life imprisonment without parole, are lawful and should not be vacated on direct appeal or on defendant's motion pursuant to CPL 440.10. The Legislature's failure to define "same criminal transaction" as an aggravating factor does not render Penal Law § 125.27 (1) (a) (viii) unconstitutionally vague. Rather, the statute unambiguously proscribes multiple killings, which is specific conduct easily avoided by the innocent minded.

Crimes - Murder - First Degree Murder - 18-Year Age Requirement

3. Defendant's counseled plea of guilty to one count of murder in the first degree (Penal Law § 125.27 [1] [a] [viii]) in satisfaction of all charges arising from the shooting death of his parents, and his sentence to life imprisonment without parole, are lawful and should not be vacated on direct appeal or on defendant's motion pursuant to CPL 440.10. Penal Law § 125.27 (1) (b) is not unconstitutional due to its failure to define the phrase "more than eighteen years old," an express prerequisite to prosecution for first degree murder. An individual concludes the "first eighteen years of life" on his or her eighteenth birthday and begins the "nineteenth year of life" on that day. Consequently, the statutory phrase "more than eighteen years old" includes persons such as defendant, who was 18 years and 11 months old at the time of the events charged in the indictment.

Grand Jury - Defective Proceeding - Integrity of Grand Jury Impaired by Actions of District Attorney

4. Defendant's counseled plea of guilty to one count of murder in the first degree (Penal Law § 125.27 [1] [a] [viii]) in satisfaction of all charges arising from the shooting deaths of his parents, and his sentence to life imprisonment without parole, are lawful and should not be vacated on direct appeal or on defendant's motion pursuant to CPL 440.10. The integrity of the Grand Jury process was not impaired and defendant suffered no prejudice from the prosecutor's exclusion of certain evidence. The evidence defendant sought to have presented was of the type tending only to mitigate his liability rather than absolve him entirely of guilt for the crimes. Furthermore, the prosecutor properly relayed the language of the statute verbatim.

Crimes - Murder - Death Penalty - Heightened Due Process Analysis

5. Defendant's counseled plea of guilty to one count of murder in the first degree (Penal Law § 125.27 [1] [a] [viii]) in satisfaction of all charges arising from the shooting deaths of his parents, and his sentence to life imprisonment without parole, are lawful and should not be vacated on direct appeal or on defendant's motion pursuant to CPL 440.10. Defendant was not entitled to a heightened due process analysis during the guilt phase of his trial, since heightened scrutiny is required only in the penalty phase of a capital prosecution. Defendant's reliance on the 8th Amendment lacks merit, since, where a capital defendant has not yet been convicted, and thus is not exposed to a death sentence, the defendant is entitled to only "standard 14th Amendment due process" rather than review under the 8th Amendment.

Schulz v. New York State Legislature


87185


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


278 A.D.2d 710; 718 N.Y.S.2d 422; 2000 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13327



December 21, 2000, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Appeal withdrawn by Schulz v. N.Y. State Legislature, 96 N.Y.2d 859, 754 N.E.2d 1115, 2001 N.Y. LEXIS 3205, 730 N.Y.S.2d 32 (2001)
Subsequent appeal at Schulz v. N.Y. State Legislature, 5 A.D.3d 885, 773 N.Y.S.2d 174, 2004 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 2536 (N.Y. App. Div. 3d Dep't, 2004)
Appeal denied by Schulz v. N.Y. State Legislature, 3 N.Y.3d 606, 818 N.E.2d 665, 2004 N.Y. LEXIS 2165, 785 N.Y.S.2d 23 (2004)



DISPOSITION: Judgment modified, on the law, without costs, by reversing so much thereof as granted the motion to dismiss the third and fourth claims against respondents Washington County and Warren County; motion denied to that extent and it is declared that State Finance Law § 123-b (1) has not been shown to be unconstitutional; and, as so modified, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged the ruling of the Supreme Court of Albany County (New York) dismissing appellants' complaint alleging the unconstitutionality of 1985 N.Y. Laws ch. 682, certain contracts entered into by appellee counties, N.Y. State Fin. Law §123-b(1), Warren County, N.Y., Budget Resolution No. 367 of 1998 and certain other 1998 resolutions of the Boards of Supervisors of appellee counties.


OVERVIEW: Appellants unsuccessfully sued appellees over 1985 N.Y. Laws ch. 682, N.Y. State Fin. Law §123-b(1) and contracts entered into by appellee counties regarding solid waste disposal. Appellants renewed these claims, in whole or in part, and additionally challenged the constitutionality of resolutions passed by appellee counties after the previous litigation. Appellee state defendants moved to dismiss the most recent complaint on the grounds of res judicata, collateral estoppel, and laches. The trial court dismissed appellants' complaint "in all respects" on the basis of res judicata and laches. Appellants sought review. Appellants' constitutional challenge to 1985 N.Y. Laws ch. 682, N.Y. State Fin. Law §123-b(1), and appellee counties' financing and management contracts pursuant to ch. 682, should have been, and, to some extent, was previously litigated. As a result, their relitigation, even under different legal theories, was barred by res judicata and was also barred by laches. However, litigation of appellee counties' 1998 resolutions was not barred, as appellants could not have raised them in their previous complaint, even though the narrow issue was previously litigated.


OUTCOME: The trial court was reversed, in part, as to its dismissal of appellants' constitutional challenge to appellee counties' resolutions adopted after previous litigation on the issue because those resolutions could not have been raised in appellants' prior complaint. Otherwise, the trial court was affirmed as to appellants' other claims, since those claims should have been previously raised.

Kubik v. New York State Dep't of Social Servs.


87424


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


278 A.D.2d 644; 719 N.Y.S.2d 130; 2000 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13027



December 14, 2000, Decided  
December 14, 2000, Entered



DISPOSITION: The order is modified, on the law, without costs, by reversing so much thereof as partially denied the cross motion for summary judgment with respect to the ninth and tenth causes of action; cross motion granted to that extent and said causes of action are dismissed; and, as so modified, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants appealed part of order of Supreme Court in Columbia County (New York) partially denying their cross motion for summary judgment, and thus failing to dismiss 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 claims and certain intentional tort claims against them under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 215(3). Plaintiff considered all those claims to be made under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, which made them subject to the statute of limitations in N.Y. C.P.L.R. 214(5).


OVERVIEW: The disputed causes of action were predicated upon allegations that defendants engaged in a conspiracy by filing a false report concerning one of the plaintiffs, which led to her arrest and prosecution in violation of her constitutional rights. The claims were claims for conspiracy to violate civil rights under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983. All intentional tort claims were dismissed by the trial court. A claim for conspiracy to violate civil rights required a detailed fact pleading. A complaint containing only general allegations of a conspiracy to deprive a person of constitutional rights could not withstand a dismissal motion. Plaintiffs failed to substantiate their causes of action with detailed factual information concerning the alleged conspiracy, thus summary judgment dismissing the claims should have been granted. The evidence raised a question of fact as to whether the police acted with probable cause in arresting one of the plaintiffs and whether they were entitled to qualified immunity. Thus, summary judgment dismissing plaintiffs' additional §1983 claims for deprivation of constitutional rights under color of law was precluded.


OUTCOME: Appellate court modified order by reversing the denial of defendants' cross-motion for summary judgment on conspiracy to violate civil rights claims, and affirmed portion of order that denied defendants' cross-motion for summary judgment as to deprivation of constitutional rights under color of law claims.

Addei v. State Bd. for Prof'l Med. Conduct


86263


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


278 A.D.2d 551; 717 N.Y.S.2d 388; 2000 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 12725



December 7, 2000, Decided  
December 7, 2000, Entered



DISPOSITION: The determination is modified, on the law, without costs, by annulling so much thereof as revoked petitioner's license to practice medicine; matter remitted to respondent for reconsideration of the penalty in accordance with this Court's decision; and, as so modified, confirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed the decision of the respondent State Board for Professional Medical Conduct (New York) to revoke his license to practice medicine.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was charged with raping a patient, sexually abusing and verbally harassing co-workers, and giving false information on applications for employment. After a hearing, respondent did not sustain the charge of rape of a patient or sexual harassment of one employee, but sustained the other charges, although it found that the false information charge did not warrant a finding of moral unfitness. Petitioner's license to practice medicine was revoked and he appealed. There was a rational basis for respondent's decision that misconduct regarding a co-worker occurred in the practice of medicine, since it happened during working hours. Sexual misconduct with a co-worker constituted moral unfitness to practice medicine within the meaning of N.Y. Educ. Law § 2530(20). Section 2530(20) gave fair notice to a person of ordinary intellect of the nature of proscribed conduct, so it was not unconstitutionally vague. Respondent was under no obligation to accept petitioner's excuses for perpetrating fraud. Revocation of petitioner's license was so incommensurate with the offense as to shock one's sense of fairness.


OUTCOME: Respondent's finding petitioner engaged in professional misconduct in the practice of medicine was affirmed because petitioner engaged in sexual misconduct with a co-worker during working hours, and the statute was not unconstitutionally vague, but revocation of petitioner's license was disproportionate with his misconduct as it did not impact patient care or relate to his skill as a physician.

Brignoni v. Abrahamson


87273


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


278 A.D.2d 565; 718 N.Y.S.2d 416; 2000 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 12726



December 7, 2000, Decided  
December 7, 2000, Entered



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee challenged the judgment of the Albany County Supreme Court (New York) granting respondents employer and employees' union's motion to dismiss the petition alleging that respondent employer had failed to give him a permanent promotion and that the settlement between respondents had adversely affected petitioner's employment.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner filed an action against respondents alleging that he should have been given a permanent promotion and that respondents' settlement agreement regarding temporary promotions adversely affected his employment. The trial court granted respondents' motion to dismiss the petition. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that petitioner's failure to join a necessary party to his action, the Public Employment Relations Board, which had originally dismissed petitioner's charges against respondents, provided ample basis for dismissal of his petition. The petition was also properly dismissed as time barred because the dismissal of petitioner's grievance against respondents occurred more than four months prior to the filing of the petition.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed because petitioner failed join a necessary party to his action against respondents and he failed to file his petition within four months of the dismissal of his grievance against respondents.

 

722 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Zorn v. Howe


85602


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


276 A.D.2d 51; 716 N.Y.S.2d 128; 2000 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 12207



November 22, 2000, Decided  
November 22, 2000, Entered



DISPOSITION: The order is affirmed, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent tenant appealed Tompkins County Court (New York) affirmance of respondent's eviction by petitioner landlord, arguing that Ithaca, New York, Municipal Code ch. 177, §§ 2, 3, authorizing eviction for illegal drug possession, was preempted by the N.Y. Real Prop. and Real Prop. Acts. Laws and was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Respondent was evicted from his apartment by petitioner landlord pursuant to Ithaca, New York, Municipal Code ch. 177 §§ 2, 3, which provided for summary eviction of tenants who had possessed or used illegal drugs on the premises. Respondent argued that New York state legislation had preempted the area. N.Y. Real Prop. Law §231(1) provided generally for evictions for illegal use, and other statutes made specific references to bawdy houses and other illegal uses. The court held that if anything, the challenged ordinance merely supplemented a statutory scheme that was not comprehensive, and certainly was not inconsistent with it. Therefore, there was no preemption. Respondent's equal protection and privacy right challenges were also unavailing. The ordinance aimed to protect the neighborhood, not to invidiously discriminate between landlords and tenants, and respondent had no right to violate drug laws in the privacy of his apartment.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order. The questioned ordinance supplemented but was not at all inconsistent with the state's statute, so there was no preemption. There was no invidious classification between landlords and tenants since purpose was to protect neighborhood, and respondent had no right of privacy to violate drug laws.


HEADNOTES

Local Laws - Preemption by State - Ordinance Authorizing Eviction Based on Illegal Drug Use and Possession

1. Respondent tenant may lawfully be evicted from his apartment in a summary proceeding based upon his admitted illegal drug use and possession pursuant to a municipal ordinance which authorizes the maintenance of a "special proceeding to evict a tenant from leased premises ... upon the ground that the premises, or any part thereof, have been used or occupied for the purpose of using or possessing illegal drugs." The ordinance is not invalid as being preempted by State law. The fact that illegal drug use and possession are not among the grounds for eviction for illegal use of premises specifically prescribed by Real Property Law § 231 (1) and RPAPL 715 (1) does not demonstrate an impermissible conflict between the State statutory scheme and the local law, or that the State intended to occupy the entire field to the exclusion of local law. Rather, the ordinance is consistent with the State statutory scheme of grounds for eviction based on illegal activity. The ordinance merely supplements the State statutory scheme by adding additional grounds for eviction. The ordinance does not prohibit conduct that the State statutory scheme allows and does not impose additional restrictions on rights granted by the State.

Constitutional Law - Validity of Statute - Local Ordinance Authorizing Eviction Based on Illegal Drug Use and Possession

2. A municipal ordinance which authorizes the maintenance of a "special proceeding to evict a tenant from leased premises ... upon the ground that the premises, or any part thereof, have been used or occupied for the purpose of using or possessing illegal drugs" does not create an unconstitutionally impermissible distinction between tenants and property owners. As with the provisions of RPAPL 715 (1) dealing with the use of demised premises for illegal purposes, the clear purpose and effect of the ordinance is to protect the health, safety and welfare of the surrounding community. Furthermore, the ordinance does not violate a tenant's right to privacy. While people have a privacy interest in their homes, they have no corresponding right to violate the law in the privacy of their homes. A tenant has no legitimate privacy interest in the possession or use of illegal drugs in his or her apartment.

 

723 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


People v. Rosenblatt


2253, 2253A, 2254


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


277 A.D.2d 61; 717 N.Y.S.2d 9; 2000 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 11970



November 14, 2000, Decided  
November 14, 2000, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state appealed the order of the Supreme Court, New York County (New York) which granted defendants' motions to set aside a jury verdict convicting them of two counts of failure to collect sales tax and four counts of willfully failing to file a tax return. Defendants appealed the judgment which convicted them of 12 counts of selling tickets in violation of the maximum premium price and one count of aggravated ticket speculation.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff state appealed the order of the county court which granted defendants' motions to set aside a jury verdict convicting them of two counts of failure to collect sales tax and four counts of willfully failing to file a tax return, and dismissed those counts, and judgments. Defendants appealed the judgment of the same court which convicted them of 12 counts of selling tickets in violation of the maximum premium price and one count of aggravated ticket speculation. The court affirmed the decisions. The court properly granted the motions to set aside the verdict because the tax laws did not currently require a sales tax to be paid on receipts derived from the resale of tickets to sports and entertainment events. The denial of the motions with respect to the other convictions was proper because the maximum ticket price restrictions contained in N.Y. Arts. & Cult. Aff. Law art. 25 were not unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: Judgment was affirmed because tax laws did not currently require a sales tax to be paid on receipts derived from the resale of tickets to sports and entertainment events and denial of the motions to set aside the verdict with respect to the other convictions was proper because the maximum ticket price restrictions were not unconstitutional.

 

724 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Welch Foods, Inc. v. Wilson


(1228), CA 99-01589


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FOURTH DEPARTMENT


277 A.D.2d 882; 716 N.Y.S.2d 243; 2000 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 11389



November 13, 2000, Decided  
November 13, 2000, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed from the order of the Supreme Court of Chautauqua County (New York), which granted defendant' motion to dismiss and denied plaintiff's cross motion for summary judgment, as to plaintiff's complaint alleging, inter alia, breach of contract.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff and defendant entered into a sewer agreement pursuant to which defendant agreed to accept wastewater from plaintiff. Defendant was to charge plaintiff based on its assigned capacity until such time as plaintiff installed certain equipment. After plaintiff installed the equipment, defendant continued to charge plaintiff based on its assigned capacity rather than its measured discharges. Plaintiff brought suit alleging, inter alia, breach of contract. Summary judgment was entered in favor of defendant and plaintiff appealed. The court found that the trial court erred in dismissing the breach of contract claim, as the sewer agreement did not unambiguously allow defendant to change any term of the agreement unilaterally. The court erred in dismissing the Contract Clause, U.S. Const., art. I, § 10, cl. 1, claim with respect to the sewer agreement, as there was a triable issue of fact whether defendant, in enacting a subsequent sewer ordinance, impaired its contract with plaintiff. The sewer ordinance was not unconstitutional, as the sewer rents bore a rational relationship to compensating for plaintiff's lost revenue due to the underutilization of the plant.


OUTCOME: The dismissal of plaintiff's claims of breach of contract and violation the contract clause of the United States Constitution were reversed, as there were material issues of fact as to the terms of the contract and whether a subsequent ordinance interfered with defendant's contract with plaintiff. The dismissal of all other claims was affirmed.

People v. Gatti


(1727), KA 99-05116


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FOURTH DEPARTMENT


277 A.D.2d 1041; 716 N.Y.S.2d 182; 2000 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 11612



November 13, 2000, Decided  
November 13, 2000, Filed


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the Supreme Court, Monroe County (New York), which denied appellant's motion to dismiss the indictment against him, and convicted appellant for attempted murder in the first-degree.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was convicted of attempted murder in the first-degree. Appellant made a motion to dismiss at the close of proof to dismiss the indictment, alleging, inter alia, that appellant was not 18 years old at the time of the crime, that the plea bargain provision of the death penalty statute were unconstitutional, and that proof of appellant's intent to kill was legally insufficient. The court affirmed the conviction. Appellant had reached his 18th birthday and was thus more than 18 years-old at the time of the commission of the crime. The death penalty plea bargain statute was not unconstitutional because appellant was not exposed to the risk of a death sentence as the result of exercising his right to a jury trial. The proof of appellant's intent was legally sufficient. The proof established that appellant attempted to forcibly steal money from the restaurant by displaying what appeared to be a pistol or revolver to a person appellant mistakenly believed to be a restaurant employee.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed. Appellant's arguments were without merit. Appellant had reached his 18th birthday and was more than 18 years old at the time of the commission of the crime. The proof of appellant's intent was legally sufficient because appellant attempted to forcibly steal money from the restaurant by displaying what appeared to be a pistol or revolver to a person appellant mistakenly believed to be a restaurant employee.

 

726 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


City of New York v. Consolidated Edison Co. of N.Y., Inc.


1615


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


274 A.D.2d 189; 713 N.Y.S.2d 40; 2000 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 9161



September 14, 2000, Decided  
September 14, 2000, Entered



DISPOSITION: Order entered March 24, 2000 reversed, on the law, without costs; cross-motion denied; complaint reinstated; City's motion for summary judgment granted; Con Edison directed to comply with the two pending Order Out Notices and to pay the cost of interference work at the three sites at issue; and matter remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant city sought review of a decision from the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), granting summary judgment to appellee utility and denying summary judgment to appellant and dismissing its complaint. Appellant contended that New York City, N.Y., Admin. Code § 24-521(b) was applicable to appellee and the protection or relocation of its utility installations were affected by a public construction project.


OVERVIEW: Appellant city brought an action to compel appellee utility to either protect or relocate its facilities located within easements that were within the area of a public infrastructure project, citing New York City, N.Y., Admin. Code § 24-521(b) as authority for its position. The trial court granted summary judgment for appellee and dismissed the complaint of appellant. The court reversed and entered summary judgment for appellant, finding appellant's ordinance was applicable whether appellee's facilities were installed pursuant to a franchise from appellant or to installations existing by easement. The court determined that the ordinance did not make any distinction between the two rights and, had such a distinction been intended, the ordinance would have so specified. The court concluded that appellant need not compensate appellee for the effects of reasonable regulations designed to protect the public health and safety and that the results of the legislation would not be a permanent occupancy of appellee's easement, but merely a temporary interference for the public good.


OUTCOME: The order granting summary judgment to appellee utility and denying summary judgment to appellant city and dismissing its complaint was reversed, and the complaint of appellant was reinstated and its motion for summary judgment was granted. The court found that appellee's interest in the easements on which its facilities were located was subject to reasonable regulation necessitated by the public safety.


HEADNOTES

Public Utilities - Excavation of Street - Utility's Responsibility for "Interference Costs" to Facilities Installed Pursuant to Both Easements and Franchises

1. Defendant public utility must comply with plaintiff's "Order Out Notices" directing it to protect or relocate utility installations, at its own expense, at the sites of three City construction projects located in areas where defendant holds permanent easements for its electric distribution facilities. Administrative Code of the City of New York § 24-521 (b), which requires public utilities to bear the costs of protecting utility installations affected by public construction projects, supersedes the common-law rule that the City must bear such "interference costs" when the utility installations are maintained pursuant to permanent easements purchased by the utility company from a private landowner, rather than pursuant to a franchise from the City. The ordinance is not merely a codification of the common-law rule that would limit the utility's responsibility for "interference costs" to facilities installed pursuant to franchises. The ordinance does not distinguish between facilities installed pursuant to City franchises and those installed pursuant to easements. Moreover, the plain language of the ordinance does not contain any exception for utility installations that occupy land by virtue of an easement.

Public Utilities - Excavation of Street - Utility's Responsibility for "Interference Costs" to Facilities Installed Pursuant to Both Easements and Franchises - No Unconstitutional Regulatory Taking

2. Administrative Code of the City of New York § 24-521 (b), which requires public utilities to bear the costs of protecting utility installations affected by public construction projects, whether the utility installations are maintained pursuant to permanent easements purchased by the utility company from a private landowner or by City franchises, does not work an unconstitutional taking. Not every regulatory intrusion on property rights amounts to a taking. While a public utility may have a property right in the land where its installations are situated, its use of that land is subject to reasonable regulation when necessitated by public safety. By imposing the responsibility for "inference costs" on the utilities, which are best equipped to find cost-effective and safe ways to shield their installations, the ordinance protects the public's interest in uninterrupted utility service and efficient completion of essential public works projects. Moreover, since there is no permanent occupation of land, there is no per se taking. Furthermore, defendant utility has not produced sufficient evidence regarding the adverse economic impact of the ordinance to establish a prima facie regulatory taking claim.

Public Utilities - Excavation of Street

3. Defendant public utility's claims that the City of New York's chosen contractors charge excessive prices for utility interference work and that certain interference work demanded by the City is not necessary, may be addressed in further proceedings after defendant has complied with the City's "Order Out Notices" directing it to protect or relocate its utility installations, at its own expense, at the sites of three City construction projects.

 

727 of 1817 DOCUMENTS


Aliessa v. Novello


2989


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


274 A.D.2d 347; 712 N.Y.S.2d 96; 2000 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 8235



July 27, 2000, Decided  
July 27, 2000, Entered


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), which granted plaintiff state medical assistance applicants' motion for summary judgment that declared that N.Y. Soc. Serv. Law § 122 violated N.Y. Const. art. XVII, § 1 insofar as it denied medical assistance to legal immigrants residing in New York under color of the law and granted injunctive relief against defendant New York medical assistance provider.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff state medical assistance applicants were granted a motion for summary judgment declaring that N.Y. Soc. Serv. Law § 122 violated N.Y. Const. art. XVII, § 1 insofar as it denied medical assistance to legal immigrants including persons residing in New York under color of the law and granted injunctive relief against defendant New York medical assistance provider. The court reversed determining that § 122 did not violate the state constitution or the Equal Protection clause. Since the state law was enacted in furtherance of constitutionally valid federal immigration policies, it did not improperly discriminate on the basis of alien status. The rationality standard was applied for equal protection review. Here, § 122 limited only one form of assistance, non-emergency Medicaid, for a limited five-year period, to certain aliens who did not meet federally defined qualification criteria. Not all assistance was denied; only the "manner and level" of medical assistance was restricted. Neither did § 122 violate N.Y. Const. art. XVII, § 3, as § 122 gave the state the same broad discretion as in art. XVII, § 1 to determine the manner and means to promote public health.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed; state law did not violate the state constitution or the Equal Protection clause. Since the state law was enacted in furtherance of constitutionally valid federal immigration policies, it did not improperly discriminate on the basis of alien status. The trial court properly applied the rationality standard of equal protection review.

Boynton Suites L.L.C. v. Board of Assessment Review


86605


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


274 A.D.2d 926; 711 N.Y.S.2d 266; 2000 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 8279



July 27, 2000, Decided  
July 27, 2000, Entered



DISPOSITION: The judgment is affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the Supreme Court of Clinton County (New York), dismissing his application for review of a determination of respondent, city board of assessment review, that denied his request for a property tax exemption pursuant to N.Y. Real Prop. Tax Law §485-e.


OVERVIEW: A municipality adopted a resolution and enacted a local law opting into a real property tax exemption authorized by N.Y. Real Prop. Tax Law §485-e. Appellant sought an exemption for his property but while his application was pending, the municipality passed resolutions and a local law rescinding the original resolution and repealing the local law retroactive to its date of passage, thereby withdrawing the tax exemption. Appellant commenced a proceeding under N.Y. Real Prop. Tax Law art. 7 against respondent, city board of assessment review, arguing that the municipality exceeded its authority by repealing the earlier resolutions and local law because the state statute did not enable it to opt out of the exemption once it had opted in, and that the retroactive repeal was unconstitutional. The trial court dismissed appellant's petition, and he challenged its ruling. The court affirmed, holding that the state statute did not preclude municipalities from withdrawing the exemption by appropriate action, and that the retroactive repeal was not unconstitutional because the two month period of retroactivity was relatively short and its application was not unduly harsh or oppressive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, holding that the lower court properly dismissed the petition. It held that the municipality was not precluded by the state statute from withdrawing the exemption once it had adopted it, and that the retroactive repeal was not unconstitutional because the period of retroactivity was of short duration and its application was not unduly harsh or oppressive in its effect.
